Report on the results of parallel checks on the management of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introduction Word
The material presented reports on the progress and results of parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší kontrolní úradom Slovenskej republiky, which focused on the field of value added tax administration and the use of the VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so that the revenue from value added tax affects not only the national budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were aimed, in particular, at checking the tax authorities' process for examining the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of VIES made it possible to exchange information electronically on the registration of value added tax payers in the various Member States of the European Union and on commercial transactions carried out by those payers.
The discrepancy between the VIES data and the data in the taxpayer's VAT return should alert the tax authorities to suspicious cases and allow tax evasion or fraud to be detected.
The benefits of the parallel checks carried out were not only in the exchange of information on the procedure followed by the financial and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular in the examination of the use of the VIES system in checking the application of the right to value added tax exemption in intra-Community transactions.
The knowledge gained from the implementation of parallel controls is beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used to carry out further parallel controls in cooperation with the control institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel controls on the administration of value added tax for the period 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of the tax authorities' procedures for the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and the performance of VIES tasks for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO, the Czech Republic) and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as the SAO of the Slovak Republic) concluded a contract on cooperation in auditing activities on 12 September 2005.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implementation of parallel auditing actions “Value Added Tax Administration”, included in the SAO, Czech Republic's 2005 audit work plan under No 05/19, and “Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and recovery of taxes on prized value and fulfilment of roles under the VIES system on the deletion of informácii medzi by the members of ECA”, included in the SAO's audit work plan under No 22/2005.
The control actions carried out in parallel were in the nature of coordinated control.
The result of the joint coordinated inspection has been processed within the meaning of the European Enforcement Regulation No 31 on INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract and producing a joint final report on the outcome of the parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated inspection was to verify selected cases of supply and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between taxpayers of value added tax from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the ‘SR’).
Both parties contractually undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the VIES electronic system (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on requests received and sent to examine commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the control was carried out by the state budget department and territorial departments of central Bohemia, northwestern Bohemia, southern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the Ministry of Finance and 12 Financial Offices: the Tax Office in Mlada Boleslav, the Tax Office in Kolín, the Tax Office in Teplice, the Financial Office in Karlovy Vary, the Financial Office in Tábor, the Financial Office in Brno III, the Tax Office in Znojma, the Financial Office in Zlín, the Financial Office in Šumperk, the Financial Office in Ostrava I, the Financial Office for Prague 7 and the Financial Office for Prague 9.
The audit was carried out in the territory of SR by the Finance and Tax Division of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the SAO Expozituras of Banská Bystrica and Košice on 9 selected tax offices: Bratislava I, Komárno Tax Office, Trenčín Tax Office, Prievidza Daňový úrad, Zvolen Daňový úrad, Dolný Kubín Daňový úrad, Košice II Daňový úrad, Košice V and Michalovce Daňový úrad.
Objective of inspections:
The aim of the parallel control actions was to examine the procedure of the financial and/or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (VAT) following the incorporation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (EU) and to examine the use of the VIES electronic information system, in particular when checking the application of the right to VAT exemption.
The audited period of the coordinated inspection was the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions An electronic VIES system is in place in EU Member States, allowing tax authorities to check whether a supplier has been authorised to exempt a taxable transaction from VAT and, in the country of destination, to check whether the purchaser has properly declared and taxed the goods acquired.
VIES is not centralised within the EU, each Member State develops its own system.
The audit found differences in the national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the following areas:
The recapitulative statements indicate the values of supplies of goods to other EU Member States, the values of services provided are not included in recapitulative statements.
Data from summary reports filed by Czech payers are processed at the level of tax authorities in the Czech Republic, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States included in VAT returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to the other EU Member States.
In SR, data from recapitulative statements filed by Slovak taxpayers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of SR (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which makes it possible to compare the values reported in the recapitulative statements with the values of supplies of goods according to VAT tax returns and to identify any differences between them.
In SR, the values of goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported cumulatively on a common line of VAT return.
As a result, in SR, the system does not make it possible to automatically identify differences between the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of goods delivery values in VAT returns allows the results of data reconciliation to be used in controlling VAT exemption of supplies of goods to the EU.
The data received from the recapitulative statements filed by payers in other EU Member States are processed into CLOs and compared with the value of acquisitions of goods declared by payers from the Czech Republic and SR respectively in VAT returns.
In the SR, these data are sent to the tax authorities, and the tax authorities decide for themselves which cases of difference to examine.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of delivery and acquisition of goods must be checked by the tax authorities, and gives a list of these cases to the tax authorities responsible locally.
This ensures that, for the most significant derogations, it will be verified that VAT was correctly declared when the goods were acquired.
Furthermore, the audit highlighted some problems in the VAT management system due to the different reporting of intra-Community transactions (i.e. supplies and acquisitions of goods made by payers from different EU Member States):
Summary reports are filed in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum period for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the respective quarter.
Reducing the reporting period of recapitulative statements to one month, together with reducing the processing time, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
Tax authorities would thus be able to check more effectively whether VAT was declared at the correct amount when intra-Community acquisitions were made.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax year (month) would allow quicker verification of whether the payer has declared in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return the same value of the supplies of goods to the EU.
Differences between EU-payer declared goods delivery values and those reported by CR and SR payers were due, among other things, to different reporting of intra-Community supplies and acquisitions data across EU Member States.
These were, for example, the presentation in recapitulative statements of advance payments received, or the presentation in a supplier's recapitulative statement of intra-Community supplies in a quarter other than intra-Community acquisitions in the acquirer's VAT return.
The harmonisation of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to streamlining of the control activities of national tax administrations.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was also aimed at examining selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two states.
A total of 40 cases of commercial transactions between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined together, where there were doubts about their implementation or suspicions of VAT evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic have found out the following:
tax entities have declared in their VAT returns for the purpose of unduly obtaining an excess VAT deduction the execution of intra-Community transactions which have not actually been carried out;
Tax Entities reported intra-Community deliveries in carousel transactions, in which there were deliberate multiple decreases in the value of the deliveries in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers declared in their VAT returns and recapitulative statements intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the goods acquired;
the suppliers made an intra-Community supply of VAT-exempt goods to tax entities which were not registered for VAT in another Member State.
In those cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
suppliers declared intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than the intra-Community acquisitions declared by the acquirers, in some cases with an incorrect amount of VAT declared.
The lessons learned from the audit action showed that VIES provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
In particular, tax administrations should pay close attention to rigorously examining the differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the VIES data and using any information in tax proceedings.
Value Added Tax Issues After the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic Join the EU
Value Added Tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic became members of the EU.
Internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within EU territory have been abolished since EU accession.
Until 30.4.2004, the VAT administrator was the competent financial and tax office, with the exception of the importation of goods and occasional bus services within the country, where the tax authority was the customs office.
In the context of the adoption of the new Act No 235/2004 Coll. on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Act No 235/2004 Coll.") and Act No 222/2004 Col. on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Act No 222/2004 Coll."), the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU Member States has shifted from customs offices to financial and tax offices respectively.
The supply of goods in the Czech Republic, according to the provisions of Section 13 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
The delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the delivery of goods that have actually been dispatched or transported to another EU Member State.
Pursuant to Article 64 of Law 235/2004 Coll., a taxable transaction is exempt with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are supplied to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
A supply of goods in SR under the provisions of Article 8 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z. is a supply of tangible property in which the right to property is altered.
The transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the territory of the country to another Member State shall also be regarded as a supply of goods if those goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Pursuant to Article 43 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z., the supply of goods from the national territory to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the purchaser is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
Acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic pursuant to Section 16 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. is the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods that are dispatched or transported to the customer by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer purchases goods at a VAT-free price and is obliged to declare VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 25 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., if he fulfils the conditions of Section 73 of this Act, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
Acquisition of goods domestically from another EU Member State in SR, pursuant to Article 11 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z., means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property dispatched or transported to the person acquiring it by or on behalf of the supplier or the person acquiring it within the country from another Member State.
The SR tax becomes chargeable to the payer when the goods are acquired within the country from another Member State in accordance with the provisions of Article 20 of Act No 222/2004 Z.z.
Under Paragraph 49 of Act No 222/2004, the taxpayer may deduct VAT if the tax is charged by him on the acquisition within the country of goods from another Member State in accordance with Paragraphs 11 and 11a of that Act.
Three-digit trade is, according to the provisions of Section 17 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. and/or Section 45 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z., a trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States where the object of the trade is the supply of the same goods between the three persons.
Intra-unitary transactions are supplies and acquisitions of goods made between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions made between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the table below.
VIES system
A VAT information exchange system has been set up within the EU to control the exercise of the right to VAT exemption on intra-Community supplies of goods.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows EU Member State tax authorities to check whether the supplier has been entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and vice versa, whether the purchaser has properly declared and taxed the goods acquired.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State develops its own VIES system.
The national systems work on a common principle and are interconnected via a common EU communication network, the Common Communication Network (CCN; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was linked to the Automated Tax Information System (‘ADIS’), in the Slovak Republic with the Tax Information System Application Software (‘APV DIS’).
These systems are used by the financial and tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the management of taxes and charges.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU country receives information on tax entities that it would not be able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
Under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State establishes a central department within the internal organisational structure in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the management of VAT, the Central Liaison Office (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance – Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the International Cooperation in VAT Administration Unit (hereinafter referred to as the MF CLO) has been established, performs the tasks arising from international cooperation.
The function of the CLO in the SR is fulfilled by the Tax Directorate of the SR, the Department of International Administrative Cooperation (DR CLO).
These departments communicate with EU foreign administrations in particular in the area of exchange of information under VIES, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, verification of tax identification numbers (TIN) of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to examine a particular intra-Community transaction or to obtain further information relating to a particular tax entity, the financial and tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via MF CLO or DR CLO respectively.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use to correctly determine VAT.
Requests for information are sent mostly in electronic form between the CLOs of EU Member States, using the standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was mainly aimed at examining selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two states, as well as the level of use of information obtained through international cooperation by the financial and tax authorities.
The SAO, Czech Republic, requested the SAO SR to verify in 30 cases the business transactions carried out between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The SAO requested the SAO of the Czech Republic to verify in 10 cases the business transactions carried out between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
Examination of intra-Community transactions revealed, inter alia:
o
The SAO, Czech Republic asked the SAO SR to verify the procedure of the tax administration, which was sent a reply to the request for information.
The Slovak Tax Office requested through the SCAC form a verification of the delivery of goods (footwear) in Q3 2004 from a Slovak payer worth 2 847 thousand Sk.
The Tax Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer had declared the acquisition of the goods at this value only in a supplementary VAT return and had returned the same goods to Slovak tax entities worth CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004.
Based on the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the tax office of the Slovak supplier has fully recognised the right to an excess VAT deduction arising, inter alia, from this supply.
This tax office did not provide information about the suspected re-export to the tax authorities locally responsible buyers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
This will provide an impetus for further examination of trading activities in relation to possible carousel fraud.
o
The Czech tax administrator requested through the SCAC form a verification of the delivery of a technology line to SR worth 4,850,000 CZK in the 2nd quarter of 2004.
The tax procedure carried out in SR showed that only part of the technology line was delivered, components worth CZK 3,395,000 were not delivered.
In examining this case, the SAO SR found that the VAT on the taxable transaction carried out was declared by the Slovak taxpayer on the amount of CZK 4 850,000 in the VAT return (DAP) for tax year 7/2004.
The SAO, Czech Republic also found that the Czech payer had reported in his DAP an excess VAT deduction of CZK 655,000 for that quarter, which was generated by the application of a VAT deduction on the purchase of this technology line from another domestic payer.
Based on the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak Tax Entities had formed a business relationship for the purpose of illegally obtaining an excess VAT deduction, disputed the realisation of the taxable transaction and failed to recognise part of the Czech taxpayer's right to deduct the amount of CZK 647,000.
o
The Slovak tax administration requested in 2004, via the SCAC form, a verification of the supply of goods (copying machines) to the Czech payer worth 24 246K Sk made in December 2002.
These goods were purchased by a Slovak payer in November 2002 in SR from another tax entity for a value of 29 667 thousand Sk and subsequently sold to a Czech payer.
The Slovak taxpayer claimed an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
A tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administration and did not file DAPs for the 4th quarter of 2002 or the following period.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak tax administration, based on the outcome of the tax inspection, did not recognise the right to an excess deduction of EUR 5 541 000. Sk applied in the DAP for the month of 11/2002 and set the tax liability at 1 750 thousand Sk.
At the same time, that taxpayer was not granted a VAT exemption in respect of exports of goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from MF CLO to verify the value of the purchased goods for Q3 2004.
According to the VIES data, the Czech payer was to purchase from SR goods (diluent) worth 3,767 thou.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administration, did not file a DAP and was assessed ex officio VAT for months 7 to 12/2004 at the rate of 0 CZK.
The Czech tax administrator asked through the SCAC form to verify whether the delivery of goods from SR to the Czech Republic took place, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In reply, Slovakia's locally competent tax office sent a copy of the invoice, the bill of lading and a demand for payment of the invoice.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with a right to deduct VAT on that supply.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech tax administration had assessed the response to the request for information received from SR as evidence showing that the company had acquired goods from another EU Member State.
Upon further investigation, the Tax Office in the Czech Republic will request a superior authority to review the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (particle products) to, among others, an American company that deposited these goods in the Czech Republic in a free zone.
The operator of this free zone was listed on invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased $57,600 worth of particle board from a Slovak payer (at a unit price of $100/piece), which it placed in a free zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company, for a value of USD 14 400 (unit price USD 25/piece) and the goods were exported back to SR.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the free zone area on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administration has initiated tax inspections of individual tax years 2004 and 2005 with the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
The verification of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech locally competent tax authorities via several SCAC forms.
Individual responses gradually built up a picture of the shops and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the carousel shops.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO of the Slovak Republic, found that in these trade relations there was a deliberate gradual decrease in the value of the goods.
On the basis of the information gathered, the SR Tax Directorate concluded that in this case of carousel trade there is free pricing (i.e. the importation of undervalued goods and its overestimation by domestic companies in the importer-exporter chain) which is not an infringement of the VAT Act in the SR.
Under current legislation, the payment of excess VAT to export companies cannot be avoided as they fulfil all the conditions of the Act to exempt supplies from VAT.
o
The Czech taxpayer had his VAT registration revoked on 12 July 2005.
On 27 October 2005, following a voluntary application for VAT registration, that body became taxable again.
The Czech taxpayer entered into the DAP for the month of 8/2005 (i.e. the period when he was not subject to VAT) the value of the acquisition of goods (a printing press) from SR amounting to CZK 1,174,000 and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to a supply of goods from a Slovak payer amounting to 1 530 thousand Sk, which the Slovak payer listed in the DAP as a supply of goods to another EU Member State with a right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator asked to verify the said delivery using the SCAC form because the Slovak supplier had not shown how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administration and did not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the locally competent tax authority to examine the data.
o
The Slovak payer reported in the recapitulative statement for Q3 2004 supplies of goods worth 956K. Sk tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The Czech entity's VAT number was marked as erroneous by VIES.
A check in the payers' database revealed that such a TIN was never allocated in the Czech Republic.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electro-fitting works on real estate in the Czech Republic, not the delivery of goods from SR to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT as the Czech entity told the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax administration requested to verify the facts by using the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, by enquiry with the local tax administration in the Czech Republic, found that the tax entity named on the invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not declare the tax on the services received from the Slovak entity and did not declare the tax on the acquisition of goods.
There was no local investigation or tax check with the Czech entity, its current whereabouts are unknown.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax authorities learned that the Czech taxpayer had become a taxpayer of VAT by law by accepting the service.
The Slovak tax entity will be subject to a tax audit for the first to fourth quarters of 2004.
o
The Slovak payer reported in the recapitulative statement for Q3 2004 the delivery of goods worth CZK 1,055,000. Sk to the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electro-fitting works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
This was not a supply of goods from SR to the Czech Republic, but a supply of services.
The Slovak tax administration requested to verify the facts by using the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, enquired at the local tax administration in the Czech Republic, found that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the supply and that a local investigation was carried out on it to verify the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
On the basis of this local investigation, it was found that the present case was not really an acquisition of goods but an acquisition of services, which was also reported by the Czech entity in a proper DAP.
Furthermore, the tax office found that the Czech operator had not paid VAT at the correct amount for the tax period of Q3 2004 as a result of a bad procedure in the calculation of VAT.
The tax entity shall submit an additional DAP.
The SAO SR enquired at the local competent tax office and found that the Slovak payer had misstated the provision of the service in the recapitulative statement and would be subject to a tax audit for the 1st to 4th quarters of 2004.
o
The Czech tax entity has voluntarily registered as a VAT payer since 10 March 2004.
For Q1 2004, DAP reported high turnover on both inputs and outputs.
The locally competent tax administration initiated the tax procedure, the subject did not cooperate with the tax administration, so he was assessed VAT of 0 CZK due to suspicion of involvement in the carousel business.
Another DAP was not filed by that payer.
He had his VAT registration cancelled on 4.1.2005 because of a failure to comply with the law.
According to the VIES data, this entity was to acquire from the Slovak payer in the 3rd and 4th quarters of 2004 goods worth 7,846K Sk.
In order to verify the execution of these transactions, the Czech tax authorities sent two requests for information to SR.
The SAO SR enquired at the local tax office and found that the manager of the Czech company had denied the transactions examined in testimony and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
As a result of the SR tax procedure, intra-Community deliveries to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer were challenged.
The payer will not be recognised as entitled to VAT exemption and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
o
According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods (work clothes) from SR in the 1st quarter of 2005 for a total value of 39 970 thou Sk.
In this quarter, the Czech payer reported acquisitions of goods from another EU Member State only in DAP for the month 3/2005, amounting to CZK 11,292,000.
The locally competent tax administration carried out a local investigation on the subject to verify the data in this DAP.
As the company did not produce any documents or otherwise prove that the taxable transactions had been carried out, the tax authorities charged VAT of CZK 0 on 9 June 2005.
Due to doubts about the realisation of the acquisition of the goods, the tax authorities sent two requests for information to SR in May 2005.
According to the reply to the requests for information, the SR tax authorities had doubts about the realisation of business cases as well as the realisation of the payment.
The SAO was informed that the Slovak tax administration had sent the DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out at the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated inspection, the local tax administration was carrying out further enquiries concerning the Czech entity in the Czech Republic, while an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was ongoing.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (working clothes) were made between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
Slovak payer No 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No 3, who supplied them back to SR to payer No 4 (see Diagram No 2).
A)
Czech payer No 2 was to purchase goods (work clothes) worth 4,847,000 CZK from Slovak payer No 1 in Q4 2004 and goods worth 17,050,000 CZK in Q1 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the VIES data, the locally competent tax authority sent a request for information to SR on 25.5.2005.
In reply, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the realisation of the business cases as well as the realisation of the payment.
On 8.6.2005, a request for information was received at MF CLO from SR, concerning goods worth 16 575 thou Sk to be delivered by Slovak payer No 1 to Czech payer No 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak side demanded to check whether the Czech No 2 had actually accepted the goods, admitted them in the DAP and paid VAT.
An official record drawn up by the local tax authority in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech taxpayer No 2 has not resided at an address registered in the Commercial Register for a long time.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax year, he filed a DAP for the quarterly tax year.
In view of this, the Czech tax authorities could not assess VAT.
Implementation of the taxable transaction between Slovak payer No 1 and Czech payer No 2 mentioned in the application in the amount of EUR 16 575,000. Sk could not be verified due to the above.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel business for the purpose of drawing an excess VAT deduction.
(B)
Czech payer No 3, who deals with the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed a DAP for the tax period of months 1 and 2/2005, in which he declared the supply of goods (work clothes) to Slovak payer No 4 for a total value of CZK 21,935,000.
These work clothes were to be purchased by Czech payer No 3 from Czech payer No 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to SR, mainly to verify that Slovak payer No 4 had purchased goods worth CZK 1,025,000 from Czech payer No 3 in December 2004 and CZK 21,935,000 in Q1 2005.
The response to this request for information received from SR showed that in the DAP for the month 12/2004 the Slovak payer No 4 stated the zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for months 1 and 2/2005 the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State was only 1 193 thousand Sk.
No 4 did not respond to the request for tax documents for the tax period of months 10/2004 to 3/2005.
A local investigation carried out in SR revealed that the company was not located at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer meets all the characteristics of a so-called "lost company" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO was informed that the Slovak tax administration had sent the DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out at the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax authorities collected documents that would confirm or deny the existence of the goods.
VAT will be calculated on the basis of the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also being handled by the Police of the Czech Republic.
Control Action Progress
In order to prepare for the parallel audits, a coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO of the Slovak Republic took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants in that meeting were acquainted with the VAT legislation in both states and the incorporation of the VIES electronic system into the national databases.
The negotiations resulted in the specification of the extent of cooperation and the setting of conditions for the selection of control samples.
The two sides agree that cooperation will focus on the following areas: (b) verifying data on intra-Community acquisitions reported in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as ‘SH’) of payers from the SR included in the VIES system, and vice versa; (c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic on the commercial transactions made.
Furthermore, it was agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection would be made following the volume of intra-Community deliveries between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intracomunitary transactions
The procedure for processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic for intra-Community supply and acquisition of goods is shown in the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intracomunitary Delivery
Where a VAT payer makes an intra-Community supply, he shall be required to submit to the SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
A payer in the Czech Republic presents in the SH summary information on his VAT-exempt supplies of goods to another EU Member State for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to enter into the SH the value of goods that have been exempt and delivered from the national territory to other EU Member States for the calendar quarter period.
The data on the value of the goods supplied are always given in the SH in Czech and Slovak currency, broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their TIN, under which they were registered in their country.
Service data are not included in the SH.
If a payer in the Czech Republic discovers that he has given erroneous data in the SH, he is obliged to give a subsequent SH.
If the payer in SR finds that the information given in the SH was incomplete or incorrect, he shall submit a corrective SH before the expiry of the deadline for the submission of the SH, after which time he shall submit an additional SH.
VIES allows the exchange of information on VAT registered payers' registration data in EU Member States.
Payees from the Czech Republic and SR respectively can verify that the respective purchaser's TIN is registered in a given EU Member State.
Data from submitted SHs are grouped by individual TIN of purchasers on the MF CLO and DR CLO respectively by VIES.
It will create the aggregate value of all deliveries for each VAT number of the acquirer and the code of the delivery method from all its Czech and Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files.
Data from files L1QDs shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-Community transactions between CR and SR (from L1QD files) is shown in the table below.
If VIES in another Member State detects a wrong customer ID in the L1QD files sent, it generates the so-called O_MCTL message, which contains all the wrong VAT number, indicating the type of error.
This report is then sent to the MF CLO or DR CLO respectively.
The O_MCTL message can contain 4 types of errors: formally erroneous TIN, TIN not registered in the state or never allocated, the purchaser with a TIN was not subject to VAT in the quarter, the purchaser's VAT registration was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, the MF CLO transmits data from received O_MCTL reports to the tax authorities.
If the wrong TIN of the EU payer is used in any of the SH or subsequent SH lines sent, a so-called "Notice of Doubt to VAT ID" is generated at the relevant IRS by the ADIS system.
The tax office will check that the delivery to a taxpayer registered for VAT in another EU Member State has actually taken place and will record the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, the DR CLO in VIES processes all O_MCTL messages and transmits them electronically to the locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of the taxpayers who have given the wrong TIN in their SHs.
The tax authorities then invite the payer to submit an additional SH and, when reporting invalid TIN in the SH file, the tax office checks the delivery of the goods with the relevant payer.
Data on the number of erroneous TIN relating to intra-Community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the table below.
Of the total number of 41 728 TIN Czech payers listed in the SH Slovak payers during the period from Q2 2004 to Q1 2005, 929 were erroneous TIN, or 2.23%.
Of the 62,997 TIN of Slovak payers listed in the SH of Czech payers during the same period, 416 were erroneous TIN, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intra-Community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer erroneous TIN's in their SH than SR payers.
An examination of the activities of the financial and tax authorities revealed that VIES did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of taxable persons in all cases.
For example:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the taxpayer's registration in Q4 2004 when questioned by the Tax Administrator in the Czech Republic, the O_MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer's registration this quarter.
The investigation found that the termination of the registration took place only on 1.1.2005;
- The SAO also found that 6 tax entities filed an SH in which the wrong TIN was reported, but the O_MCTL reports did not include this TIN.
In SR, the submitted SHs are converted into electronic form at the tax offices and the data from them is sent to the DR CLO.
Following the subsequent processing of this data in VIES, the DR CLO shall send to the relevant tax authorities the so-called SH error breakdowns submitted by the tax entities for the respective quarters.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH at 26.7.2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection) and at 2.2.2006 (i.e. data processed after the completion of the inspection).
The data reconciliation is presented in the table below.
The above data show that the SAO audit of SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with erroneous TIN (on average by 199 SH per quarter) but also on the reduction of the number of unrepaired errors in SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-Community deliveries reported by the payer in the relevant DAP rows is compared at the financial offices with the value of intra-Community deliveries reported by this payer in the quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates differences between these values.
The tax manager should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data obtained in determining the tax liability.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values in SH and DAP in these cases was 537,231,000 CZK.
Since Q3 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administration in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values given in the SH and the DAP of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-Community supplies according to the SH as a match and to set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-Community deliveries per quarter, 0.5% of the value is a not insignificant amount, therefore tax administrations in these cases should not set the SH and DAP compliance without explaining the causes of the differences.
For example, the tax administrator, without verification, set the match in case of a difference in values of CZK 1,561,000.
Examination of differences in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was complicated by the fact that SH was filed by payers for each calendar quarter within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
Tax authorities could not compare the intra-community delivery values in those DAPs with the SH values for payers with a monthly tax year at the time of DAP submission for the first two months of the calendar quarter.
In those cases, the tax authorities became aware of any data mismatch in the DAPs and SHs only when the tax liability or excess VAT deduction was assessed or refunded.
5.1.2 Intracomanial acquisition
VIES provides, inter alia, information on the values of intra-Community transactions made within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, data received from SH submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered by L1QD) are processed by MF CLO.
In the processing, the data are recalculated by the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the acquisition value reported by the Czech payers in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of acquisitions reported by payers in the DAP should be within the minimum and maximum converted values of L1QD (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is less than L1min, a so-called validation order is generated for payers with the most significant irregularities.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax entities and are transmitted to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders concerning audited financial authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the table below.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that in 33 cases audited financial authorities did not check for irregularities in the values of intra-Community acquisitions indicated by the verification orders received.
The total difference between the values reported in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases was at least CZK 148,319,000.
The SAO, Czech Republic selected for inspection 533 files of tax entities for which audited tax authorities received a verification order from MF CLO.
In the following cases, the most common causes of the differences between the values given in the purchaser's DAP and in the supplier's SH were found: on the purchaser's side (Czech payer), in 263 cases, the purchaser did not declare the purchase of goods in the correct DAP, in 93 cases the payer acknowledged the acquisition of goods in a different tax period than the one in which he was required to declare VAT, in 6 cases the purchaser reported the value of goods acquired in the wrong line of the DAP, on the supplier's side (EU payer's) in 88 cases the EU payer included the value of goods in their SHSR included the values of goods supplied to the Czech payer.
On the SR payers' side, the most frequent erroneous inclusion of the value of the services provided was in the SH.
54 such cases were identified at audited tax offices.
For example, when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 was created by the Slovak payer entering into the SH for the 1st quarter of 2005 the provision of services (construction work and delivery of goods including assembly in the territory of the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of the received advances in the SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers indicated in the SH received advances from Czech payers, resulting in a command to verify the difference of CZK 3,580,000.
Orders to verify acquired goods are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where data from the SH are subsequently changed in EU Member States, such as a change in the purchaser of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new validation orders are not generated.
Since the VIES system does not automatically notify these changes, the locally competent tax authority of the person acquiring the goods may, without any other initiative, be unaware of the facts relevant to the correct determination of the tax liability on the goods acquired, and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
An audit by the SAO, the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer reported in the SH for Q2 2004 the value of the supply of goods to the Czech payer at 1 504 thousand Sk.
On 1.2.2005, the tax office of the locally competent Czech payer sent a request for information to SR, as the Czech payer admitted acquiring goods only in the amount of CZK 425,000.
As a result of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer filed an additional BI on 1 March 2005, in which he corrected the details of the delivery of the goods to the Czech Republic, by reducing the value of the delivery for the Czech payer initially mentioned to 538K. Sk and by increasing the value of the goods delivered to another Czech payer from the amount of £194,000. Sk to the value of 1,160 thou Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported intra-Community deliveries to payers from the Czech Republic totalling 10,240,000 CZK (or 8,183,000 CZK) in their SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004.
However, the Czech acquirers did not report intra-Community acquisitions in the DAP.
On the basis of the international exchange of information, it was established that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer not mentioned in the SH filed by Slovak payers.
During the 1st quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased the value of intra-Community deliveries for this Czech payer by a total of 10 240 thou in the additional SH relating to the 2nd quarter of 2004.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax authority in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the correctness of the data in DAP's submission for Q2 2004, even if the actual acquirer failed to comply with the obligation to declare intra-Community acquisitions for that quarter.
The SAO, Czech Republic, found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the aforementioned Czech taxpayer was additionally assessed VAT for tax years 5 and 6/2004 of 3,640,000 CZK and for Q3 2004 of 3,305,000 CZK on purchased goods during these periods.
It can be seen from the above that tax administrations have had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences arising from errors in the acquirer's DAP, but also differences due to different reporting of intra-Community supply and acquisition data across EU Member States.
Unifying the conditions for reporting these data would lead to streamlining the control activities of tax administrations.
Acquisition of goods in SR
In SR, the APV DIS system makes it possible to compare the data on the value of goods acquired through VIES from other EU Member States with the data listed in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
The method by which the data are compared is called the ‘MIN-MAX method’.
This method recalculates the delivery values of the goods specified in the BI of payers from other EU Member States at the minimum and maximum exchange rate for the quarter in question.
The MIN-MAX interval will be created, which is used for comparisons with the acquisition values listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
The DR CLO will send information to tax administrations on the values of intra-community acquisitions listed in the DAP and the values of EU deliveries in VIES.
The tax authorities will decide for which VAT-registered persons the difference will be checked, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
Based on data provided by the DR CLO, the SAO collected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods for inspection at audited tax offices, of which 25 payers also acquired goods from the Czech Republic, for which the highest differences were found between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and those declared in the DAP.
The audit carried out by the SAO of the Slovak Republic confirmed that the tax authorities did not rigorously verify the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the accuracy of the data given in the Slovak acquirers' DAP.
As part of the audit, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations with specific tax entities.
During the audit of SAO SR at tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies, which showed significant differences in MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU member countries, the following were found to be among others:
In the DAP for Q4 2004, the Slovak payer did not give the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The tax office found that a company from the Czech Republic had mistakenly given the VAT number of this payer in SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while goods worth 19 184 thousand CZK were actually delivered to another Slovak payer.
Under the VIES system, the Slovak company was to acquire goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria in the 4th quarter of 2004 worth MIN 682 692 thousand Sk and MAX 715 105 thousand Sk.
This company filed DAPs for the periods in which it reported an EU acquisition value of only 480 599 thousand.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation, finding that the tax entity purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and to DAP did not indicate intra-Community deliveries by invoice date, but by delivery date.
Due to further irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU states, the tax authorities will request a verification of the value of the goods supplied using SCAC forms.
Acquisition of goods from EU member countries in Q4 2004 was not reported by the Slovak payer in the DAP.
Under the VIES system, this payer was to purchase goods worth MIN 11,286 thousand Sk and MAX 11,845 thousand Sk.
The tax office carried out a local investigation, which showed that the taxpayer had not purchased any goods from EU member countries in Q4 2004.
The SAO recommended that the tax office request a verification of the delivery of goods from EU member countries via the SCAC form.
In the VIES system, delivery of goods to a Slovak customer of MIN 557,000 Sk and MAX 565,000 Sk was reported.
In the DAP for the tax period of months 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not report any acquisitions of goods.
A local investigation by the tax administration found that the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier in the Czech Republic on 10 December 2004 for materials consumed in the repair of a hydraulic loader.
The SAO recommended a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO of the Slovak Republic, in 16 cases the tax authorities did not complete the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out a tax audit on the tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax inspections will be filed by the tax authorities after their implementation by the SAO.
Examples were:
The Slovak purchaser did not declare the acquisition of goods from EU member countries in the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004 and did not declare any tax for the tax period of 10 to 12/2004 and claimed a refund of excess VAT totalling 1,236 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation which showed that the taxpayer had purchased goods from the Czech Republic worth EUR 683,000 (about EUR 27,080,000 Sk).
The said goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
A Slovak payer for customers in the Russian Federation issued an invoice for the amount of EUR 683,000, which was not mentioned in the DAP submission.
The tax authority carries out a tax audit on the taxpayer.
The difference between the acquisition data reported in the Slovak payer's DAP for Q3 2004 to Q1 2005 and the data on deliveries reported by EU member state payers for each quarter was a total of 4,800,000 CZK.
The tax office found that the taxpayer purchased goods from suppliers in the Czech Republic and Belgium and then sold those goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by an export single customs declaration.
The acquisition of goods in the DAP was not specified by the tax entity, according to the statement of the company's manager, goods in transit were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The taxpayer did not submit any VAT records at the time of the local investigation.
A tax audit has been initiated on the payer.
5.2 International Level L3 Information Exchange
The exchange of information at level L3 is initiated by locally competent tax administrations who send their requests for information (RFID) or spontaneous information (SPI) relating to a particular tax entity or transaction through MF CLO, respectively.
DR CLO to another EU member country. For example, the objective of the LIO is to demonstrate the execution of a given transaction in intra-Community transactions, to verify a certain TIN, etc.
In the case of SPI, this is a communication of information relevant to tax administrations in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the exchange of information is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for responding to YEI was set at 3 months in Article 8 of this Regulation.
The conditions for the admissibility of applications are governed by the Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15.11.2004, which provides that, unless otherwise agreed by the Participating States, the ŽOI must relate to commercial transactions with a value of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
Where the RU relates to a commercial transaction of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to respond in view of its workload.
The procedure for handling received YEI by the Tax Administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of the internal timescales set for processing at individual organisational levels, is illustrated in the following diagram.
In the SR, the deadline for the discharge of the RU by the tax authorities has been set internally at 2 months so that the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 can be met.
The MF CLO accepted a total of 29 RWs and 3 SPIs from SR from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Of the 29 RUs accepted, 26 (or 89.7%) were discharged within the time limit of 3 months and 3 (or 10.3%) were discharged after that time limit.
During the same period, DR CLO accepted a total of 71 ZhOI and 7 SPI from the Czech Republic.
Of the 71 RUs accepted, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were discharged within the stipulated time limit of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were discharged after this time limit (for the remaining 2 cases, no discharge deadline could be determined from the material transmitted).
More detailed data on the time taken to process YES received by MF CLOs and DR CLOs are given in the following graph.
Reasons for sending an APO, as stated on SCAC forms, are given in the following table.
Conclusion
Compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT, as well as the use of the VIES system to exchange information between EU Member States, in particular to monitor the exercise of the right to VAT exemption, has been tested on the basis of international cooperation.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intra-Community transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
An examination of the selected transactions revealed that, on the basis of an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of the two countries had detected cases of companies making fictitious intra-Community commercial transactions to obtain excess VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers had failed to declare the correct amount of VAT on supplies received.
Furthermore, the audit found differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of the two countries.
The audit also highlighted problems caused by different reporting of intra-Community supplies and acquisitions data across EU Member States.
The harmonisation of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to streamlining of the control activities of national tax administrations.
Examination of the VAT administration and use of the VIES system by the financial and tax authorities revealed that the VIES system was not sufficiently used by all VIES options and the relevant statutory authorisations.
Furthermore, it was found that the VIES system did not in all cases provide up-to-date information on deliveries of goods and on the validity of taxable persons' VAT registration.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with the data processed after the completion of the inspection.
From the comparison of these data, it was clear that the SAO audit of SR had an effect not only on reducing the number of IA with erroneously reported TIN, but also on reducing the number of unrepaired errors in the SH.
In case of discrepancies in the reported data, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or to carry out tax checks.
The SAO, Czech Republic did not have such an option under the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The lessons learned from the audit action showed that VIES provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
As there continues to be scope for tax evasion in this area, increased attention needs to be paid to intra-community transactions when managing VAT.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Najvyššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introduction Word
This information material provides an overview of the progress and results of parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which focused on the area of administration based on added value and excise duties.
Cooperation between the supreme audit institutions of the two countries was carried out on the basis of the control cooperation agreement concluded in February 2004.
The theme of the parallel control actions was chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes contribute significantly to the revenue of the national budgets of both countries.
The design of value added tax, allowing the refund of excess deduction, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duty, particularly on tobacco and tobacco products, ethyl alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Given the need to address this issue comprehensively across the European Union, the VAT Working Group has been set up by the supreme audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union, with both countries' highest audit offices actively involved.
The greatest benefits of the control actions undertaken can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in the joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax management in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The experience and knowledge gained will be used in the framework of planned indirect tax controls, mainly aimed at involving the tax administrations of the two States in the VIES system, which allows the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union to be controlled.
Report on the results of the Value Added Tax and Excise Administration Review for 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Object of control:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the tax administration process for the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On 11.2.2004, the Contract for Cooperation in Audit Activities between the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) and the NajHigher Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (SAO SR) was concluded. The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implementation of parallel control actions "Value Added Tax and Excise Tax," included in the SAO's 2004 audit work plan under No 04/07, and "Control of the management process of dane pri administration, control and recovery of taxes on prized value and rebrebrebrebate taxes," included in SAO SR's audit work plan under No 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract and producing a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
Both parties undertook in the contract to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from the tax files kept by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain when checking the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the relevant State.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic), the control was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of southern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected financial offices: the Tax Office for Prague 1, the Tax Office for Prague 3, the Tax Office in Český Budějovice, the Tax Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Tax Office in Hodonin, the Tax Office in Jihlava, the Tax Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Tax Office in Kroměříž, the Tax Office in Písek, the Tax Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Velký Meziříčí.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as ‘SR’) was carried out by the Tax and Customs Division of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO Expozituras SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 10 selected tax offices:
Bratislava Tax Office pre Selected Tax Entities, Bratislava Tax Office III, Trnava Tax Office, Pú-chov Tax Office, Banská Bystrica Tax Office I, Liptovský Mikuláš Tax Office, Žilina Tax Office I, Žilina II Tax Office, Košice Tax Office I and Košice Tax Office IV.
Target of control
The aim of the control actions was to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of financial and tax authorities and customs authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise duties, with a focus on the collection of such taxes on the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the Customs Database and the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic and to verify them in tax returns at the relevant financial and tax offices respectively.
The audited period was 2002 and 2003.
2. Review of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
In the framework of the international cooperation of the SAO, the SAO of the Czech Republic transmitted from the Customs Database 22 206 items of the Uniform Customs Declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, and vice versa, the SAO of the Slovak Republic forwarded 30 221 items of the JCD to the SAO of the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic.
A comparison was made between the printed JCD items from the Customs database of the Czech Republic and the Customs database of the Slovak Republic.
Out of 5,883 selected JCD items from the CR Customs Database, a total of 43% of related JCD items were assigned.
Out of the 12,343 selected JCD entries from the SR customs database, a total of 26% of the related JCD entries were assigned.
On the basis of the unassigned JCD entries, a selection of the files of the tax entities was made at the financial and tax offices, where the declared imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Based on the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and the financial and tax authorities respectively, the implementation of the reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified in the territory of the second state.
The SAO and SAO SR carried out a joint pilot inspection at the Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma border customs crossing, in which both parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The audit did not identify any deficiencies in the record of selected cases of imports and exports of goods made in 2002.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine trade transactions made between trading partners from both countries and has highlighted deficiencies in the record of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of control results
The audit of the SAO and SAO of the Slovak Republic focused on imports and exports of spirit and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, as well as other types of goods, in the field of international cooperation.
On the basis of a check of the files of tax entities at selected financial and tax offices, the SAO asked for verification of the execution of exports of goods declared on 40 JCDs for a total statistical value of 15,301,093 CZK and the SAO SR for verification of exports for a statistical value of 56,989 Sk.
Among other things, the SAO and SAO SR found the following:
- the commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, making it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic,
- errors in the entry of data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- there has been no evidence of corresponding imports into the SR for some Czech exports.
In such cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of improperly claiming value added tax deductions;
- Tax entities failed to comply with some of the statutory obligations in reporting imports and exports on value added tax returns;
- shortcomings have been identified in the work of the financial and/or tax offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duties and in their interaction with customs offices.
In the field of value added tax and excise duties, international trade will continue to need attention in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activity of tax administrations in the administration of value added tax.
The basis for effective control of excise duties is the control of document circulation, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on the import and export of goods.
3. Description of the value added tax and excise tax situation
Value Added Tax
Value added tax (‘VAT’) was levied by the tax and tax authorities on taxable transactions effected within the country and by the customs authorities on importation of the goods.
The revenue from the tax was due to the difference between the tax liability collected and the excess VAT refunded in the case of the tax authorities.
The VAT revenue at the customs offices was determined by the amount of tax they collected.
The tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected, in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, in the tax deductions applied to the financial and tax authorities respectively.
For most financial and tax authorities, excess VAT deductions exceeded tax liability.
VAT is one of the flagship taxes in terms of state budget revenue, as it accounted for about 31% of the tax revenue of the state budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and approximately 42% of the tax revenue of the state budget of the Slovak Republic.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT refunds totalled CZK 231.4 billion.
The total VAT collection in SR in 2003 amounted to 83.8 bn Sk.
Tax and customs authorities collected 187.0 billion in VAT in 2003, and refunded excess VAT totalled 103.2 billion Sk.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (‘SpD’) was carried out by the competent financial and tax authorities and, on importation, by customs authorities of products subject to SpD.
The share of SpD in the tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic was about 16% in 2003 and about 19% in SR.
The total collection of SpDs collected in the Czech Republic by financial and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to 85.6 billion CZK and in the Slovak Republic amounted to 38.0 billion CZK.
4. Control Action Progress
The cooperation between the SAO and SAO SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was made; in the second stage, the results of this comparison were used in the mutual verification of the implementation of selected trade transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and in the checks carried out on the territory of the two states.
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation on parallel VAT and SpD controls was presented at a working meeting of SAO and SAO SR representatives in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting was held at which, among other things, a selection of commodities was agreed - goods which posed a significant risk in complying with customs and tax legislation: - ethyl alcohol, tariff headings 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff headings 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff headings 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff subheadings 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
The two parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be made: (a) from unallocated items identified by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic; (b) from entities carrying out imports and exports regularly or on a one-off basis in large volumes; (c) on the basis of findings from inspections carried out by selected tax and financial authorities.
4.2. Comparison of Customs Databases of the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic
In the first stage, the mutual attribution mechanism of JCD items registered in the Customs Databases of the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
Subsequently, a proportion of exports from the Czech Republic were compared with imports into the Slovak Republic for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the Customs Tariff:
- 2207 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol or higher; Ethyl alcohol and other spirits denatured, of any strength,
- 2208 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol; spirits, liqueurs and other spirituous beverages,
- 2401 Unmanufactured tobacco; tobacco waste,
- 2402 Cigars (whether or not with their ends cut off), cigars (cigarillos) and cigarettes made of tobacco or tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and punishments (essences);
- 8525 20 91 Transmission apparatus containing reception equipment: For cellular network (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmission apparatus incorporating reception equipment: Other,
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with the apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling in subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
The JCD entries from the Customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic were attributed to each other based on the conformity of the individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle carrying the cargo, date of crossing the national border, tariff heading, etc.).
The results of the comparison are presented in the following tables and graphs.
The cross-attribution of individual imports and exports was hampered by, among other things, the fact that trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides.
For example, an export from the Czech Republic declared on one export JCD was declared on the territory of SR for multiple import JCD, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors influencing the success of the attribution were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of corresponding imports in the customs database of another.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited financial and tax offices respectively.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that carried out imports/exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, which could not be identified in both databases.
