Monitoring the handling of special mineral oils, which are a group of mineral oils under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion), whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2 s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: a flash point lower than 150 °C, at least 20 % by volume including losses up to 350 °C shall be distilled during the distillation test.
These mineral oils were misused as an additive in the finished fuel, in particular diesel fuel, or were directly used or sold for motor propulsion because the physical characteristics are very similar.
Entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres must register with the tax authorities.
For the issuing of the registration, the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be fulfilled, which shall apply throughout 2 Except for beer, fruit wines, other wines and meads and fruit spirits obtained by firing.
No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 For example, when using mineral oil as propellant (excluding navigation on waters other than private pleasure craft) or as a fuel ingredient, when the markings are at fault for their use.
registration.
As of 30.11.2016, the Register of Persons Handling Specific Mineral Oils contained 54 valid marketing authorisations, four marketing authorisations were revoked on the proposal of the marketing authorisation holder.
The electronic register shall contain detailed information on receipt, own consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, notification numbers of acquisitions by the tax authorities, places of storage and consumption, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption or, at the time of sale, place of delivery and customer registration number.
Notification of any acquisition of the special mineral oil must be given to the tax authority between 24 and 72 hours before acceptance.
The identification of the commercial partners, the name and nomenclature of the particular mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of the consumption or information on the sale or transfer shall be notified.
The notification of the estimated quantity in the relevant year of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notices of the purpose of use and labelling, the place of storage or consumption, the identification details of the person to whom the special mineral oil is resold or transferred, shall be provided before any change.
Notifications shall be made electronically using smart forms or a PDFa data container.
In 2015, persons handling special mineral oils filed 630 notifications.
The provision and forfeiture of special mineral oils and, where appropriate, means of transport must be pronounced by the tax authorities in cases where they find the disposal of special mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to fulfil his obligation to notify.
As in the case of non-compliance in the transport of products subject to excise duties, these deficiencies cannot be remedied retrospectively.
Registration of a fuel distributor is mandatory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Registered fuel distributors may only be persons meeting the following criteria:
Compulsory trade authority concession (a specific form of business licence).
The customs office shall give an opinion on the application for the concession, or on the appointment of the responsible representative, as appropriate, examining whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or the members of the applicant's statutory body, the legal person and the appointed responsible representative meet the condition of reliability.
Where such persons meet the reliability condition, the customs office shall issue a favourable opinion.
A reliable person is a person of impeccable character, from the point of view of criminal assets, customs and tax law.
Expertise is a condition of the concession.
The indebtedness of the same circle of people as in the case of reliability.
The debtor is the person who provides sufficient guarantees that he or she will duly and timely discharge his or her payment obligations to the State, i.e. he or she does not have arrears on the State budget and on universal health insurance.
A fuel distributor shall not be prohibited by a court or administrative authority from carrying out an activity which makes it impossible to carry out his activity.
The fuel distributor must not be wound up or bankrupt.
The deposit of a security (or bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. around €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000 (i.e. around €370,000) after three years of registration as a fuel distributor and the fulfilment of other conditions.
Notice of fuel distribution shall be given by the distributor to the customs office within 20 days of the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall include details of the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The data reported are data on trading partners, document numbers, product selected, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
Entitlement to repayment of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced in late 2014.
Only an activity which is clearly related to an activity carried out on land can be claimed for reimbursement of excise duty on mineral oils.
In 2015, there were about 64,000 claims for tax refunds, totalling CZK 1,172,844,680 (or €43,401,720).
As of 2017, the government of the Czech Republic has also introduced a refund of fuel excise duty to livestock farmers.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, are involved in cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats will be able to make this claim.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on sales of old-rate tobacco products
In response to the long-term failure to achieve budgeted revenue from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced with effect from 1.12.2014 restrictions on the sale of old-rate tobacco products in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid by the use of tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco label is understood as placing it on a unit packet (Section 116 of the Excise Duties Act).
For the application of the rate of excise duty, the production of the tobacco product in the condition intended for the final consumer is decisive, without the need for it to be removed, delivered, dispatched or sold, or sold to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the excise duty rate appears on the tobacco sticker along with the price to the final consumer of cigarettes, and the sticker indicates the number of items in the pack or the quantity of tobacco to be smoked in kilograms.
The tobacco sticker has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the sale of unit packets of ready-to-eat cigarettes bearing a tobacco sticker with the previous (old) rate of duty has been fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month after the new rate of excise duty takes effect.
Developments in the removal of tobacco labels in 2014 and comparisons with those in previous years show that tobacco manufacturers have significantly pre-loaded tobacco products with the "old" tax rate each year, effectively shifting the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Raw tobacco tax
Because of the misuse of raw tobacco to produce tobacco products without the permission of the tax authorities and the non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and the monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as measures against tax fraud.
With effect from 1 July 2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products shall be subject to excise duty on delivery to another Member State or a third country or for which the origin, the purpose of use or the person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been proved.
Restrictions on handling raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, the marking of unit packets with surveillance tape and restrictions on sales at designated points have been added to the restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Manufacturing equipment for the processing of tobacco raw material and the manufacture of tobacco products shall not be subject to customs supervision.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or modified.
Only a person meeting the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative may be a registered person, which is valid throughout the registration period.
The conditions of registration are: (a) authorisation to operate a business enabling the activity of a person storing raw tobacco, (b) reliability, (c) debt-free, (d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been declared prohibited from carrying out his activity, (e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) the granting of a bond of CZK 20,000 (i.e. around €740,000).
The electronic register must include the date of receipt or delivery of the raw tobacco, the document number, the identification of the commercial partner, an indication of the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco must be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours prior to receipt or dispatch.
Information on the commercial partner, quantity of raw tobacco, storage address, purpose of use and carrier details shall be reported.
The notification of the estimated quantity in the relevant year of raw tobacco received or shipped shall be submitted by the body together with the registration application or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically through a data container in PDFa format.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document containing the prescribed particulars.
Excise Tax Legislation in SR
The legal framework regulating the area of excise duties in the SR is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its single tax system.
The various types of excise taxes are exhaustively determined by the SR legislation, which is similar to that of surrounding countries.
Definition of legislation in SR
Legislative arrangements for excise duties are secured by four laws on a subject-by-subject basis.
The harmonisation was achieved by the adoption of the following excise laws: Act No 98/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530/2011 Z. z., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609/2007 Z. z., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All excise laws are substantive laws and deal with the taxation of the object of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No 563/2009 of the Z. z., on the Administration of Taxes (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulating the administration of taxes, the rights and obligations of tax subjects and other persons.
This legal framework has transposed individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008 concerning the general arrangements for excise duty and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, and has also transposed provisions of other directives and European Community legislation.
Structure of legislative changes for different types of excise duties in relation to the subject matter of the SR inspection
Since 2011, the excise administration legislation has undergone several major changes to the structure of individual excise duties.
In EMCS, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duty under the conditional exemption regime has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system where such traffic is monitored in real time.
Under the EMCS electronic system, the suspension of access to the EMCS by tax entities was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office has the option to suspend access precisely when there is a justified concern about a tax that has not been paid or determined in previous tax years and is not recoverable.
This concerns the payment of the tax, as the composition of the security is required for the transport of excise goods, but it is released by the end of the transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011 when the option to use so-called red diesel was removed.
Labelled gas oil, commonly also called red diesel, was one of the mineral oils.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific legally defined purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The abolition of red diesel was aimed at reducing the public deficit, simplifying the system of taxation of mineral oils and reducing the administrative burden on the businesses concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel retailer.
The purpose of this legal amendment was to introduce a record-keeping obligation for all service stations.
Making the movement of taxed petrol and diesel more transparent is linked to the obligation to buy petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
New institutes of tax entities were introduced in 2014, namely the distributor of motor fuels and the consumer of motor fuels.
This change has contributed to eliminating the emergence of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and has clarified the movement of these propellants (see Annex 4, Schedule A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
However, in SR, these mineral oils are not subject to the indication requirement.
Excise Duty on Tobacco Products
As part of the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of the tobacco raw material, the scope of the Tobacco Ingredient Act has been extended and a new tax entity - the tobacco trader - has been introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, an obligation to register technological equipment for the manufacture of tobacco products has been introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packages of tobacco products.
Cigarettes, cigarillos and tobacco are marked with a check mark.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the surveillance stamps must apply electronically to the customs office to issue the surveillance stamps, using an information system for the collection of the surveillance stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax authority.
One state stamp printing house was set up - in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of surveillance stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system for printing control stamps strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the control stamp to simply verify that goods come from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1st to 2nd place is the checksum; 3. place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th to 8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12. instead is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
The control mark intended for the labelling of cigarettes shall also bear the price of cigarettes, the mark for the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in consumer packs and the length of cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer, as the original three substantive law provisions were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was drafted mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to alcoholic beverage taxation, solutions to their production, monitoring of movement, ensuring tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, streamline the administration of the tax, reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
A new way of tackling the issue of the taxation of different types of alcoholic beverages introduced the application of a uniform rate of excise duty to alcoholic beverages and took into account the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength.
For still wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the final product shall be taken into account.
The concentration of beer is also expressed as a percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the finished product.
A category of small-scale fermented beverage producer has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household of not more than 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the surveillance stamps must apply electronically to the customs office to issue the surveillance stamps, using an information system for the collection of the surveillance stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax authority.
One state stamp printing house was set up - in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of surveillance stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Schedule B) and the elimination of falsification of control stamps.
The new system for printing control stamps strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the control stamp to simply verify that goods come from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1st to 2nd place is the checksum; 3. place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th to 8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12. instead is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
Comparison and Evaluation
Comparison
Excise taxes on ethyl alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common law No 353/2003 Coll.
The solid fuel tax, the tax on natural gas and certain other gases and the tax on electricity are part of Act No 261/2007 Coll.
In the SR, by contrast, every excise duty is regulated by a special law, apart from the Alcoholic Beverages Excise Tax Act, which contains a tax on ethyl alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A separate law regulates excise duties on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, from 1.1.2015, the issuance of an authorisation to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Law on Excise Duties is subject, among other things, to proof of the economic stability of the applicants, which is verified annually by the customs authorities by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the RS, a similar form of analysis is undertaken only when deciding to waive or reduce the collateral tax.
The FŘ SR carries out tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the finance directorate over the handling of the control marks for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printing works and their sale to individual customers.
The law provides that Mincovna Kremnica, a state-owned company, is to produce the inspection marks.
The production of tobacco stickers and check strips in the Czech Republic is not supervised by the customs authorities at the printer.
Tobacco stickers and check bands will be taken from the printer by the competent territorial office of the Kutna customs office.
Tobacco labels are taken over by their customers in this territorial location, surveillance tapes to mark the ethyl alcohol are further distributed to individual locally competent tax authorities according to the location of the markings.
The Czech legislation does not define the manufacturers of tobacco stickers and check bands.
In the Slovak Republic there is an obligation to register technological installations for the production of tobacco products or parts thereof, in the Czech Republic there is no such obligation.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco label bears excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when the tobacco stickers are removed from the competent customs office.
In SR, on the other hand, the control mark does not include excise duty on tobacco products.
A refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced in the Czech Republic during the audited period for their use for agricultural plant primary production, so-called green diesel.
As of 2017, this tax refund was extended to livestock production.
In the SR, such support for farmers is not in place (it existed until 31.12.2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a bond of CZK 20 million (i.e. €740,000) has been introduced in the Czech Republic for fuel distributors.
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1,891 in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1,717 tax entities).
In the SR, a similar fuel distributor is introduced, but without the deposit needed to ensure excise duty on mineral oils.
In SR, 303 distributors were registered in 2014 and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
In SR, there is an institute of fuel retailer and fuel consumer, which is licensed by the local competent customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils are subject to labelling, as well as some other mineral oils; in the Slovak Republic, following the abolition of so-called red diesel, the labelling of mineral oils is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the surveillance tape for the marking of spirit contains an eight-digit individual code to verify the origin of spirit and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spirit spirit level under which the record of surveillance tapes is kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the surveillance tape shall be entered in the register on the following working day.
The holder of the tape shall also be required to notify its use within the same time limit.
In SR, the control mark for the labelling of ethyl alcohol in a consumer pack contains a unique 12-digit identification number which, if used, is communicated to the tax authorities once a month and is used to check the authenticity of the control mark.
The register contains the number of control marks taken, used and returned.
Both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have introduced the institute of compulsory registration or registration of the distributor of alcohol.
In SR, registration is subject to conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol of at least €100 000 or paid-up capital of at least €100 000; minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining registration is subject, among other things, to a deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) in favour of the tax administration for the entire duration of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In the RS, the production of ethyl alcohol, not only in consumer packaging, requires the permanent presence of the tax authorities.
In the Czech Republic, the production of ethyl alcohol in a consumer pack requires a special form of registration of the person required to mark ethyl alcohol, with a condition of bail in favour of the tax authorities of between CZK 100,000 (i.e. €3,700) and CZK 5,000 (i.e. €185,000) according to the quantity of control tapes taken and the installation of a tracking device with continuous access by the tax authorities.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic goes far beyond the EU's minimum requirements for the object and management of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as those identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax administrations to do more to prevent the emergence of possible tax evasion.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, as part of the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw material (e.g. leaves), excise duty on raw tobacco and tobacco raw material was introduced in addition to EU legislation.
Although neither raw tobacco nor tobacco raw material is a harmonised tobacco product, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic monitor their movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic may recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that checking economic stability for applicants for authorisation under the Excise Tax Act has worked well because it reduces the risks of tax arrears.
For this reason, both supervisory institutions recommend applying such screening also in SR conditions.
The distribution of control stamps is more efficient in SR than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden customs with the costs related to transportation between the printer and the purchaser of control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The SR's financial administration has a better understanding of the existence and location of technological equipment for the manufacture of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the levying of the tax on tobacco products is more efficient, as the order of the tobacco sticker itself is a tax return with subsequent payment of the tax.
The financial administration in the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the sales points for propellants, thanks to the introduction of the "seller of propellants" and "consumer of propellants" institutes.
The introduction of mandatory labelling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils at a reduced rate of tax, or exempt from tax.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and SR (2014), a new check tape or stamp containing an identification code was introduced.
The surveillance tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation has abandoned its introduction.
Impacts cannot yet be assessed due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of the consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark or tape is an effective measure to combat tax evasion.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic can also recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States.
The SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-ient approach that does not block tax entities' funds.
By contrast, the CR's approach is rather restrictive, since it introduces a bail-in weighing on the cash flow of tax entities, but it reduces the risk of tax arrears more.
Development of excise revenue
An excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State to increase the revenue of the State budget and also to regulate the amount of goods sold whose consumption is considered harmful to individuals and/or to society (the regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Communication from the Commission: EUROPE 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3.3.2010 under the Resource Efficient Europe flagship initiative, the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, including by revising energy taxation with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
To achieve the EC's aim, Member States should seek to shift the tax burden from labour to energy and environmental taxation, among other things, as part of a greater "greening" of tax systems.
The collection of tax revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic includes the collection of excise duty on mineral oils, tobacco products, ethyl alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP is also monitored by, among others, the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Both supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to query the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties linked to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP fell slightly, according to OECD data.
The European Central Bank's rate of exchange was used to convert the amounts in CZK into € on the 31st 12th of the relevant year.
The denomination of CZK against €1 in 2013 weakened by 9.1% year-on-year against 2012 (from 25.140 to 27.425).
This was mainly due to the monetary policy decision of the CNB Bank Board on 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of excise collection, excise rates and per capita income in € have decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the share of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off revenue shortfall from excise duties on tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of old-rate tobacco products.
The share of excise duties is also affected by a rise in revenue tax collection, which has grown significantly due to the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
Excise duties on mineral oils account for the largest share of total excise collections (about 55.7% in 2015), but this has fallen despite significant growth in the economy compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as a measure against tax fraud.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively impacting the tax's revenue.
A negligible proportion are the natural gas tax, the solid fuel tax and the electricity tax, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to the surrounding states.
In the absence of a rate increase, their share will decline in the future in view of the ever-decreasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on ethyl alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a massive case of tax fraud involving the putting into circulation of untaxed ethyl alcohol, ethyl alcohol containing methanol or an under-denatured ethyl alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a series of measures against such behaviour and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the 2012 recovery by €4m.
The share of tax on tobacco products has increased as a result of increasing rates.
The basic rates of excise duties varied between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on manufactured tobacco, where the rate was increased mainly to comply with Council Directive 2011/64/EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on manufactured tobacco.
As a result of the CNB's currency intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, excluding the tax on tobacco products, has fallen significantly. For tobacco products, it has risen only slightly.
In relation to price growth, GDP or living standards, the indexation of the excise rate is not set, so the excise duties function of regulating socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
As the Czech Republic's economic growth and living standards rise, real excise rates fall.
7 Indexation – automatic adjustment of a certain economic quantity for inflation, this adjustment is made on the basis of a law or a contract (in the case of pensions paid by the State, this is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties linked to macroeconomic indicators in SR
In the current legislation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the indexation of the level of excise rates to the evolution of consumer prices is not addressed because they are fixed.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Of all the excise taxes introduced in Slovakia, it is the excise duty on mineral oils that accounts for the largest share of the national budget's full-year tax revenue, with the proportion not falling below 52% over the whole period audited.
The second largest share is accounted for by excise duties on tobacco products.
This tax accounts on average for around 32% of total excise collection.
Between 2012 and 2015 there was an increase in the collection of excise duty per capita of SR.
This development is due to a rise in excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption by the population in a given year.
The growth in excise collection per capita of SR is constant and corresponds to the evolution of excise rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the reduction in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention on the currency rate of the crown against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which is about 2.7 and 2.8 times higher in the Czech Republic, respectively, but per capita of the Czech Republic the collection is already only about 1/3 higher for these selected products.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise taxes in the Czech Republic and the price of CZK against the € for foreign consumers.
For the mineral oil tax, the cause is also greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, increasing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a not insignificant effect.
Evaluation Real rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic were falling as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in total tax revenues is not rising and there is no shift away from labour taxation to taxation of consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the figures achieved for the share of excise duties have consistently been above the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is influenced in particular by the change in excise rates, the development of economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures, which are subsidised by the state in various forms, will need to be compensated by other revenues or reductions in state spending.
In the absence of indexation of excise rates in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, their regulatory function is reduced and there is insufficient support for the EU's objectives of making Europe less dependent on environmentally harmful sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic translates into higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the management of excise duties, i.e. it expresses the level of expenditure per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the administrative cost effectiveness.
The efficiency of the tax administration affects the scope and organisational set-up of the tax administration, the management of the organisation, the legal environment and the level of computerisation of the various activities.
The calculation of the administrative cost effectiveness of the tax administration by the conversion rate method is based on the number of employees involved in the management of excise duties in a line-managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the management of excise duties is carried out, among other activities, by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organisational arm of the state and an entity.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax is managed by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, with customs authorities being the internal organisational unit, costs and revenues are included in aggregate for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, in view of the possibility to compare the efficiency of excise administration, the expenses and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were also included in the calculation of administrative cost efficiency.
Administrative costs of excise administration in the Czech Republic
The Administration of Excise Duties is a complex of administrative tasks carried out mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial control tasks are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
In particular, excise duties are administered by the following departments:
Directorate General of Customs
Department 23 TAX
Division 231 - Tax Methodologies monitors and proposes legislative measures, provides interpretation of legislation, methodically manages and coordinates: the execution of tax administration and related regulatory agendas, in particular tax management and related control and oversight activities, the administration of transport of selected products;
Unit 232 - ELO and search performs searches and methodically manages traffic controls for selected products and ensures international ELO and EMCS cooperation;
Unit 233 - Tax Controls methodically manages and coordinates the execution of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30
Unit 301 — Legal carries out methodological work in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative procedure, tax inspection process, registration procedure, declaratory proceedings, payment of taxes, fines for late claims of tax, penalties and interest;
Unit 302 — Administrative Activities carries out decision-making in cases where the legislation provides for the remit of the DG, e.g. deciding on the delegation of the entity's territorial jurisdiction to another materially competent tax authority, deciding on the attraction, i.e. taking over the matter from a higher tax authority, appealing against customs decisions and examining incentives for inaction in tax and administrative procedures;
Unit 303 — Revenue and Enforcement Administration methodically manages, coordinates and performs international cooperation tasks in recovering tax arrears and carrying out insolvency-related tasks;
Department 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION AID
Unit 601 - Risk and criminal analysis provides and conducts risk analyses and is involved in managing executive risks and planning control activities and control actions;
Unit 604 - Financial Analysis carries out financial analysis in the customs administration, in particular in the context of the authorisation procedure.
Customs offices carry out agenda activities at various points in the county, and even agendas are dispersed in multiple locations:
Unit 02 — Analysis and information support which carries out risk analysis, risk profile management and the collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1
Division 11 — Legal and administrative activities, which handles supporting documents, opinions and submissions to the Appellate Body, issues authorisation decisions in relation to the administration of excise duties and environmental taxes, the Law on compulsory marking of ethyl alcohol and the Law on ethyl alcohol, decides on securing payment for a tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Department 3 - TAX
Division 31 - Tax which carries out the agendas: tax supervision of taxable entities, e.g. monitoring of compliance with the conditions laid down in the permits issued, supervision of the functionality and correctness of the production equipment for the production of ethyl alcohol and the determination of the quantity and concentration of the produced ethyl alcohol, professional supervision of the denaturing of ethyl alcohol, physical checks on the management of excise duties; non-tax checks on controls on the basis of laws having an indirect relationship with excise duties, in particular the control of the compulsory labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils, control of the taxation of selected products, control of the marking of tobacco products, control of the sale by means of the Law on fuel, and other acts of goods are carried out in connection with the Law on free movement of goods; registration of economic operators for taxes, registration of persons obliged to mark ethyl alcohol and of distributors of ethyl alcohol, and registration of fuel distributors; tax administration, in particular the conduct of the tax procedure on assessment and prescription, where applicable refund, monitoring of the tax collateral and its use to pay the tax, conducting searches;
Division 39 - Tobacco stickers and check tapes - is the organisational unit of the Central Bohemian Customs Office and carries out activities in ordering, manufacturing and distributing and disposing of tobacco stickers and check tapes.
For the disposal of returned/damaged tobacco labels, both Customs and DG representatives are present to oversee the disposal process and to draw up a record of the disposal.
For control tapes for the marking of ethyl alcohol, the director of the customs office shall appoint a three-person panel for the disposal of discarded non-removed/returned control tapes by shredding by internal management act.
After the physical shredding of the surveillance tapes has been carried out, the chairman of the winding-up board shall ensure that the details of the destroyed surveillance tapes are recorded;
Department 5 - CONTROL,
Division 52 - Tax Inspections carries out tax inspections;
Department 6 - SUPERVISION
Unit 61 — Supervision of entities is supervised by entities at points of sale, e.g. control of the sale of spirits and tobacco products;
Unit 62 - Mobile Surveillance carries out traffic control of selected products en route.
Administrative costs of excise administration in SR
Since 1.1.2012, the Finance Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a challenging transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The creation of the PŘ SR was also reflected in the staff mix of the newly formed departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In the context of the performance of excise management, excise management activities within the organisational structure of the FŘ SR have been integrated into a larger number of different sections and related departments.
Finance Directorate of the Slovak Republic Customs and Taxation Section FŘ SR Excise Duties Department (Slovak-wide scope):
excise departments - guide and coordinate excise management activities; draw up expert opinions; submit proposals and comments on legislative changes; issues decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax entities; assigns and deletes registration sampling numbers;
Tax Supervisory Unit — directs and coordinates activities in the exercise of fiscal supervision and control; exercises fiscal supervision;
ELO and SPD systems unit — directs and coordinates administrative mutual cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including exchange of information through SEED and MVS systems; provides management and updating in SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
Control Marks Department – regulates printing activities and handling of control marks; exercises fiscal supervision over the handling and disposal of printing sheets and control marks in the printing works.
Vice President of Financial Management
Excise and Customs Remedies Department (Slovakia-wide scope):
excise appeals unit — reviews customs decisions on the basis of regular and extraordinary appeals made; appeal procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
A section of customs offices was created in the course of 2012; under it were directly incorporated individual customs offices (9 customs offices) which have a territorial scope determined by higher territorial units, with the exception of one customs office which was established, inter alia, to carry out tasks in relation to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
excise departments — carrying out methodological activities in relation to customs offices' branches and customs offices' stations; for the selected entities, the direct actions of the tax administration are determined by the registration (tax warehouse, beneficiary recurring, registered shipper), the amount of the tax collateral, the determination and refund of the tax, the tax supervision and the tax control; decides to waive the deposit of the tax collateral; Decides to waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee in a tax warehouse for ethyl alcohol;
legal department - decision-making activities on tax infringements; activities relating to ordinary and extraordinary remedies; tax execution procedures;
Customs office branch - decides on registration (except for tax warehouse, receiver, registered consignor), the amount of tax collateral; prescribes and refunds tax; performs tax oversight and fiscal control; decides on the security and forfeiture of goods;
Customs office station — exercise of fiscal supervision over the possession and movement of goods subject to excise duties; Ensuring the exercise of permanent tax supervision in a tax warehouse for ethyl alcohol; deciding on the security and forfeiture of goods.
Spending by the SR's financial administration on excise management is growing steadily as, with the exception of wage increases, investments are increasing to manage taxes efficiently and electronicalise the financial administration.
Although excise revenue grew, spending grew faster as a result of IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
In the Slovak Republic, wage expenditure is significantly affected by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol, which is not applied by the Czech Republic.
Expenditure by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on excise management increased more significantly between 2012 and 2015 in 2015, mainly due to an increase in wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise taxes also grew at about the same rate.
Wage expenditure in the Czech Republic is positively influenced by the wider competencies of the customs administration, e.g. weighing of trucks, checking the fulfilment of duties related to the myth, compared to the SR.
Administrative cost efficiency in SR shows a slightly worsening trend year-on-year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but spending per employee increased.
In the Czech Republic, too, the number of employees did not change significantly, but spending per employee grew more slowly compared to the Slovak Republic.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, wage growth is a major factor in the deterioration of administrative expenditure efficiency, which can be seen as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a high administrative burden in excise management seems to be a negative factor, as confirmed by the shrinking number of staff in excise management.
In the SR, however, managing excise duties at lower incomes is significantly more challenging for staffing capacity.
Performance indicators of excise administration
The management of excise duties is a set of activities aimed at correctly identifying, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
The main processes in the management of excise duties are tax assessment, authorisation and registration, transport supervision, control and search of tax subjects.
Numbers of administrative tasks and entities managed are indicators of the performance of the tax administration.
The correlation between the observed indicator and the number of tax administrations expresses the efficiency of the tax administration's activities and defines the cost of a particular activity.
Authorisation and registration for the activity are essential preconditions for the handling and transport of selected products for commercial purposes under a conditional exemption scheme.
The tax authorities are required to perform a systematic administration of authorised or registered entities, with a focus on supervising compliance with the legislation and conditions laid down by the tax authorities, to which adequate staffing resources must be allocated.
The observed indicator was the number of valid permits or registrations for activity at 31 December of each year.
The number of permits or registrations issued is not the same as the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are concrete administrative acts on the merits.
The administrative acts monitored are the frequency of the most significant actions of the tax administration (tax claims, traffic administration in EMCS), or those that are a sequence of actions ending in a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Permission and registration for activities in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
The products selected may be manufactured, processed, stored, received or dispatched with the permission of the tax authorities to operate a tax warehouse.
If the operator of the tax warehouse has multiple warehouses, a permit shall be issued for each separately, including securing the tax.
Tax security is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administration (i.e. the physical presence of the official and the securing of the equipment by the tax administration's accounts).
Permanent tax supervision is not applied in the Czech Republic.
The tax warehouse operator also registers for tax under Section 125 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.
An authorisation to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products, conditionally exempt from tax, from the place of importation to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to the place of exportation in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (replacing the status of registered consignor under Article 4(10) of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels, excluding tax, which are analogous to tax warehouse permits.
Growing spirit produces alcohol at a reduced 50% tax rate (£14,300/hl ethanol) — fruit spirits for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and operating permits are issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced rate of tax can be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of a grower destined for personal consumption for the production period (July-June).
The register of cultivation burning, kept by the operators of the brandy and made available to the tax authorities, must include details of the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
A beneficiary for re-receipt of selected products and a beneficiary for one-off receipt of selected products shall be entitled, subject to the authorisation of the tax authorities and the conditions laid down, to receive or re-receive selected products on a one-off basis under a conditional system shipped from another Member State.
The beneficiary is not the operator of the tax warehouse and may not store or dispatch the selected products under the conditional exemption scheme.
The user of the selected tax-exempt products is the legal or natural person who accepts and uses, or sells the selected tax-exempt products to another user, according to §§ 52a or §53 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.; users have the status of tax entities without the obligation to register for tax.
Exempt products selected may be accepted and used only on the basis of a valid authorisation, and only from the supplier indicated in the authorisation.
On the basis of the authorisation, exempt mineral oils may be sold to another authorisation holder or user who is authorised to use mineral oils without authorisation.
Mineral oils may be sold exempt without a licence in statutory cases, e.g.:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year, if produced by the user himself or generated by his activity,
Selected mineral oils exempt from tax in unit packets of not more than 20 litres for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production, and for sale at the same time to the final consumer.
Selected exempt products may be transported with proof of exemption.
The distributor of the consumer-packaged spirit shall be entitled, after compulsory registration with the tax authorities, to sell or otherwise transfer the ethyl alcohol put into free circulation for tax purposes.
A storer of raw tobacco is entitled to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, subject to registration with the tax authorities and the conditions laid down.
A person handling special mineral oils shall be entitled to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils which are in bulk or placed in packaging exceeding 220 litres, on the basis of registration with the tax authorities and subject to specified conditions.
The fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel in the territory of the Czech Republic, except for the sale of fuel from a service station, on the basis of the concession issued and the registration of the tax administrator under specified conditions.
The PHM transport must be accompanied by a tax document, proof of sale or proof of transport, where appropriate, a distribution plan and bottling vouchers.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent by the tax authorities before the transport begins.
The service station operator is the owner of the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where the sale or delivery of PHMs is permitted, as a general rule, to the fuel tank, subject to a permit from the building authority.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators with a breakdown into: registered - normal sale or delivery of PHMs generally to vehicle fuel tanks; with a defined approach - operating generally in different business premises (e.g. quarries, sawmills, farm farms, transport organisations, construction yards), sales here are limited to the other party based on specific contractual relations; non-public - fuel outlets only for operators' own consumption.
A service station is not a construction or installation in the form of an operating tank located in service (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is only issued for own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to the tax authority's authorisation and are not registered.
Natural and juridical persons may purchase, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free circulation for resale on the authorisation of the tax authorities.
They must also be authorised when buying or obtaining liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption exceeding 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of operations. Tax control shall cover tax obligations, claims made by the taxpayer or other circumstances relevant to the correct determination and determination of the tax relating to a single tax proceeding.
Tax control can be carried out jointly for multiple tax procedures of a single tax entity.
Repeated tax inspections may only be carried out under the conditions laid down by law and on the grounds when the inspection is initiated.
Tax control is carried out within a tax-setting period of three years, with the deadline extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. filing additional tax proceedings, launching criminal proceedings in relation to the tax in question), or suspended (legal proceedings, international cooperation).
The period for determining the tax shall end not later than 10 years after the expiry of the period for making a proper tax claim.
There is no obligation on the tax authorities to carry out a tax audit on each taxpayer.
The commencement of the tax inspection suspends the deadlines for the possibility of the tax entity submitting a supplementary tax return or a supplementary statement (§ 141 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.) and restarts the deadline for determining the tax (§ 148 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
On the basis of its result, the tax may be levied ex officio.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) in which the tax administration searches for evidence and inspects premises, goods, documents, registers, means of transport and transport packaging at tax agencies and other persons involved in the tax administration, on the spot outside the premises of the tax administration (e.g. tax entity, point of sale, transport journey).
The tax authorities shall be entitled to borrow documents and items, to take samples and, where appropriate, to secure them.
On the basis of the outcome of the local investigation, the tax cannot be assessed separately, but the taxpayer can be invited to submit a supplementary tax return (§ 145(2) of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
Checking traffic data in EMCS is not a local investigation.
Ordering surveillance tapes to mark ethyl alcohol can only be made by the registered person required to mark ethyl alcohol to the tax authorities of the locally relevant place of marking, and is done through intelligent forms that are automatically imported into the application of the ethyl alcohol mark register.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the amount of control tapes ordered and orders the production.
He doesn't oversee the production of surveillance tapes.
Production is provided by the State Printing House of Cenin, a state-owned enterprise.
The customer of the check tapes shall take the check tapes to the tax authority of the locally relevant marking point.
Ordering tobacco stickers to mark cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco serves as a tax declaration.
The value of the tobacco sticker shall correspond to the amount of the tax liability, with the purchaser of the tobacco stickers being required to pay their value within 60 days of the date of their removal from the tax administration.
The customer is obliged to calculate in the order itself the value corresponding to the tax liability of the tobacco stickers ordered.
This time limit only applies if the value of the tobacco stickers is ensured.
The order for the tobacco stickers shall be made on a form established by the Ministry of Finance in writing or by means of a data container with the possibility of using intelligent forms.
Manufacture of tobacco stickers is provided by the State Printing Company, a state-owned company.
The trustee of the tax, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (Kutná Hora's territorial site), ensures the purchase and transport of the tobacco stickers to the tax authorities, who distribute them and further examine their transport, storage and use with customers.
Tax claims include regular tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco stickers, filed by tax entities.
Included is not the declaration of tax under customs procedure based on customs declarations and the declaration of claims for repayment of tax on: mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrol used in the course of business other than for the production of heat or the propulsion of engines, mineral oils used for primary agricultural production.
The fines imposed include an administrative procedure to deal with the infringements identified, a set of successive administrative actions. The International Exchange of Information on Tax Entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes the form of: a request for administrative cooperation, replies to a request for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, incident reports, inspection reports.
Transport taking place under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech customs office is the tax administration of the receiving or dispatching tax warehouse or the authorised consignee.
Performance indicators in SR
Permission and registration to operate in SR
The management of excise duties in SR is primarily ensured by the customs offices and the excise department of the Customs and Tax Division of the FŘ SR, whose procedure for the administration of excise duties is governed by the various laws on excise duties and the tax code.
These laws lay down not only the scope of authorisation for the CA and the FŘ SR to administer excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax subjects in relation to registration or payment of excise duty.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax entities (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, driven by an increase in tax warehouse permits issued, an increase in registrations of the authorised beneficiary for re-admission and the registration of a large number of user businesses.
The legislation clarified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils, as well as the notification requirement if they are transported in bulk or in packaging of more than 150 litres and 230 litres respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils that are subject to control and transport procedure to other goods, such as anti-knock motor products, oxidation inhibitors, bitumen inhibitors, viscosity enhancers, anti-corrosive products.
A mandatory indication regarding the indication of their kinematic viscosity has been introduced for lubricating oils.
An approximation of the registration process with selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the SR is provided in the following sections of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Under national SR legislation, when registering a tax warehouse operator in respect of all excise goods, a person wishing to operate a tax warehouse must also apply for registration and authorisation to operate a tax warehouse at the same time.
The resulting decision in the registration process is the certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty by which the tax warehouse operator acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA issues a tax warehouse permit authorising the tax warehouse operator in that tax warehouse to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under a duty suspension arrangement.
Where a tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in multiple locations, the tax authorities shall issue a separate tax warehouse permit for each tax warehouse.
The transport of excise goods under a duty suspension arrangement is monitored electronically by EMCS.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, the so-called
An ARC code under which said shipments can be monitored online and therefore in real time.
Where the tax warehouse operator is also the person authorised to distribute the ethyl alcohol, he shall notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the consumer packaging of the ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of the ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging of the ethyl alcohol and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free tax circulation, no later than the date of its release.
Registered sender
A registered consignor is a special type of taxpayer who cannot also be registered as a tax warehouse operator at the same time, even if he dispatches a subject of excise duty under a duty suspension arrangement after his release for free circulation.
Under national SR legislation, when registering a registered consignor in respect of all excise goods, a person wishing to dispatch an excise goods under a duty suspension arrangement after their release for free circulation must also apply to the CA at the same time for registration and authorisation to dispatch an excise object under that arrangement.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, while also issuing an authorisation to dispatch the excise object under the duty suspension arrangement after its release for free circulation.
Growing spirit
The basic act for the operation of growing brandy is to obtain authorisation for the production of alcohol at the distillery plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the permit itself from the Ministry does not entitle the holder of the licence to practice cultivation brandy.
In order to be able to practise cultivation brandy, a person must apply to the CA to register and issue a certificate of registration as a producer brandy operator.
The CA issues a registration certificate for the relevant excise duty, which also entitles the operator of the producer brandy to produce ethyl alcohol in the producer brandy.
The purpose of cultivation brandy is to provide services to growers.
Growing spirit cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislature allows a reduced rate of tax to be applied to ethyl alcohol produced in cultivation brandy, at 50% of the basic rate of tax, i.e. 540 €/hl a.
The reduced rate of tax shall be applied to ethyl alcohol produced in cropping spirit at a maximum quantity of 43 litres a. per grower and his household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year and therefore a reduced rate of tax can be applied to the ethyl alcohol produced more than once per calendar year, as the ethyl alcohol is produced in two production periods.
It is the production of ethyl alcohol outside the conditional exemption scheme, which in practice means that the ethyl alcohol produced is in free tax circulation.
The grower pays not only excise duty and value added tax to the grower's distillery for the ethyl alcohol produced, but also the price for the services provided.
The crop brandy issues the grower with a removal certificate, which serves not only as proof of the origin and method of obtaining the ethyl alcohol, but also as proof of payment of the excise duty.
Transportation of the ethyl alcohol thus produced is not subject to monitoring by the tax authorities.
Consumer Packaging Importer
National legislation allows persons intending to import consumer packs of ethyl alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country as part of a business and to place them in free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packs.
The importer of the consumer packaging does not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA issues him a certificate of registration as a importer of the consumer packaging.
That certificate authorises the importer to import consumer packs of spirit or consumer packs of cigarettes from the territory of a third country.
At the same time, he must lodge a tax guarantee on the amount of tax attributable to the quantity of ethyl alcohol or cigarettes he wishes to put into free circulation before the control marks are issued.
The importer of a consumer pack must release for free tax circulation only a consumer pack marked with a control mark.
For this reason, they must submit to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the surveillance marks exported to the territory of the third country.
On importation, the importer shall have the number of surveillance stamps imported back from the territory of a third country confirmed by the customs office of importation.
On importation of consumer packaging, the importer shall proceed in accordance with the customs legislation, where the amount of excise duty shall also form part of the customs debt.
In the event of the release for free circulation of the consumer package, the tax guarantee lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay a customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
Where the importer of a consumer pack of ethyl alcohol is also the person authorised to distribute ethyl alcohol, he shall notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the consumer pack of ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer pack of ethyl alcohol and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer pack which he puts into free tax circulation, no later than the date of its release.
Seller of consumer alcohol packaging in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of ethyl alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislature has introduced a new tax institute of the seller of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a permit for sale must apply to the CA for a permit and fulfil the legal conditions (business license for commercial activity; integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes; has not had its marketing authorisation withdrawn for ten years; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of those goods.
An invoice, for example, which also includes the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the consumer packaging of the ethyl alcohol.
The holder of the authorization shall keep a calendar month record for each establishment of the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received, the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging on the last day of the month and a record of the shortfall or surplus in the number of consumer packages of ethyl alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the authorisation shall be obliged to purchase the ethyl alcohol in the consumer pack or otherwise take it in the course of business only from the person authorised to distribute it.
Consumer Alcohol Packaging Distributor
In order to monitor the movement of ethyl alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislature has introduced a new tax institute, the distributor of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
A person intending to hold a distribution permit must apply to the CA for a distribution authorisation.
The applicant must fulfil the legal conditions (a business license for a business activity; a storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol of not less than €100 000 or paid-up capital of not less than €100 000; minimum number of 10 employees; has no arrears to customs; has no arrears on compulsory contributions; integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes; has not had its marketing authorisation revoked for ten years; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of those goods.
An invoice, for example, which also includes the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove the method of acquiring the consumer packaging of the spirit.
The holder of the distribution authorisation shall keep a calendar month record, for each establishment, of the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received, the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging on the last day of the month and a record of the shortfall or surplus in the number of consumer packages of ethyl alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the distribution authorisation is obliged to purchase the ethyl alcohol in the consumer package only from another person authorised to distribute it.
The person authorised to distribute shall report the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel Seller
A new type of tax entity, the fuel retailer, has been introduced to monitor fuel in free tax circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion.
There is no specific regulation governing petrol stations in the territory of SR.
That's why gas stations are incorporated as fuel retailers in the SR's national legislation.
A person wishing to sell petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation for final consumption in the course of business activity in the tax territory is required to apply to the CA for a sales permit before commencement of the sale and provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with an appropriate verified measuring device to measure the quantity of mineral oil when it receives and dispenses, and the tank must comply with the technical standards.
If the fuel retailer is a tax warehouse operator, authorised consignee or registered consignor, CA will also automatically issue a permit to sell fuel to registered persons.
A fuel retailer is required, among other legal obligations, to keep a register of petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold in a calendar month and also to notify the CA of a new fuel supplier (distributor).
A fuel retailer is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from the distributor of the fuel or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
However, when the propellant is delivered by means of an auto tanker, the distributor, when pumping the propellant to the dealer, prints out the so-called bottler from the measuring device incorporated in the car tank.
The document shall include, in addition to the quantity data, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the DMV.
An invoice, for example, which also includes the number of the distributor of the fuel allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
The tax authorities in the territory of SR, when exercising fiscal supervision over mineral oils, record tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Above all, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks when transporting, so hauliers use secondary roads, circumventing the toll collection system because of the more difficult monitoring of actual transports.
Transportation of mineral oils in converted double-bottomed tanks is also carried out.
Many times, illegal shipments are accompanied by a vehicle that carriers report possible mobile patrols to change the route and avoid roadside control.
Mixing of propellants with light fuel oils or waste oils also occurs.
Fuel distributor
A new type of tax entity, the distributor of the fuel, has been introduced to monitor fuel in free tax circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion.
A person intending to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in the free tax territory as part of a business activity shall, prior to commencing distribution, apply to the customs office for a distribution permit and provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with an appropriate verified measuring device, as well as a list of suppliers and purchasers.
A fuel distributor is required, among other legal obligations, to keep separate accounts for each establishment of petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold in a calendar month.
A fuel distributor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise source fuel only from the distributor of the fuel or from a registered person.
A fuel distributor can only sell in the tax territory to a distributor of fuel, to a registered person or to a consumer of fuel.
However, when the fuel is supplied via an auto tanker, the distributor will print out, when the fuel is pumped, a so-called bottler from a measuring device incorporated in the car tank to the seller of the fuel or to the consumer of the fuel.
The document shall include, in addition to the quantity data, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the DMV.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
An invoice, for example, which also includes the number of the distributor of the fuel or the registered person allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
Fuel Consumer
The fuel consumer has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation for his own consumption in the tax territory and stores that mineral oil in a storage facility of 15 000 litres or more shall notify the customs office at the latest before the first placing in the storage facility.
Fuel consumers shall be entered in the register by the customs office.
In addition to the legal facts, he is required to give the address of the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
The storage device must be verified and fitted with a measuring device enabling the amount of propellant (gauge, gauge bar) to be measured when receiving and dispensing.
The tank must meet technical standards.
The fuel consumer must purchase the fuel only from the distributor of the fuel or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for transportation.
However, when the propellant is delivered via an auto tanker, the distributor will print a so-called bottler from the measuring device incorporated in the auto tanker when the fuel is pumped to the consumer.
