That document shall include, in addition to the quantity data, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the DMV.
An invoice, for example, which also includes the number of the distributor of the fuel allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
The tax authorities in the territory of SR, when exercising fiscal supervision over mineral oils, record tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer in the course of business and meets the legal conditions.
Provided that the conditions laid down by law are met, a small independent brewery may apply a reduced rate of tax, i.e. €2,652 per hl/percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to up to 200,000 hl of beer.
As it is the production of beer outside the conditional exemption scheme, the accompanying document is not needed for transport as it is in free tax circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, they are small family-run businesses that also run restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own production of beer for sale.
Administrative tasks in SR
This sub-chapter approximates the exercise of excise tax administration tax supervision by selected tax entities within the meaning of the SR national legislation.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative tasks (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, driven by more EMCS traffic.
In contrast, the biggest decrease year-on-year was in 2014, by up to 4.3%, driven by fewer tax checks completed and fewer tax returns filed.
That decrease concerned legislative changes.
Tax controls
By exercising tax control, the CA ascertains or examines the facts crucial to the correct determination of the tax.
CA staff are shown, when carrying out a tax audit, by a mandate to carry out a tax audit which includes, inter alia, the purpose and subject matter of the audit and the extent of the tax years audited.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period can be one month, but also multiple tax years.
The scope of audited tax years is determined by CA.
Tax inspection begins with the writing of the tax inspection opening minutes.
CA will confirm receipt of the documents.
Borrowed documents shall be returned to the CA within 30 days of the completion of the tax inspection.
A CA employee from the tax audit draws up a report.
If the tax audit identifies a difference in the total that the audited tax entity should have paid, declared or claimed a refund of, the CA will also send the audited tax entity a call for comments on the findings in the report, together with the report.
The tax inspection shall cease on the date of receipt of the report.
The deadline for carrying out a tax audit shall not be more than one year from the date on which it is initiated.
Tax checks on registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once before the expiry date of the right to establish the tax, which is 5 years.
The FŘ SR issued an internal management act adjusting the abovementioned time limits because of the uniform procedure of the tax administration in the territory of the SR.
Local inquiries
Local inquiries are the activities of the tax authorities in which they seek evidence, examine and establish facts which are needed for tax administration purposes.
A CA employee will draw up a record of the local investigation and submit a copy to the tax entity.
When carrying out a local investigation, a CA employee has the right to unrestricted access to land, operational buildings, rooms and places including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The clearance of the quantities of ethyl alcohol produced shall be ascertained by means of a local investigation.
The facts established are the basis for the exercise of tax control.
Also in carrying out the local investigation, the CA is entitled to take samples as well as to safeguard the case.
The FŘ SR issued an internal management act regulating the exercise of tax supervision and local investigation for individual excise goods in order to unify the tax administration's procedures.
Permanent tax oversight in alcohol tax warehouses
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1.5.2004, there was also a change in the field of excise management.
The need for more efficient spending of state funds in administering excise duty on ethyl alcohol, improving the business environment in the area and introducing legislative instruments to more effectively curb the grey economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in relation to excise duty management.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the excise tax administration from the tax offices to the customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administration to be present in the alcohol tax warehouse.
In the territory of SR, national legislation defines exhaustively that it is only possible to receive, supply, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse in the presence of a CA employee.
This does not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or dispatches ethyl alcohol only in consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
At the same time, the CA is obliged to safeguard employees in the tax warehouse in order not to restrict the receipt, supply, production or processing of ethyl alcohol.
The tax warehouse operator incurs the obligation to safeguard working environment conditions for CA staff.
Under the contract concluded with the FŘ SR for the premises provided, the CA pays the tax warehouse operator the rental costs each month.
In a tax warehouse for the production, processing or storage of ethyl alcohol, the production facilities for the storage of ethyl alcohol must be such that the quantities of ethyl alcohol produced, processed ethyl alcohol, stored ethyl alcohol, including stocks of ethyl alcohol and the alcohol contained therein, can be determined at any time.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Where ethyl alcohol is not accepted, dispensed, produced or processed in a tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee, with the obligation to secure that area by sealing the customs office.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often because tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs office employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators make use of a legal option within the meaning of Act No 467/2002 on the production and marketing of alcohol, and use the production facilities for the production of alcohol at the distillery for cultivation burning and also for the purposes of the distillery for distillates, which must be a tax warehouse.
Around 250 customs officers provide permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
Issuing vouchers to collect alcohol control stamps
The basic procedure for collecting the control stamps is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration take-off number and the issue of a receipt for the alcohol control stamps.
Alcoholic beverage which is ethyl alcohol means goods of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength by volume exceeding 1,2 % vol.
The trademark is intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
A sealed consumer container filled with spirit intended for direct human consumption is regarded as a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Consumer packaging of Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be released for free tax circulation in the tax territory only if it is marked with a control mark.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee and the importer of the consumer packaging, who will place it in free tax circulation, may label the consumer packaging with a control mark.
The check mark shall contain, inter alia, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical character. The identification number contains the registration take-off number (1st to 6th for the numerical digit), the volume of ethyl alcohol (7th to 11th for the numerical digit) and the bulk concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer pack (12th to 14th for the numerical digit).
Original alcohol control mark pattern:
The registration take-off number shall be assigned separately by the CA to each purchaser.
Only a control mark, the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of the consumer package, the bulk concentration of the ethyl alcohol in the consumer package and the customer's control mark, may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of the ethyl alcohol.
National legislation towards the end of 2014 brought in the introduction of a new information system for check marks.
The aim of the new control mark information system was to simplify and computerise the ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of the control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee, the importer of the consumer package and the consignee (buyer) of the alcohol may label the consumer packaging with a control mark.
A trademark purchaser wishing to take control marks under the "new system" must apply electronically to the customs office for the stamps to be issued.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of the inspection marks is obliged to request their issue, to notify the data resulting from the SR national legislation and to keep a register of the inspection marks.
The number of consignments of the inspection stamps ordered may not be less than 500 or more.
Also, the tax authorities communicate with the purchasers of the surveillance stamps through an electronic system of surveillance stamps, in particular when notifying the number of control stamps which may be withdrawn by the purchaser of the control stamps or when determining the date of acceptance of the control stamps by the purchaser of the control stamps at the printing works.
The purchaser of the vignettes shall, before accepting the vignettes, deposit into the tax authority's account the funds corresponding to the price of the vignettes which he may withdraw, the quantity of which shall be notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the control mark takes into account the amount of the printer's refunds. However, it does not take into account the level of excise duty.
Control stamps are authorised to be printed by the state-owned Mincovna Kremnice.
The FŘ SR carries out tax supervision over the handling of the inspection marks and their disposal at the printing works.
The FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of a financial directorate employee in the printing works when handling the control marks.
The FŘ SR secures the sale of the control stamps to the purchaser of the control stamps at the printer.
Checkpoints can only be removed at the printer from an employee of the finance directorate.
Issuing vouchers for taking control marks for tobacco products
The collector of the control mark must request the CA to assign a registration sampling number and issue a receipt for the control mark.
A consumer pack of cigarettes can be put into free circulation only if it is marked with a control mark.
It is only possible to label the consumer pack of cigarettes with a control mark in a company that manufactures cigarettes.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee or the importer of tobacco products wishing to place tobacco products in free circulation in the tax territory can be a purchaser of the control stamps.
Only a control mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of cigarettes, the particulars of which correspond to the respective price of the cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the pack, the length of the cigarettes, the tax rate validity symbol and the registration take-off number.
Consumer packs of cigarettes can only be sold for final consumption at the price indicated on the control mark.
National legislation towards the end of 2014 brought in the introduction of a new information system for check marks.
The aim of the new control mark information system was to simplify and computerise the ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of the control marks intended for the marking of consumer packages of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A trademark purchaser wishing to take control marks under the "new system" must apply electronically to the customs office for the stamps to be issued.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of the inspection marks is obliged to request their issue, to notify the data resulting from the SR national legislation and to keep a register of the inspection marks.
Control stamps are authorised to be printed by the state-owned Mincovna Kremnice.
The FŘ SR carries out tax supervision over the handling of the inspection marks and their disposal at the printing works.
The FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of a financial directorate employee in the printing works when handling the control marks.
The FŘ SR secures the sale of the control stamps to the purchaser of the control stamps at the printer.
Checkpoints can only be removed at the printer from an employee of the finance directorate.
A tax warehouse operator or importer of tobacco products may mark consumer tobacco packages with a control mark.
A tax warehouse operator, importer of tobacco products or authorised consignee may mark a consumer pack of cigars or cigarillos with a control mark.
Only a control mark shall be used to indicate the consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos, the particulars of which correspond to the validity feature of the rate of excise duty.
It is only possible to label the consumer pack of cigarettes with a control mark in the business that manufactured them.
The number of consignments of the inspection stamps ordered may not be less than 500 or more.
The CA shall, within three working days at the latest, electronically notify the buyer of the inspection marks of the number of inspection marks it may withdraw, the price of the inspection marks and the account number of the FŘ SR.
The CA may reduce the number of inspection stamp units ordered if circumstances have arisen which make it reasonable to assume that tax infringements may occur.
The FŘ SR shall determine the date of acceptance of the surveillance stamps by the buyer of the surveillance stamps, but no later than 10 days.
The date of receipt of the inspection marks shall be notified by the FŘ SR to the buyer of the inspection marks via the electronic system of inspection marks.
Surveillance stamps are issued by the finance directorate exclusively in the printing works, but only after receipt of funds corresponding to their price to the relevant account specified in the electronic notification from the customs office.
The collector of the control marks shall be required to keep separate registers of the control marks in the electronic system of the control marks, broken down for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the ELO and SPD systems unit of the Excise Duties Division of the FŘ SR is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information upon request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the relevant financial administrations.
These include, in particular, requests to examine bodies within the excise administration, requests for information on excise administration, as well as requests to confirm information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications takes place electronically under EMCS.
The following actions are included in the administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (request for screening, request for information on excise management, request for confirmation of registration in the SEED); response to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; check report.
Comparison and Evaluation
Comparison
Authorisation and registration
In the Slovak Republic, permanent tax supervision is applied to tax warehouses for ethyl alcohol, in the Czech Republic this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administration through a tracking device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are tax warehouses, in the Slovak Republic they are only registered by the tax authorities.
In SR there is an institute of registered shipper which is included in tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In SR, it is possible to burn 43 l a with a reduced rate of excise duty on ethyl alcohol in case of cultivation burning.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of tax on ethyl alcohol can only be applied to 30 l a.
The growing spirit in SR must be authorised not only by the Slovak Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development, but also by the tax authorities.
In the Czech Republic, only the Ministry of Agriculture allows cultivation distilleries.
In SR, the importation of consumer packs of ethyl alcohol is carried out by the importer of consumer packs of ethyl alcohol in addition to the tax warehouse operator.
The importer's authorisation is subject to the applicant being registered with the excise duty manager.
In the Czech Republic, no special permission from the tax authorities is required to import a consumer pack of ethyl alcohol.
In SR, the sale of a consumer pack of ethyl alcohol is subject to the issue of a tax administration permit to the seller.
The seller of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep a register of, inter alia, purchases and sales.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administration does not issue any permit for final sellers of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of ethyl alcohol by the trade office; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In SR, the fuel retailer must have permission from the tax authorities to sell them.
The national legislation in the Slovak Republic does not provide for any special regulation of petrol stations, all activities relating to petrol stations are governed only by the Act on Excise Duty on Mineral Oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by a special law on fuel, but the tax administrator does not issue any permit for the sale of fuel.
Petrol stations are registered and a list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In SR, it is technically not possible to obtain a list of petrol stations from the financial management system.
In the SR, there has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities since 2012.
That increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits dropped significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of a bond for fuel distributors.
Administrative tasks
In the SR, substantive law provides for the obligation to exercise tax control on selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified in the internal management act issued by the FŘ SR for the purpose of applying the uniform procedure of tax administrations to the territory of the SR.
In the Czech Republic, the substantive law does not regulate the obligation to carry out a tax inspection, the procedural law only provides for the possibility of carrying out a check at the latest by the deadline for the tax assessment.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax checks carried out and the local investigations in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is that the internal management act of the FŘ SR stipulates in which cases and within what time limits the tax authorities must carry out a tax inspection, while in the Czech Republic the correctness of the declared amount of excise duty or its reimbursement is verified in particular by the local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative actions in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 due to the increase in the number of traffic in the EMCS system and at the same time due to the increase in the number of tax returns filed.
In the SR, the number of administrative tasks between 2012 and 2015 had a slightly increasing trend, which was influenced by the increasing number of traffic in the EMCS system while decreasing the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the numbers of comparable permits and the registration of taxable entities were reflected in the different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative actions of tax administrations was similar in the SR and the CR in the different years of the audited period.
In the Slovak Republic, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for about the same amount of administrative operations.
It can be concluded from this that the SR is more focused on carrying out administrative tasks by tax administrations, such as the exercise of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, the emphasis is more on remote surveillance, e.g. surveillance devices, immediate data transmission via the web interface and risk analysis.
Electronisation of administrative tasks
Electronization of administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax returns can be filed through a data container.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced so-called interactive tax return forms, but they can no longer be processed in an automated way.
In addition, the data must be entered into the personal tax account of the taxpayer.
The benefit is a reduction in the error rate of filed tax returns (DAPs), which saves the actions of the tax administration related to the correction procedure for erroneously filed DAPs.
DG is working on a new e-processing application for DAP.
Through intelligent forms, the following can be used: to submit tax applications or registration for activities and notifications of changes to data, to claim a refund, to fulfil reporting obligations for the handling of special mineral oils, the handling of raw tobacco and the fulfilment of biofuel obligations.
The handling of surveillance tapes is recorded by the tax subjects in the ORO WebClient information system, which is available for registration by the tax authorities of the specified data.
The transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the conditional exemption regime must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transportation of selected products in free tax circulation within the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, proof of excise duty exemption, decision of the customs office to place the selected products under a customs procedure, simplified accompanying document or other decision to levy excise duty.
The required data content is set by law.
To facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for the issuance of alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents sent via the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic web interface to a data warehouse where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
The ICU serves for control purposes by the customs authorities en route and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
For the largest operator of the fuel tax warehouse in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of PHM into free circulation, CS CR has online access to an electronic filing system, into which the entity automatically stores the tax documents issued.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for registering and monitoring the transport of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should make use of 70% of the existing EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for both declarants and customs officers.
It will also be linked to a system of global guarantees, a register of tax entities or a system of risk analysis.
The system should allow for an overview of transport in free circulation between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of documentary evidence without registration and the sharing of procedural numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure for registering the transport of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in the misuse of a simplified accompanying document, the repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronisation of administrative tasks in SR
In the management of excise duties, the SR tax administration uses electronic communication to monitor the movement of goods in the EMCS system under the conditional exemption regime, the control stamps, the submission of tax returns, as well as the registration and registration of tax subjects.
A one-way electronic communication between tax entities and the tax authorities was also introduced in 2014 and extended to two-way communication in 2016.
As part of electronic communications, a personal internet zone, known as an electronic personal mailbox, is made available to the taxpayer after the entry of the access data, which is intended for communication with the financial administration.
Within this zone, the taxpayer has access to an electronic registry through which he submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents relating to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication via a personal Internet zone does not apply to all tax entities.
National legislation defines tax entities that are required to communicate electronically with the tax administration.
They are mainly value added tax payers, tax advisers representing a tax entity and lawyers representing a tax entity.
The SAO also addressed the issue of the scope of electronisation of excise administration in the audit.
Only fully electronic acts were involved, namely tax returns and electronic communication within ELO.
Leaving aside the traffic carried out under EMCS, there has been an increase in the computerisation of selected comparable administrative tasks, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and Evaluation
Comparison
In SR, a fully electronised processing of the tax return is already in place, from its filing to the registration of the tax liability.
The electronic processing of the tax return is not set up in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, the possibility is set up for tax entities to insert on the web page mandatory documents for individual transports in free tax circulation.
In the future, the reporting of transport in free tax circulation in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system is being prepared.
Evaluation
The system of reporting traffic in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax surveillance, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid contrary to the legislation.
This can be recommended as good practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to the good practice in the Slovak Republic in the field of electronisation of tax returns, the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend completing the electronisation of the processing of tax returns in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organisational structure and staffing in the field of excise duties
The organisational arrangements of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic have undergone fundamental changes.
Organizational arrangement of Customs Administration
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic since 1.1.2013 consists of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
DG is the unit of account for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has performed comprehensive excise management since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
The Czech Republic also carries out:
(a) control:
ശശ in the field of road transport (weighing of lorries, payment of road user charges, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road haulage and in matters of international passenger transport),
ശശ waste and packaging material management,
ശശ safety of imported food,
ശശ in the areas of consumer protection and intellectual property
ശശ employing foreigners,
(b) customs administration - this is the comprehensive application of customs legislation, commercial policy measures and formalities for the import and export of goods,
(c) the collection and recovery of pecuniary obligations imposed by other public authorities in a divided administration;
(d) the activities of the police authority (authorised customs authorities) in proceedings concerning offences committed in breach of customs and related regulations and tax rules, where the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administration.
While the scope of the competences (concurrent control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are economies of scale, as the public administration does not have to spend on the status of the control group for each subject of the control separately.
At the same time, there is a reduction of the administrative burden on the persons checked by the re-check.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has, since 1.12.2016, exercised the powers to verify compliance with the obligations to register sales (Article 2(2) of Law No 112/2016 Coll., on the Record of Sales) and, from 1.1.2017, the supervision of compliance with the law and the conditions of operation of games of chance, including the imposition of penalties (Article 116 of Law No 186/2016 Coll., on games of chance).
Under the project Modernization of Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-tiered structure to two-tiered structure with effect from 1.1.2013, with the abolition of the middle article of management (customs directorates).
The DG spent around CZK 51 million on the project (i.e. around €2,031,000).
The Czech Republic's CS since 1.1.2013 has been made up of DGs and county customs offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competences are determined by law, excise administration is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial offices.
Territorial workplaces are the internal organisational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is empowered by decree to establish and abolish territorial sites and to determine their material scope.
The legislation does not provide for any competences for the territorial workplace; the territorial workplace exercises the competencies of the customs office on its behalf.
Organisational structure until 31.12.2012
Organisational structure since 1.1.2013
Management of excise duties until 31.12.2012 was carried out by DGs, eight DCs and 58 CA units (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 unions and units.
As of 1.01.2016, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the DGs and 51 departments in the CA and its territorial offices, as well as by eight departments in the legal department of the DGs and the CA departments providing mobile supervision, i.e. about 60 posts.
The costs of the CS CR most significantly affect wage expenditure.
There were no savings in personnel resources as a result of the reorganization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
The performance of the main processes is ensured by customs officers in service under the Law on the Service of Security Forces.
The possibility of reducing the numbers of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, since under the provisions of Section 42(1) of Act No 361/2003 Coll., on the service of members of the security forces, they can only be dismissed from the service in cases that are exhaustively defined.
Reduction of service posts due to organisational changes in the security corps is not a reason for dismissal, and the employer is obliged to ensure that members are assigned adequate service posts within the corps, or to secure service posts with another security corps (e.g. the Police of the Czech Republic, the Prison Service of the Czech Republic), or else to transfer them to the reserve for the temporarily non-attached, in which the members of the security corps are entitled by law to 80% of the average service income.

Organizational arrangement of excise management in SR
As part of the Programme Declaration for 2012 to 2016, the Government of the Slovak Republic has set as one of its priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS programme, which will safeguard additional budgetary resources by aligning tax collection, duties and levies and curbing tax evasion.
In this context, tax reform was implemented at the central level, resulting in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the SR and the Customs Directorate of the SR into the Financial Directorate of the SR and the creation of a financial administration.
The PŘ SR was set up on 1.1.2012 by Act No 333/2011 of the State Administration on Taxation, Charges and Customs, as amended, as a budgetary organisation which has its headquarters in Banska Bystrica and is linked to the State budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The FŘ SR, the CA and the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No 199/2004 Z. z., the Customs Act and amending and supplementing certain Acts, as amended, are customs authorities when they perform tasks under customs legislation.
Within the meaning of Act No 333/2011 of the State Administration in the field of Taxation, Charges and Customs, as amended, together with the Tax Offices, they form a financial administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competence Centre of Financial Operations, the Tax Offices, the Tax Offices Branch, the Tax Offices Contact Points, the Customs Offices Branch (CA Tax Branch, CA Branch Combined, CA Branch) and Customs Offices Station.
The main mission of the FŘ SR is the effective collection and management of taxes and duties, i.e. including excise duties, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the FŘ SR is the President of the Financial Administration, appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The president of the financial administration is responsible to him for the activities of the entire financial administration and therefore for those of the FŘ SR, which he manages and represents in its entirety.
Organisational structure of the FŘ SR since 1.1.2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in the territory of SR, excise duties management activities and processes are carried out by excise duties departments (9 departments) and legal departments (9 departments), in addition to customs offices (38 branches) and customs offices (18 stations).

Comparison and Evaluation
Comparison
Within the organisational structure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic, 74 organisational units, with a total of 1 300 employees, handled excise administration in 2015, in addition to the FŘ SR; almost 48,000 tax entities are managed by these departments.
Within the organisational structure In 2015, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic dealt with the management of excise duties by some 60 organisational units with a total of 1 011 employees, which manage some 114 000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of the various activities of excise administration is divided among several independent personnel services.
Their co-ordination and co-operation is addressed through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax inspection) in the field of excise management is divided between the excise department and the customs office branch, within the framework of which the same employees of the tax administration often deal with the said agenda.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, there is about a third of the number of tax entities on the total number of employees in the field of excise administration compared to the Czech Republic; the effect of a higher number of employees on the efficiency of excise administration is not clear.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the movement and monitoring of excisable products, the objective of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to make it possible to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty, and to carry out the prescribed checks.
When introducing the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to make use of these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of that EP and Council Decision allows the inclusion in the EMCS of national specifications, national databases forming part of the system and such technical or software as a Member State deems necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionality of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by a system of registration of selected products (EVV), which operated from May 2004 until the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1.4.2010 and is continuously complemented by European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
A so-called Customs Module and Declarant Module have been introduced in the Czech Republic.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
Beyond the Community scheme, in the Czech Republic, the EMCS system monitors shipments under the conditional exemption scheme both started and ended in the Czech Republic.
The system provides for the automatic upload of information to the Register of Tax Entities following the approval of the notice of receipt of the shipment intended for the authorised consignee for one-off receipt, with subsequent invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures the administration of both received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELOs, including sending replies with an attachment in any format and providing translations.
The report on manual export termination in ECS is also allowed to be accepted (only the referral of an automatically generated message is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS will not permit the approval of an e-AD or a notice of receipt without the response of the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The Declarant module is available free of charge for tax entities, in the form of a web application to which the user logs in with the username and password(s) assigned to him after registration with the CS CR.
Each operation against an EMCS customs module shall be accompanied by a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declarant module.
The Declaration Module allows tax entities to directly record data on commenced and terminated shipments under a conditional exemption scheme, so that tax entities do not have to spend money to acquire the scheme.
The declarant module's national functionalities allow data to be retrieved and stored off-line (saving time on frequently used data), filling in recipient data based on the SEED ID check and requiring mandatory completion of data that is optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for any consignment dispatched from the Czech Republic to be blocked in real time from securing an excise duty equivalent to the taxable transaction until the time the transport ends.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS.
Without a sufficient amount of collateral, the EMCS declarant module is not allowed to send the draft e-AD for approval to CA of dispatch.
Each warranty has a unique number and contains the transport ARC (including the amount of the blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The tax entity can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it sees the current amount of the blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantee.
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS
The development of the EMCS was realised on the basis of eight contracts with performance from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46,791,924.60 (or €1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the contracts concluded, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of £43,577,255.19 (or €1,640,401.10) excluding VAT between 2006 and the end of 2015.
During the audited period, expenditure amounting to CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. €547,438.99) was incurred for the EMCS upgrade.
The amount spent on EMCS upgrades during the audited period and converted to one transport entered into EMCS averages 16.49 CZK (or 0.62 €), excluding national transport, this expenditure in terms of one transport between the Czech Republic and EU Member States is 24.40 CZK (or 0.92 €).
The EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four performance contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, a total amount of technical assistance of CZK 7,499,675 (or €281,389.77) including value added tax was invoiced.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 per transport contributed to the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (or €0.23).
Both the development and technical support invoices related to the national solution and led to the development of the EVV application, which DG already operated before EMCS itself.
The invoices were paid in programme funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services as well as other applications provided by the supplier for Customs Administration of the CR.
EMCS v SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor movements of excise goods between Member States under a duty suspension arrangement.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document — SAD, which was used before the system was effective, thereby ensuring better control and management of traffic.
It has been in place in the SR since 1.4.2010 and has been continuously supplemented by requirements under EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, the so-called
An ARC code under which said traffic can be monitored online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS
The EMCS only ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods by those taxable entities authorised to use the EMCS, thus largely reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest development in functionalities came in 2011, when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS
The introduction of the EMCS has been implemented as an additional module of the SysNeD application equipment and therefore it is not possible to accurately determine on the Slovak side the cost of its initial application.
Comparison and Evaluation
Comparison
The aim of EMCS was to replace a system based on the administration of paper-based transport.
The benefits of EMCS are a comprehensive overview of intra-EU transport between Member States from the announcement of the start of transport to its end, with significant reductions in administrative costs for tax administrations and tax entities to process, transmit and archive documents.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, a national functionality has been introduced into the EMCS system allowing monitoring of traffic in a conditional system between two locations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic respectively.
In addition, automatic functionality of online monitoring and guarantee of excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
A national functionality is also introduced to monitor the riskiness of the taxpayer or transport, followed by a mandatory response from the tax authorities.
SR and the Czech Republic record a comparable number of intra-EU traffic in the EMCS system.
However, spending in SR on upgrading this system was €744,310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO SR only obtained the EMCS upgrade data from the FŘ SR for the period from 2011, although this system had been introduced and operated before.
Yet the expenditure incurred for the upgrade of the EMCS system in SR was €188,134.44 more than the expenditure for the introduction and upgrade of the EMCS system in about ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
During the audited period, the volume of expenditure related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in SR in terms of one shipment is 2.3 times higher than expenditure of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic met the objectives.
Both audit institutions have acquired a deeper knowledge of the excise management system in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in the two tax systems which affect the efficiency of excise administration.
Parallel checks have identified examples of good practice that could contribute to curbing tax fraud, which will grow in importance as tax rates rise.
Procedures reducing the cost of excise administration have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons if coordinated due diligence checks are not carried out at the tax administration.
In this, the role of the supreme audit institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel review of the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction Word
The Lima Declaration of 1977 stresses that the supreme audit institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled to the fullest extent possible.
The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers tax as one of the most significant components of public revenue.
The VIth EUROSAI Congress, held in Bonn in 2005, dealt with SAI audits of public revenues.
A major step towards optimising SAI control activity is the development of a specific strategy for auditing public revenue.
This is particularly relevant to taxes as the bulkiest source of public revenue, most vulnerable to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of another State's SAI.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in revenue for many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
The SAIs that carry out inspections in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation between themselves.
It was at the VIth EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea arose of carrying out a review of the administration of value added tax (VAT) and the VIES system within the framework of cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
Careful preparation ensued, with both parties first having to familiarise themselves with the legal environment and procedures for managing VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Analysis of this information led to a selection of control topics to be included in the control programme.
Achieving an efficient and efficient VAT administration has been a long-standing problem and individual states (in particular the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve the system, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We believe that the results of our scrutiny can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrations, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel controls on the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 - 2005 - 1215
Object of control:
(CZ) Value Added Tax Administration after the Czech Republic's accession to the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Target of control:
(CZ) The objective of the audit operation in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration of value added tax following the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (EU) linked to the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the exercise of the right to value added tax exemption for intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system for checking intra-Community value added tax, with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the aforementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
The system of exchange of information on value added tax The auditing actions were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as BRH) in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two auditing institutions on 8 June 2006.
Cooperation focused mainly on examining selected business transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (the Czech Republic) and the Federal Republic of Germany (the Federal Republic of Germany (the Federal Republic of Germany), using information obtained through international cooperation between tax administrations and comparing the VAT administration systems of the two countries.
The joint final report on the results of the control actions was prepared in the sense of the European Directive No 31 for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards.
The audited period covered the period from 1.5.2004 to 31.12.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The parallel control in the field of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and the German Republic was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
Beyond the main point - the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 - the control covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the control included the legal situation of international bus passenger services and a comparison of some statistical data.
Comparing the VAT management systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) Registration for VAT.
While in Germany, entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic, the primary criterion (among others) for registering is exceeding the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, taxpayers are given a tax number when registering for VAT, which only serves for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, it must request the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different ways of registering cause problems, conditions should be levelled out across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International bus passenger transport.
In the Czech Republic, international bus transport of persons is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport that takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2)
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic, taxpayers only submit VAT returns for individual tax years (month or quarter), in Germany, taxpayers are obliged to submit so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and must submit annual VAT returns after the end of the calendar year.
Unlike CR payers, payers in Germany are required to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to submit VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic, payers file summary reports at financial offices, in Germany, payers file summary reports at CLOs.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have the data from the recapitulative statements immediately after they are filed.
The information from the recapitulative statements is only available to the German tax authorities once they have been processed into CLOs.
Combating VAT fraud requires updated information on intra-Community transactions to be available as soon as possible.
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements would reduce the time lag between the transaction date and the update of the VIES data.
This in turn would allow for a timely examination of taxation in the purchaser's Member State (see 4.4).
Which would, but would require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submitting a recapitulative statement.
(5) International VAT Information Exchange.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for the information requests received.
The German CLO does not track the elapsed time.
As a result, the German tax authorities dealt with a significantly lower percentage of applications received within the time allowed.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent warning (see 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (RMS), which has its strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in every EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5).
In the framework of cooperation, the two SAIs examined selected cases of intra-Community transactions, carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and the CFN.
Together, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution or suspicions of VAT evasion were examined using the CLO legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained through international cooperation to calculate the taxpayer's VAT liability.
In those cases, the payers either improperly claimed exemption from VAT on the supply or failed to declare the acquisition of the goods on the VAT return.
In some cases, the financial authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used due to different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases have been identified where payers have erroneously reported business transactions in summary reports.
As a result, the data in VIES was incorrect and the tax administrations had to examine these cases (see 6).
Control Action Progress
Conduct of the audit operation in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and March 2007 by Division II - the revenue division of the state budget and territorial departments of Central Bohemia, northwest Bohemia, southern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were: the Ministry of Finance (hereinafter ‘MF’) and 10 tax offices – the Financial Office in Humpolci, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kadani, the Financial Office in Liberec, the Financial Office in Nymburk, the Financial Office in Otrokovice, the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 4 the Financial Office in Sokolova and the Financial Office in Thirti.

The inspection was part of the 2006 control plan and was therefore notified to the Federal Ministry in 2006.
After the testing phase, the review started in the fourth quarter of 2006.

4. Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
A taxpayer, under Act No 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter referred to as Act No 337/1992 Coll.), is a taxpayer, a taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person defined as a taxpayer by law.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421,865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
On 1.12.2005 there was an increase in the number of taxable entities registered for VAT to 457 590.
A taxable person who has his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds the amount of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months, becomes a taxable person from the 1st day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (Article 94(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; ("Law 235/2004 Coll.").
The person is required to submit an application for registration within 15 days of the end of the month in which he or she exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow a taxable person to be registered so-called retroactively in cases where the reason for registration is that the legal limit for registration has been exceeded.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable or VAT-exempt transactions with a right to deduct may become a taxable person, even if he does not exceed a turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575), if he fulfils any of the other conditions laid down in Act No 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not meet any of the conditions laid down by law can apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration procedure under Act No 337/1992 Coll. is initiated by the delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax authorities.
A voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate on his VAT registration application the date on which he applies to register as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator shall examine the data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed registration form with all annexes.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall invite the taxpayer to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
Once the tax authorities have verified that the taxpayer meets the conditions for registration, they issue a decision in the form of a certificate stating that the taxpayer is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (‘TIN’).
On the certificate, the tax authority shall indicate the effective date of registration for VAT and the periodicity of the tax year for VAT.
The tax period is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year has not reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year was CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax year is the calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year was CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax year and shall notify the tax authority of the change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the TIN in the registration certificate is always constitutive and the taxpayer is obliged to indicate it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax authority and in cases provided for by a specific law (e.g. Act No 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TIN contains the code ‘CZ’ and the tribal part, which consists of the general identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number or other general identifier, if provided for by a separate law, and for a legal person the identification number (provisions of Section 33(12) of Act No 337/1992 Coll.).
If the taxpayer has not complied with his registration requirement, even at the request of the tax authorities, the locally competent tax authorities shall register him of their own motion without delay.
The outcome of the registration procedure is the issue of the Ex officio Registration Certificate, which is delivered to the taxpayer.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has obtained a business license is assigned a TIN at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The same TIN is used by the tax entity even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
Pursuant to the wording of Act No 235/2004 Coll., which has been in force since 1.1.2005, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, the tax authorities may impose on the taxable person a refund of up to 10% of the aggregate income or income for taxable transactions which that person has wrongly carried out tax-free, for the period from the date on which he was legally required to be a registered payer until the date on which he became a registered payer by virtue of the tax authority's decision (Paragraph 98(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined is considered to be a tax payment (Article 98(3) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a penalty.
The deregistration of the VAT payer, subject to the conditions laid down by law, is possible for two reasons:
1.
Withdrawal of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover below the registration limit (§ 106(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer shall be entitled to apply for deregistration at the earliest after 1 year has elapsed from the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
2. Withdrawal of registration ‘ex officio’ (Article 106(7) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.), if: (a) the payer has not carried out the transactions for 12 consecutive months without notification of the reason to the tax authorities, (b) the payer fails to fulfil his obligations under Act No 235/2004 Coll., (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
(B) Payees who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who makes a transaction with a place of supply in the Czech Republic and is liable to declare and pay tax on that transaction pursuant to Section 108 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. (the so-called “non-established payer”) shall become liable on the date on which that transaction takes place.
This person is required to submit an application for registration to the Tax Office for Prague 1 no later than the date on which the transaction takes place.
It is required to indicate in its registration application all TIN allocated to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If a ‘non-resident’ payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Tax Office for Prague 1 registers it retroactively because, under Act No 235/2004 Coll., the taxpayer became liable for VAT on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
When registering retroactively, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires proof from tax entities that the transaction has been performed (invoices and explanatory letters, as appropriate).
If the "non-resident" taxpayer applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable transaction takes place, then the Tax Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the transaction will take place.
There were 473 "non-resident" payers registered at the Tax Office for Prague 1 on 31.12.2004, out of which 124 payers from the SRN, and 951 "non-resident" payers registered at 31.12.2005, out of which 233 payers from the SRN.
Pursuant to Paragraph 106(9) of Law No 235/2004 Coll., the tax authority is entitled to cancel the registration of a ‘non-resident’ payer on 31 January of the following calendar year, if that payer has not incurred any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
An audit by the SAO found that if a non-resident payer files a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the legal regulations at the deadline for filing a tax return, it is often not yet available to the tax office on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant to the possibility of de-registration are known to the Tax Office later than 31 January, it is no longer possible in the Czech Republic to de-register a non-established taxpayer for VAT in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in the SRN
In view of the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (Sections 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter ‘AO’), anyone carrying on a business activity is required to inform the city/municipal authority or the competent tax authority.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of business.
This information is processed by the City/Municipal Bureau for the Financial Conduct Authority.
If the Financial Conduct Authority identifies an enterprise that has commenced operations but has not registered, the Financial Conduct Authority may register that payer ex officio - and retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both resident and non-resident taxpayers in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria laid down in Paragraph 2 of the German VAT Law (UStG).
That obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover they realise.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in the SRN.
There are special finance offices for entrepreneurs permanently resident abroad.
For example, for those based in the Czech Republic, the competent Tax Office is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; A total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered as of 1 March 2006.
The BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As work permits for employees from the 10 new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have sought to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
Those undertakings do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs laid down in Paragraph 2 of the UStG because they are usually dependent on a single employer to determine their working hours and the way in which they carry out their work.
In order to be registered, an entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire from the relevant tax office, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form which is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by the special departments of the tax authorities or by general departments responsible for assessing taxpayers.
This form provides a risk assessment of each taxpayer before the IRS issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions follows certain rules:
The first three digits provide information on the relevant tax office, the following three (or four) provide information on the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are to distinguish payers, the last always being a check digit.
If a trader intends to engage in intra-Community trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive a tax-exempt intra-Community supply.
The CLO will assign a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in the SRN and if he has a VAT number.
The CLO assigns VAT IDs to entrepreneurs automatically when payers include intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns.
Structure VAT ID is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
The registration of an entrepreneur may be revoked: 1. at the request of the entrepreneur (for example, if he has ceased his business activities), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all business years), and 2. if the tax administration becomes aware that he is no longer engaged in business activities.
The validity of a VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of a VAT tax number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are required to inform the CLO of the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (§ 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not required to pay VAT in case 1. the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. in the following year is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000.
So-called small entrepreneurs (‘Kleinunternehmer’) are not entitled to invoice other entrepreneurs for VAT and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not liable to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small businessman may declare that he will not apply the provisions of Paragraph 19(1) of the UStG.
That return is binding on him for the next five years.
The trader can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
There is an option for non-residents to appoint tax representatives (section 22a UStG).
It is a prerequisite that they carry out exclusively exempt commercial transactions and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign businessman who thus does not have to register for VAT.
Information on representation for tax purposes must appear on invoices.
Comparison and Evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany, entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic, the primary criterion (among others) for registering is exceeding the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
If the taxpayer in the Czech Republic does not exceed the limit set, he has the option to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration process is standardized in the SRN, but differences may occur as a result of different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, a payer is assigned a TIN at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he also uses the same TIN in intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, the taxpayer is given a tax number when registering for VAT, which only serves for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, it must request the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH have found, Germany's two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other member states, such as the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration to intra-community transactions.
On the other hand, a two-tier system allows for retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax authority about their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax year, a particularly accurate estimate of VAT liability.
As different ways of registering cause problems, conditions should be levelled out across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (TIN).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate the TIN at the birth of a natural person.
This TIN will be valid for the lifetime of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax authority will request an economic TIN to be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of the VAT ID.
Work on implementing an IT resource to manage the TIN has not yet been completed.
International bus passenger services
Legislation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., with effect from 1 May 2004, the carriage of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct.
Such carriage is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by traders who are registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return service is considered to be a separate service.
Unless ‘non-established’ tax entities in the Czech Republic carry out other economic activities in addition to international bus passenger transport, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
The international carriage of persons was exempt from VAT in the Czech Republic on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V Cap. 5 paragraph 1 (b), which states:
‘For the purposes of Article 28(3)(a), the following definitions shall apply: The Czech Republic may continue to exempt international passenger transport under point 17 of Annex F to the Directive from value added tax until the condition set out in Article 28(4) of the Directive is met or the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier. "
Description of legislation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in Section 3b(1) of the German VAT Act, the place of supply of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) is the route (i.e. the place) where the transport takes place.
The German tax system therefore makes no distinction between domestic and international cross-border passenger traffic.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable supply of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also makes no distinction between tax residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident taxpayer transports passengers through the SRN, the part of the route that takes place in the SRN also constitutes a taxable supply of transportation.
The non-resident taxpayer must notify the competent tax office of his intention to provide passenger transport before performing his services in Germany.
The tax office registers this non-taxable person (cf. 4.1.2) and issues a special certificate for any bus or coach that is mentioned in the taxpayer's notice.
The taxpayer is required to declare his taxable supplies of transport on the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Financial Conduct Authority of Chemnitz-Süd had registered 741 Czech payers who were engaged in passenger transport.
Where passenger transport is provided to a taxpayer liable for VAT, the non-resident taxpayer does not have to pay the VAT himself to the tax office.
Instead, the entity liable to pay the VAT to the Tax Office and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident taxpayer is the resident taxpayer who is the recipient of the services; This process is known as reverse charge and complies with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
Apart from the notification of the non-resident taxpayer and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have several means of assessing the correctness of the taxable supplies of passenger transport declared.
The customs office's mobile control groups audit the certificates of buses licensed (licensed) for foreign transport that are used to carry passengers through the SRN.
After each audit, the mobile control groups send a check report to the competent tax office.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to claim VAT from the bus driver before continuing the onward journey.
A non-resident may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated on his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may announce its intention to carry out an audit, which must take place in the tax office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident taxpayer refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If there is to be a review of the VAT return or of the non-resident taxpayer's obligations, BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable supplies of passenger transport.
In particular, auditing the accounts of a non-resident taxpayer incurs disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration has to audit foreign accounting, which means not only a need for knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than a tax resident's audit, but this is limited to the provision of passenger transport that takes place in Germany.
