On the other hand, a non-resident taxpayer may not only accept the right to carry out a check, which is a matter for his national tax administration, but also the right to be audited by other Member States in which he is carrying passengers.
Moreover, in any Member State in which only one supply of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all the tax obligations imposed on him in those Member States, in all the languages and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger traffic therefore generates disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and Evaluation
The legal situation in the two countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the carriage of persons between individual EU Member States or between Member States and third countries is exempt from VAT with a right to deduct tax under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport that takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
When such carriage is first provided in Germany by a non-resident payer, he or she is required to give advance notice of the provision of carriage to the relevant tax office.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare taxable supplies of part of the carriage on the tax return in Germany.
Implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are in the passenger transport business.
Compared to the effort, the tax take, when realized, is rather low.
Member States collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive outcome.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs for charging VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport begins or where the provider is based.
Such taxation would require modification of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
Tax returns for VAT
Submission and processing of VAT tax returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is required to submit a VAT return on a form prescribed by the GIF within 25 days of the end of the tax year, even if he has not become liable for tax, unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is due by the deadline for filing the VAT return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the importation of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., in respect of which the tax liability is determined by the customs legislation.
If a refundable excess arises as a result of the excess deduction being assessed, the payer shall be refunded without request within 30 days of the excess deduction being assessed.
The time limit is not applied in cases where the tax administration initiates a tax procedure concerning the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with Paragraph 73(11) of Law No 235/2004 Coll., the right to deduct may be exercised on the regular VAT return at the latest for the last tax year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
At the end of that period, the right to deduct may be further exercised within three years of the end of the tax year in which the right to deduct may have been exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible by filing an additional VAT return.
The amendment to Act No 235/2004 Coll., in force since 1 January 2005, allows the submission of a supplementary VAT return only for the period in which the right to deduct could be exercised for the first time.
The payer is required to submit a supplementary VAT return if (a) the sum of the corrections increases the tax liability, (b) he makes a correction which does not alter the last known tax liability but only the data previously claimed by the taxpayer, (c) he makes a correction to the rate and amount of tax pursuant to Article 49 of Law No 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if the total of the corrections reduces the tax liability.
The taxpayer is required to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery.
Electronic VAT returns can be submitted either via the Internet or on a technical data medium.
Internet submissions can be made as submissions with a data message bearing an advanced electronic signature or as submissions with a data message not accompanied by an advanced electronic signature.
In the case of filing with a data message not accompanied by an advanced electronic signature, filing in writing, i.e. delivery of a computer report to the tax authority (e-form), is still required.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to intra-Community delivery/acquisition values.
Service acquisition values are reported on separate lines of the VAT return.
Some of the lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated check within the ADIS system.
The values of supplies of goods to other Member States to taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with the data provided in the summary reports filed by Czech payers.
Values of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with those obtained through VIES from the recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
The IRS is running a credibility test on VAT returns under the ADIS system.
This test is automatic, as without the test, VAT returns cannot be assessed.
The credibility test involves calculating credibility criteria and evaluating risky types of VAT returns.
Pursuant to Article 37(1) of Law No 337/1992 Coll., the tax office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply within the prescribed period with a non-pecuniary obligation arising under this or a special tax law or imposed by a decision under this law.
An automated tax information system used by the FCA to provide technical support for tax administration.
The audit of the SAO found that the tax authorities did not make use of the possibility to impose a fine on taxpayers for not submitting a VAT return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, a distinction is made between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit provisional VAT returns still have to submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not liable for VAT have to submit an annual tax return.
As a general rule, taxpayers are required to submit their quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which the VAT is incurred (Paragraph 18(2) of the UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the preceding calendar year, or if the business is newly created, the trader concerned is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
A taxpayer may also choose to submit a monthly VAT return if a refund has been made in the past year which has exceeded EUR 6 136 (Paragraph 18(2a) of the UStG).
VAT returns need not be made if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant VAT liability amount must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax year in which the VAT was incurred.
The tax refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FCA.
There are no deadlines (by law) for processing tax returns and refunding excess VAT.
In order to have the tax refunded in good time, it may be offered to secure the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and refund the tax quickly.
German VAT law provides for the possibility of extending that period (Paragraph 18(6) of the UStG).
Such an extension must be requested separately.
It allows a VAT return to be submitted and the relevant VAT tax liability to be paid a month later, provided that a special advance is paid on the monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the trader must submit a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the trader cannot correct the erroneous preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
A correction of the annual VAT return to or from the payer is possible during the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally only be corrected in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payees are required to submit their provisional VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid undue hardship.
Submission of the annual VAT return is possible on paper or via the Internet, with or without certification.
If it is made without certification, payers must submit the return once more on paper with their personal signatures.
If the payer fails to submit a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In the case of late filing, a penalty payment can be imposed on the payer (up to a maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
BRH found during a previous inspection that the IRS often failed to measure this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard penalty therefore fails to meet its objective of reducing the average delay, particularly when filing an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
Service acquisition values are reported on separate lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate tax return/VAT line.
In the case of VAT returns presented in paper form, a copy must be made either through a scanner or by the staff specifically authorised to do so.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically are immediately available to the Financial Conduct Authority.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, RMS staff will go through it and make a selection of cases that meet certain criteria.
Selected VAT returns must be checked by an IRS official on the basis of a control report prepared by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration has to make a rough estimate of the amount of VAT a taxpayer has to pay, the estimated tax has to be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and Evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers submit their VAT returns within 25 days of the end of the tax year.
The tax year is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month, depending on the amount of the payer's turnover.
In Germany, taxpayers file provisional VAT returns, depending on tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or month.
Payers are required to file an annual tax return by May 31 of the following year.
There are pros and cons to filing an annual VAT return:
+ on the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly provisional) tax returns by submitting a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the admitted intra-Community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period covered by the recapitulative statement;
– Federal states generally do not compare VIES data on intra-Community acquisitions of German payers before processing the annual VAT return.
In accordance with registration (see 4.1.3), German taxpayers are required to submit an annual VAT return, irrespective of the amount of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German tax authority to check the maximum turnover limit for small businesses.
In addition, the Tax Office responsible is able to compare annual VAT returns with direct tax returns and with final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax authorities are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from filed income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are required to submit VAT returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to submit tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to improving the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as ‘SH’) is filed under the provisions of Article 102 of Law No 235/2004 Coll. by a payer who has made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State.
The data on the value of the goods supplied are always given in Czech currency, broken down by individual tax entities, with their VAT IDs, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services rendered are not included in the SH.
SH shall be filed by payers with both monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days of the end of the quarter with the Tax Office, which shall have local jurisdiction.
The correction of erroneous data shall be made in the subsequent SH within 15 days of the date of detection of the errors.
Incorrect data in the SH is always replaced by data in the subsequent SH.
Like tax returns, payers can submit the BI in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not file SH or the subsequent SH and should have filed it pursuant to Act No 235/2004 Coll., the tax authority shall invite him to file it, while informing him of the consequences in the event of failure to file SH or the subsequent SH, namely that the tax authority is entitled under Section 37 of Act No 337/1992 Coll. to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2 000 000 (EUR 67 150) for non-monetary infringements.
The audit of the SAO found that the tax authorities did not make use of the possibility to impose a fine on payers for failing to comply with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of the filing of the SH, the tax entities are not sufficiently incentivised to fulfil their obligations, as the failure to file the SH does not affect the VAT liability.
The tax administrator is obliged under Section 102(5) of Act No 235/2004 Coll. to check the data in the SH, where appropriate in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and to use the data for determining the tax liability.
In the event of inconsistencies between the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payer with a monthly tax year) or relevant (payer with a quarterly tax year) VAT return, the tax authority should verify the accuracy of the declared tax liability as stated in the VAT return.
The tax entity removes erroneous data in the SH by filing a subsequent SH itself, or may be required to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the details of the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
– the payer fails to demonstrate the data in the SH (or subsequent SH), correcting it by submitting a subsequent SH,
– the tax authority has demonstrated that the information provided by the payer in the SH or subsequent SH is not true.
The tax administrator does not substitute the taxpayer's submission by inserting a correction without the submission of a subsequent SH, but merely modifies the information in the VIES database so that it is up to date, complete and accurate.
Data from the SH shall be sent to the relevant Member States.
They can only be sent and received by the national financial administration authority, designated to cooperate with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic, this function is performed by the Ministry, the International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (CLO).
O_MCTL is an automated message that the CLO receives from other Member States.
Contains all the bad VAT IDs listed in SH's sent lines.
If a bad VAT ID is used in one of the transmitted normal SH or subsequent SH lines, it is recorded in the table of the bad VAT IDs.
The table includes a so-called "Notice of Doubt to VAT ID."
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is required to declare VAT and enter the acquisition values on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of purchased goods declared by a Czech payer on his VAT return and in the value of the goods supplied, as reported by payers from other Member States in their SHs, are sent from the CLO to the tax office for examination.
Tax authorities have a duty to investigate irregularities.
Three situations can arise:
(a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant VAT return lines is lower than the value of the supply declared by the EU payers.
In this case, the tax authorities will check the accuracy of the data.
(b) The difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the EU data (the foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech taxpayer will itself submit an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administration to verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return despite this.
(c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States stated by the Czech taxpayer in the relevant lines of the VAT return is higher than the value of the goods supplied declared by the EU taxpayer.
Here again, it is at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the discrepancy and explaining the causes of its occurrence, the tax authority shall provide the result of the verification to ADIS.
The results of the screening are relayed back to the CLO.
Figure 1 (NB: MF) shows the number of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005.
Chart 1 above shows that the number of cases transmitted from the CLO to the tax authorities was decreasing for the quarters of 2005.
A significant decrease in numbers occurred in Q4 2005. The CLO has raised the minimum financial limit, including with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT return data and EU data does not always have to be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of the EU payers, or one resulting from the fact that in individual EU Member States certain types of transactions may be introduced into the SH in a different way.
The most common reasons for irregularities in the value of reported transactions found at audited financial offices are shown in Table 1.
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the SRN
Entrepreneurs who carry out intra-Community deliveries from the SRN to other EU Member States or engage in triangular transactions are required to submit an SH once every quarter specifying intra-Community deliveries by beneficiary (§ 18a(1) UStG).
SH must be administered by the 10th day of the month following the corresponding calendar quarter.
If an extension of this time limit is allowed in the case of provisional VAT returns, this also applies to the SH.
SH must be supplied by CLO.
They must be submitted electronically from 1 January 2007.
Exemptions may be allowed by the relevant tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realise that erroneous data are given in the SH, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that the taxpayers do not file with the SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to compel the submission of this report.
This procedure includes: – a first reminder – a second reminder linked to the threat of a fine/penalty payment, and – an assessment of the penalty payment.
Although the German tax code allows a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (§ 329 AO), the CLO assesses fines in three steps, amounting to EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a(1) No 5 of the UStG provides that payers are to act unlawfully if, intentionally or negligently, they fail to submit them properly to the SH, file them incomplete, fail to file them on time or, if they fail to repair or repair the SH late at all.
This offence can be punished with a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intra-Community deliveries cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office as the processing of SHs is the sole task of CLOs.
SH data is stored only in the CLO system.
The data from the SH are therefore only visually available to the Financial Conduct Authority after processing into CLO.
The deadlines for processing the SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Data from SH must be stored during the three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
If incorrect VAT IDs are provided in the SH of German payers, the CLO will receive O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
The CLO contacts a particular entrepreneur and asks them for the correct data.
If CLOs fail to obtain correct information, the case is referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
BRH found during the check that most entrepreneurs corrected the VAT ID at CLO's request.
However, the challenge, the threat and the assessment of three additional fines take up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within a month or two.
The IRS rejected exemptions for reported intra-Community deliveries in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the Financial Conduct Authority asked him to submit a corrected SH to the CLO, as the Financial Conduct Authority could not correct the VIES data on its own.
BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the submission of the corrected SH, so payers often did not comply with the request.
In view of the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, the comparison of the data on the supply of goods declared in the VAT return and in the SH will not take place before the submission of those data to the CLO of other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually used in the preparation of a VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed into CLOs.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then presented to the relevant Member States.
This data is used for the purpose of checking acquisitions by the tax authorities.
Once entered into the system, the CLO rechecks them based on a comparison with data from previous calendar quarters.
Where they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), audit information is generated and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is produced later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the assessment process will then cross-check these data with intra-Community acquisition data.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and Evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State shall submit the SH within 25 days of the end of the calendar quarter to the Tax Office, which has local jurisdiction.
The tax authorities process the SH and transfer the data to the CLO.
The values of the supply of goods to another Member State, declared by the payers in the SH, are compared at the tax offices with the values of the supply of goods to another Member State indicated by those payers in the VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used within the assessment procedure.
In SRN, payers who have made intra-Community deliveries are required to submit quarterly SH by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers have been filing CLOs, since 1.1.2007, in electronic form.
The tax authorities only have the information from SH after processing it into CLO.
Both CR and SRN payers report only the supply of goods in the SH, the supply of services is not mentioned in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are unable to correct erroneous lines filed by SH on their own.
As a result of this limited access to German VIES data, the erroneous VAT IDs were not corrected, even if the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FC.
The German tax administration does not compare the figures for intra-Community supplies given in the German taxpayer's VAT return and his SH.
Differences between the data of the two statements are usually not detected before the German CLO provides data from VIES to other Member States.
Given the BRH findings, it is clear that a comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
Data on supplies of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on acquisitions of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT returns.
Comparison is conducted by CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are referred to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in taxpayers' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax authority controls the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions of other payers only if the RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is destined for control anyway.
This approach relieves the tax authorities of the need to clarify the reasons for any difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
Tackling carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-Community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if payers administer the SH on a monthly basis.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, since most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file VAT returns on a monthly basis – and the SH does not require any additional information as opposed to a tax return.
To avoid bureaucratic costs, filing a SH may involve filing a VAT return.
However, an obligation to administer SH on a monthly basis would cause more time mismatches between the reporting of intra-community delivery and intra-community procurement and could increase the flow of data between CLOs.
The German federal government considered a general provision of monthly SHs in 2006.
Its implementation failed because of federal doubts.
These were concerned that the monthly submission of data from VIES to other Member States' CLOs could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly SH submission and monthly data transmission obligations were to be effective, a monthly update of VIES would require a European monthly SH standard.
Statistical data on delivery and acquisition of goods between Czech Republic and Germany
In foreign trade, the CFN represents the Czech Republic's most important trading partner.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions in goods made between the CR and the SRN are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous TIN or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL messages transmitted between the CR and the SRN for each quarter of the audited period.
These figures are set out in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLOs relate their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLOs relate their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
Level 3 international information exchange
Implementation of international information exchange in the Czech Republic
International exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States regarding intra-Community trade transactions and the payers who have carried out those transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92, distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information upon request shall take the form of so-called requests for information (RFIs), using the standardised SCAC forms.
Tax Administrators from the Czech Republic send their ZhOI or replies to received ZhOI through the financial directorates at the CLO, which provides for the translation of the information provided on the SCAC standardised forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The CLO also provides for the receipt of the YEI from other Member States and replies to the transmitted YEI, their translation into Czech and distribution to the locally competent tax authorities for processing.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 sets the maximum time limit for processing an RFID at 3 months from receipt of the application.
The SAO audits were carried out on all YES, transmitted during the audited period between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Of the 94 YEARS recruited in the Czech Republic from the SRN, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were processed within the three-month deadline, a further 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were processed after this deadline, and the remaining 1 were not sent to the SRN by the time of the SAO audit.
Figure 2 provides more detailed information on the deadlines by which replies to the RU received from the SRN were sent from the Czech Republic.
Of the 335 YEARS sent from the Czech Republic to the German Republic, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) were answered within the three-month deadline, another 179 (i.e. 53.4%) were answered after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) were not answered by the time of the SAO audit by the SRN (in the remaining 1 cases, it was not possible to determine when the SRN response was received from the transmitted data).
Figure 3 provides more detailed information on the deadlines by which the replies to YES sent to the SRN were received in the Czech Republic.
The percentage expression of the intra-Community transaction values reported in the GI transmitted between the CR and the SRN is included in Chart 4.
As can be seen from the chart above, the value of commercial transactions, examined through the RBI, was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
International exchange of information without prior request takes the form of either an automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or a spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax authorities from other Member States are often provided without prior request with information that may be relevant to them in administering VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at CLO.
The information shall be transmitted electronically between Member States.
‘Automatic exchange’, according to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange" then means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information about the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax authorities from the Report form for the delivery of the new means of transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the tax document issued.
When processing the aforementioned form, the tax administrator shall fill in the necessary data in a specially created template and forward it in turn to the liaison officer at the Financial Directorate where the data are collected and transmitted to the CLO for subsequent processing and transfer to other Member States within a specified time frame, i.e. not later than two months after the end of the quarter in which the information was available.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions that appear to be unauthorised and information on potential missing traders.
That information shall be sent to other Member States by spontaneous exchange using an SCAC form.
Conduct of international information exchange in Germany
In the SRN, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the local tax office.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form by email directly to the German CLO, which forwards the SCAC forms to the foreign CLO.
Financial authorities have been instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information audited by BRH were sent in order to ensure taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State, or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supply of goods or services referred to in the request for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
If there is no reasonable basis for such a request, the German CLO will reject any request containing an amount lower than that fixed limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
To answer a request for information, the CLO sends the request to the relevant IRS, pointing to a three-month deadline.
There are no further deadlines for processing requests at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor past deadlines, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to alert the tax authorities to the response to blank requests for information.
The tax authorities will obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or conducting an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit covering any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only cover one transaction that has been carried out recently.
This short and ﬂexible type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has proven its utility in investigating individual taxable transactions.
Under the automatic exchange without prior request, the SRN provides other Member States with information – on VAT IDs allocated to payers resident in other Member States, – on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, the SRN committed to provide other Member States with the following information through structured automatic exchange:
a. Supply of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without the use of their VAT ID; b. shipping or catalogue sales in other Member States not taxable in the SRN; c. significant differences between intra-Community acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States; d. intra-Community supply of goods not declared by the German payer in the SH because the supplies were treated as domestic transactions; e. potential "missing trader" who carried out their intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID; f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "missing traders" or to those VAT recipients.
Comparison and Evaluation
In both the CR and the SRN, local tax authorities initiate the submission of YEI or spontaneous information and send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech-English) and translates the information sent into English and German respectively, the German tax authorities follow the instruction that they should write ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German on the monolingual form.
The German CLO does not provide translation of German texts.
Examination of the RUs transmitted between 1.5.2004 and 31.12.2005 between the CR and the SRN found that the Czech tax administration had completed 74.5% of the applications received within the three-month time limit, while the RUs sent to the SRN were only processed by the German tax administration in 40.6% of the cases.
Although the German CLO alerts the tax authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not monitor the elapsed time limits.
The result of missing notifications is a large number of late replies to YES.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended a regular alert to CLOs.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO is now alerting the tax authorities to answer unfinished answers to the Yi.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at different organisational levels of the tax administration deal with VAT risk management.
Within the IFI, the following services deal with risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
VAT Methodology and Performance Unit and a report within it VAT risk management, which, among other things, manages the risk selection of possible tax evasion and assesses trends of such risks at both national and Community levels.
Coordinates the operation of the job nationwide The credibility of VAT tax returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-Community transactions.
Based on trade balance data, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, processes conceptually the management of VAT risks and cooperates with relevant EU institutions and other Member States in this field.
The International VAT Management Cooperation Unit, which inter alia ensures the exchange of VAT information, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses VIES data from other Member States, ensures public awareness and provides other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous TIN or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL messages transmitted between the CR and the SRN for each quarter of the audited period.
These figures are set out in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLOs relate their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLOs relate their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
Unit Tax Control and Search Methodologies, which inter alia performs risk analysis in the methodological management of tax controls and, in line with risk analysis, sets priorities for targeting tax controls in the plans of the Financial Directorates, processes risk analyses in the context of tax evasion reduction, including the collection of lessons learned from tax administration as well as from other sources, and proposes measures to curb tax evasion.
Search departments are set up in the finance directorates to carry out, inter alia, searches of tax entities and areas at risk of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceuticals), searches of unregistered tax entities in terms of the risks of tax evasion (e.g. internet services, job placement, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of the links of chain fraud and transmission of information to territorial financial authorities.
Specialised control units are set up at the selected 12 financial offices.
They have regional competence, tax controls outside the territorial competence of the tax authorities are carried out by delegation.
The need to set up a specialist tax inspection unit has arisen from the mounting findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which are mainly found in entities linked to the chains.
These departments focus on controlling tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities, and multinationals and tax entities with a large scale of activity in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms have been integrated into the ADIS system to limit VAT risks: – the role of the Trustworthiness of VAT returns, used to assess the riskiness of tax returns filed, – the role of the Selection of Tax Entities to Control, enabling the collection of taxpayer checks on the basis of the chosen criteria, – the role of the VIES, through which tax authorities have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The VIES role allows, among other things: – to check the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States, – to obtain from other Member States the values of goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in the SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, – to generate a report of payers who have not filed the SH, – to carry out a formal check of the data supplied by the CR payers in the SH before sending those data to other Member States, – to generate a report of payers where the data on the supply of goods to other Member States stated in the VAT returns do not tally with the VAT returns of Member States.
As part of their activity to reduce the risks of tax evasion, tax authorities have access to registers of government departments such as the Commercial Register, Land Register, Motor Vehicle Register, Business Register, etc.
For more detailed information, see Chapter 4.4.1 Reporting and Processing of Summary Reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in the SRN
Due to the federal (federal) structure of the SRN, the federal tax administration (in particular the CLO) and the tax administrations of 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At the CLO level, ST I 2 (‘KUSS’) collects audit findings on tax fraud in a special database called the OPUS.
KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has set up a new database called ZAUBER designed to transmit the names of companies of tax fraudsters as "missing traders."
KUSS coordinates related cases of domestic and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of KUSS is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other CLO and MF departments are entrusted with RMS-related duties and powers.
A formal check on the composition of other Member States' VAT IDs in the SH filed by German payers is introduced at CLO level.
This formal check is carried out before the SH data are provided to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Validation of the VAT IDs in the SH is done on the basis of O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the process of correcting invalid VAT ID, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS on the CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and produces several types of control reports based on several characteristics that typically feature in so-called carousel trading operations to identify potential missing traders.
The federal tax authorities are instructed to process these inspection reports and, in some cases, report on the results of their findings to the CLO.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if the existence of a tax fraud case (instead of an exclusive focus on the company's turnover) is to be presumed with sufficient probability.
BRH therefore proposed that MF take into account different characteristics when processing the reports.
The RMS should also sanction other facts, such as a taxpayer's payment behaviour (morality), industry (economic activity) or shareholder structure.
The second level of the RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the federal states and focused on the processing of VAT tax returns.
RMS, for example, generates a list of those payers who have reported intra-Community delivery in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the full submission of the SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-Community acquisitions, reported in the payer's annual VAT return, with VIES data.
The tax administrations of the federal states try to avoid comparing quarterly data because such comparisons would reveal too much disapproving data attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
- different execution times for an intra-community transaction in the view of the supplier on the one hand and the recipient on the other;
– Different accounting for sales discounts and sales events (incentives) and their different presentation on the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT returns and VIES, many federal states have introduced elements of RMS that are based on VAT return data and some other facts (such as company name structure, shareholder age, number of employees and payment behaviour/taxpayer morality).
Bavaria has introduced RMS based on rules that allow a team of tax fraud specialists (risk managers) to program their own rules for singling out potential tax fraud perpetrators.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
Accordingly, the competent tax authority will receive a recommendation made by the RMS before setting VAT.
Because this RMS is not able to reflect current findings in its operations, risk managers have to adjust the relevant rules based on financial authority feedback.
The Mecklenburg-West Pomerania administrative district programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with tax file data in which a check revealed tax evasion.
Based on this data, the RMS is able to identify the characteristics of the tax evasion.
The RMS produces a monthly list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities use this list as a basis for decisions on auditing proposed taxpayers.
Following the audit, auditors must report their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The North Rhine-Westphalia administrative district uses an adaptive artificial neural network that is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large number of data of VAT returns under consideration and some other facts, this neuron-fuzzy system or data-mining system calculates the likelihood that a particular taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential fraud offenders.
The local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers to check and report the findings of the check to the data processing centre.
The roll-out of one of the three RMS in the other Länder is ongoing.
As none of the three RMS is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful to tackle tax fraud.
It remains to be seen whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and Evaluation
Although the specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State developed its own RMS.
As well as the different approaches in the three federal states of the SRN, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
New trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud are currently being discussed by the tax authorities of EU Member States.
VAT fraud - particularly carousel fraud - is proving not to be a national problem, but rather a European one.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State, but in multiple states.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in every EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
A VAT loss caused by EU fraud may not hit the Member State of the initiator of the fraud.
Any Member State that is involved in fraudulent activities can be affected.
There should therefore be a European exchange and discussion of the RMS.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
In the framework of cooperation on the implementation of parallel control actions, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the CR and the FRG.
In addition, the two control institutions jointly examined the execution of several commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution or inconsistencies in the way in which the payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions on their VAT and VAT returns respectively.
The SAO examined a total of 8 cases involving business transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities at the request of BRH.
In 43 cases, the SAO checked the values of intra-Community transactions with the SRN reported by Czech payers in their tax returns and SH, based on the BRH warning.
BRH examined a total of 23 cases at the SAO's request, relating to business transactions carried out between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the CLO.
Examination of the selected cases found, among other things, that a different way of registering in the EU Member States leads to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer should have purchased EUR 60 500 worth of goods from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
Since the Czech taxpayer declared the acquisition of goods only worth the equivalent of EUR 29 869, the Czech tax authorities sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the goods supplied.
In a reply to the RU received from the SRN, the German side stated that in Q2 2004 a German payer delivered goods worth EUR 27 381 to a Czech payer, EUR 31 997 in Q3 and EUR 10 276 in Q4 2004.
The reply further showed that the VAT ID of the German payer had only been valid since 28.9.2004, but the German CLO retroactively issued a VAT ID certificate of validity from 1.5.2004 in 2006 following an additional request from the German payer for a VAT ID certificate of validity.
The German payer made a correction to the SH.
The Czech payer, on the basis of this information, was the acquirer of the goods.
The SAO's enquiry with the local tax administration in the Czech Republic revealed that the Czech taxpayer had submitted additional VAT returns for the various tax years of 2004, in which he had increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States while claiming the right to deduct VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, it was not possible for the Czech tax authorities to determine unequivocally from these additional VAT returns whether the values of supplies from the German supplier mentioned above were also included.
BRH discovered, as requested by the SAO, that a German supplier had been registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not request a VAT ID when registering, he was only assigned an identification number for transactions within the SRN.
Although it is not usually possible in Germany to assign a VAT ID to a payer retroactively, in this case a German tax official in 2006 assigned a VAT ID to the German payer referred to above retroactively as of 1 May 2004.
The German CLO assigns a VAT ID retroactively if the German entrepreneur did not cause the delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by a CLO after the payer's request for a VAT ID.
In this case, CLO allocates VAT IDs retroactively because the trader does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community supplies under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
Conversely, the German beneficiary does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier in order to report intra-Community acquisitions.
Because of these different procedures between the Member States, the German CLO assigned VAT IDs retroactively in this particular case.
2.
As part of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax authorities asked for the registration of a German taxpayer for VAT to be verified.
The VIES indicated the date of registration as 5.3.2005, with the date of 1.10.2004 on the registration certificate for the German payer issued by the competent German tax office.
In a reply received from the SRN, the German side stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1.10.2004, but the VAT ID was not provided to it in the SRN for organisational reasons until 16.2.2005.
The SAO's inquiry with the local tax administration found that the Czech tax administration had carried out a VAT check on the Czech taxpayer for the tax period from the third quarter of 2004 to the second quarter of 2005.
With this check, the tax office found that the Czech payer had included in the VAT return services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314), provided to the German payer before his VAT registration (i.e. before 1 October 2004).
For the tax year of Q3 2004, the tax office charged VAT to the taxpayer in the amount of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
BRH found out, as requested by the SAO, that the German payer was not assigned the VAT ID until 16.2.2005 when he informed the IRS of his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the filing of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer declared an intra-Community acquisition from the Czech Republic worth €160 (approx. £5,000).
3. The Czech payer declared a supply of goods worth 114 615 CZK (3 642 euro) to the German payer in the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for the third quarter of 2004.
The Czech tax authority, when verifying the registration of a German payer in the VIES system, found that his registration was valid from 11.11.2004, i.e. only after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to the SRN.
The Czech payer filed an additional DAP for VAT, in which he declared the taxable amount of the transactions effected within the country, worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) and the VAT of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692) which he had paid.
The SAO enquired at the local tax office in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer had subsequently submitted a request for a retrial in respect of the additional VAT return and provided as evidence confirmation by the German tax administration that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2000.
That is why the Czech tax authorities verified the validity of the German payer's registration in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The reply received from the German Government showed that the VAT ID was not allocated to the German payer until 11.11.2004, i.e. after the date on which the goods were delivered.
For this reason, the tax administration in the Czech Republic rejected the request for a retrial.
BRH found that this was not an intra-Community acquisition of goods because the German payer had obtained the VAT ID only on 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared the VAT on that acquisition by claiming a refund of input tax of the same amount.
However, as there would have been no changes in the value of the VAT payable by the German taxpayer, the tax authorities in Germany did not correct the figures in his VAT return.
BRH further found that the name of the German payer, given in the RGI, had been changed during the processing of the reply in the SRN, resulting in confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax authorities.
4.
In the framework of the international exchange of information, the German tax authorities verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech payer in the first quarter of 2005 for a value of EUR 22 686 from a German payer.
The SAO enquired the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that this administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, verifying that the delivery of the goods had taken place and that the Czech payer had accounted for and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not declare the acquisition of the goods on the VAT return because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the application of VIES, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intra-Community transactions only from 21.4.2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax authority asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the registration certificate for the German payer so that, if necessary, it could take steps to assess the tax.
The Czech Tax Office assessed the transaction in question as an acquisition of goods from a non-payer of the FRG and therefore did not charge the Czech payer the tax retrospectively on that transaction.
BRH found that, under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for an intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier only has to have the VAT ID of the customer from another Member State and be able to prove that the goods are transported to another Member State.
Under the German VAT law, it was therefore an intra-Community transaction and VAT should be assessed in the Czech Republic.
In any event, it is important that the Czech tax authorities noticed this transaction, as the delivery of the machine at that value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to respond to the YEI concerning intra-Community transactions of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased EUR 12 561 worth of goods from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
The Czech tax authority carried out a tax audit on the taxpayer for this tax year.
In the context of international administrative cooperation, he asked the German tax authorities, using the SCAC form, to verify the delivery of those goods.
The Czech payer denied acquiring the goods, claiming that he had never traded with the German company and that the acquisition of the goods was not accounted for in his accounts.
The German tax administration rejected the requirement to provide evidence – contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents, arguing that the turnover did not exceed the value of EUR 15 000 and no further explanatory reasoning was given.
Since the Czech tax authorities did not obtain evidence to assess the tax on the goods acquired, they ended the tax inspection without finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
BRH found, as requested by the SAO, that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (§ 22 a – e UStG).
The German payer declared these deliveries in his annual VAT return and in the SH.
He was granted the right to free delivery.
Based on the BRH's warning, the German tax office will send to the Czech Republic the supporting documents needed to assess the tax on the purchased goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in Chapter 4.6.1 of the reply to the JOI sent from the SRN to the Czech Republic, they exceeded the three-month deadline more often than the answers from the Czech Republic to the SRN: 6.
The SAO's audit found that the Czech tax administration sent a request for information to the SRN on 5.10.2005 regarding the verification of the value of the delivered goods for the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German payer declared a supply of goods to the Czech payer worth EUR 86 307 in the SH for this period, but the Czech payer declared in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only worth EUR 35 314 in the same period.
In its reply to the ŽOI, received in the Czech Republic on May 9, 2006, i.e. after the expiry of the deadline for processing laid down in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German side stated that the application could not be processed as the German firm's operations had ceased at the end of 2005.
By failing to comply with the deadline for processing the ŽOI, the German tax administration did not have the necessary documents for the tax procedure in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator applied through the SCAC form for verification of the delivery of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to a German payer, made in Q3 and Q4 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that there had been no response to YES from the SRN by the time of the inspection.
The SAO also found, by enquiry with the local tax authority, that the Czech taxpayer had not included in the VAT return the supply of new means of transport for the German taxpayer, worth CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375,472).
The Czech Tax Administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech Tax Entity filed the subsequent SH.
BRH found, as requested by the SAO, that for technical reasons the German CLO had not forwarded the above mentioned ZhOI to the local tax office for verification.
Following the BRH warning, a check was carried out at the German acquirer's office in Germany, which found that the acquisition of all cars had been properly taxed and that the cars in question had been sold to the next payer in Germany.
8. According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased a passenger car from the German payer in the 4th quarter of 2004 for a value of EUR 48 500.
The acquisition of these goods was not acknowledged by the Czech payer.
An enquiry with the local tax administration in the Czech Republic revealed that the Czech taxpayer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
The tax returns were not filed by the Czech taxpayer even after calls from the tax administration, so on 23 May 2005 the tax office charged him VAT of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
On 2.6.2005 CLO drew attention to the abovementioned supply from the German payer.
Since the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax authorities, the tax authorities sent the ŽOI to the SRN, concerning the aforementioned supplies.
Since the reply to the JOI was not delivered to the Czech Republic until 7.2.2007, it was not known until the end of the audit of the SAO how the Czech tax administration used the information obtained by the international exchange.
On 23 August 2005, the tax office revoked the VAT registration of the Czech taxpayer on account of his failure to comply with the VAT Act.
In some cases, only a partial reply was sent to the RU, as the audit carried out by the tax authorities on the payers was not completed at the time of the SAO and BRH audit:
9.
In 2005, the Czech tax authorities requested through the SCAC form a verification of the delivery of a car worth EUR 16 991 to a German payer, made in the third quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
In its reply to Zhoei, the German tax authorities stated that they had only an invoice issued by the Czech payer for a delivery of EUR 16 335.
BRH found, as requested by the SAO, that the audit carried out by the German tax office on the purchaser of the SRN had not yet been completed.
The German acquirer declared the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice, in tax returns for August and September 2004.
10. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator requested, through the SCAC form, an examination of the delivery of cars to a German payer worth EUR 198 167, made in Q4 2004 and QI 2005, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent a partial reply to the JOI to the Czech Republic in which it confirmed the acquisition of some cars by a German payer and further stated that the investigation into the SRN had not been completed.

The SAO found that several local investigations were carried out at the Czech contractor's premises by the local tax office in order to verify the use of excess VAT deductions, which did not identify any undue drawings.
BRH found that the German payer had declared in his VAT returns the acquisition of goods from other Member States for a total value of EUR 579 114 during that period and that the check carried out by the German tax office on the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
Chapter 4.4.1 describes the reasons for the differences between the intra-community acquisition values given by the recipient in the tax return and those given by the supplier in its SH.
The audited cases showed that the most common reasons for the differences were not the time lag or the misrepresentation of the value of intra-Community supplies of goods in the SH:
11.
In Q1 2005, according to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth €35,716 from the German payer, but the Czech payer did not acknowledge this acquisition.
Since the Czech taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax authorities and did not carry out any activities at the company's registered office, the Czech tax authorities requested, in the framework of an international exchange of information, to verify how the German taxpayer communicated with the Czech taxpayer.
The reply to the RU from the SRN showed that the German tax administration had established that the Czech taxpayer was unknown at the address communicated and that the goods had been taken over by the contracted carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only delivered goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false certificate of payment of EUR 155 153 in favour of the German payer.
After discovering fraudulent behaviour on the part of the Czech acquirer, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the delivered material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7 916.
The SAO enquired at the local tax office in the Czech Republic and found that, based on information obtained, the tax administrator had charged the Czech taxpayer VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States amounting to CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).
BRH confirmed, as requested by the SAO, that the German supplier had reported only EUR 7,916 worth of supplies to the Czech payer after repairs.
According to the German legal situation, the German payer reported the corrected values of the goods and a reduction in the taxable amount in the quarter in which the correction took place.
Thus, his SH contained the following delivery values in relation to the Czech payer:
12.
In the context of the international exchange of information, the German tax authorities requested through the SCAC form to verify the supply of goods and services made in the third quarter of 2005.
According to this ŽOI, the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth a total of EUR 396 126 to the German payer during this period and to provide services worth EUR 11 885.
The SAO found that a local investigation had been carried out by the Czech tax administration to verify this supply with the Czech payer.
In reply to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer supplied the German payer with a production line including assembly.
Individual parts of the production line were supplied by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic joined the EU, and after 1.5.2004 the line was assembled on the basis of an order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because it claimed to have defects.
In the third quarter of 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for the amounts of EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took the invoices issued but did not acknowledge them and did not pay them.
The SAO also discovered that all invoices are properly registered in the accounts of the Czech payer by enquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Only the amounts evidenced by the Czech payer and relating to invoicing after 1.5.2004 are shown in the VAT returns for the third quarter of 2005.
BRH found that, based on a reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax office in Germany concluded that the transaction in question was a supply of goods from a Czech payer to a German payer, including services for assembly.
In this particular case, the place of the so-called fulfilment of work is where the assembly of the production line took place.
Under German VAT law, the German recipient of the service supplied is liable to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient can claim a VAT deduction on the same amount.
As there would be no changes in the value of the VAT payable by the German taxpayer, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax office.
13. In February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth €58,000 from German payer C, according to VIES data.
The Czech tax authority sent a request to the FRG to verify this supply.
In reply to the Yi, the German side stated that this machine had already been delivered by German payer C to Czech payer B in 2004, but that this machine was to be returned to German payer C in October 2004.
According to the information of the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to the SRN, but was transported to the organization of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the reply to the request for information showed that the German payer C had sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organization of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Since the delivery was made only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-Community supply of goods.
The SAO enquired from the tax administration of the local payer B and found that according to VIES, German payer C delivered goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027 to Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004.
Payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the locally competent tax authority from the Czech Republic sent the RU to the FRG.
According to the response to that request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Further investigation with payer B found that the machine, worth EUR 88 027, was not in payer B's accounts, and that it could be a machine of the same type as that supplied by the organisation of German payer C to Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax administrator of the local tax payer A carried out a local investigation on this payer.
The tax authorities had at their disposal an invoice from German payer C dated 7.2.2005, which identified payer A as the purchaser of the machine.
The Czech Tax Administrator found that Payer A did not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payer A had a lease agreement with another Czech company where the subject of the lease was a machine of the same type.
The transfer of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9.2.2005, the transport of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax office to establish the tax liability of Payer A.
BRH found that German payer C did not deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was not therefore an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax authorities did not grant C, the German taxpayer, a VAT exemption and corrected the figures in his tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to Czech payer B.
Under German law, that supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that German payer C reported in its SH for QI 2005 the delivery of a machine worth EUR 58 000 to Czech payer A.
That supply was not verified during a tax audit carried out by the German tax office.

14.
The SAO's audit of the accepted ŽOI found that the Czech tax administration had received a request for information from the FRG on 4.10.2005, in which the German tax administration requested verification of an intra-Community supply from a German payer worth EUR 879 680 625 to a Czech payer.
According to the German tax authorities, there was a suspicion that this was a sham intra-Community supply of goods.
It was further stated in the RBI that the German payer had not engaged in any active commercial activity since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administration had carried out a local investigation on the Czech payer.
According to the observations of the manager of the Czech company, the aforementioned case appears to have involved a claim by the German taxpayer against the German tax authorities, which was claimed by the Czech taxpayer as a partner in a German company with the German tax authority.
According to information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administration has no information to date that the issue related to the Czech payer has been addressed by the German tax administration.
According to the available information, it was not a supply of goods, yet the value is still included in VIES as an intra-Community supply of goods to a Czech payer from the FRG.
The main reason for the following irregularities was that the beneficiaries did not report intra-Community acquisitions of goods in their tax returns (see also Chapter 4.4.1):
15. According to the VIES data, the German payer delivered goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the Czech payer in Q3 2004 to QI 2005. The Czech payer did not acknowledge this acquisition.

The Czech tax administration has requested verification of the supply of goods from the FRG as part of an international exchange of information.
In response to that request, the German tax authorities stated that the German payer had sent some of the goods to the address of the Czech payer, the remaining goods being collected by the Czech payer himself.
An inquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic revealed that even before receiving the reply to the ŽOI, the Czech payer had submitted additional VAT returns for the periods mentioned.
Despite this submission, the differences in acquisition values have not been resolved, so the Czech tax authorities recommended a tax audit of the Czech taxpayer.
The check has not yet been carried out.
16. The German payer delivered goods worth EUR 46 854 to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004 as reported in VIES.
The Czech payer only granted intra-Community acquisitions for the same period of EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax authority requested verification in the framework of the international exchange of information of the value of the supplies made.
The reply to the JOI, received from the SRN, was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total declared value of the delivery of the goods of EUR 31 999, i.e. a value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer and the VIES data.
The SAO's inquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic revealed that after receiving the reply from Germany, the Czech tax administrator contacted the Czech taxpayer's accountant and agreed with her to discuss the submission of a supplementary VAT return for the third quarter of 2004, after examining these invoices with the company owner.
No additional VAT return has yet been filed.
The Czech Tax Administrator told the SAO that it would proceed further to meet the deadlines for any additional VAT assessment for the relevant tax period.
17.
The German payer was due to deliver EUR 11,600 worth of goods to the Czech payer in Q4 2004.
In an international exchange of information, the German tax authorities asked for confirmation of whether the Czech payer actually existed, as the alleged partner of the German payer had set up more fictitious companies in the SRN.
When examining the business transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition to the tax office.
However, according to the Czech payer, the goods were not shipped from Germany to the Czech Republic and were resold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer submitted sales notes for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, neither declared nor paid the tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic nor in Germany.
All these facts suggested tax evasion within the territory of the FRG and were communicated by the Czech tax administration to the German tax administration in its reply to the GI.
The SAO's enquiry with the local tax administration in the Czech Republic revealed that the Czech taxpayer had submitted a supplementary VAT return for the fourth quarter of 2004, including the value of the acquisition of goods from, inter alia, the German taxpayer, while claiming the right to deduct tax on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
He did not enter VAT on the sale of goods in Germany on the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administration assessed the additional VAT return unchanged following a local investigation.
According to Czech legislation, that case did not involve the acquisition of goods from other Member States because the goods were not dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administration therefore made the wrong conclusion of the local investigation.
BRH found that the German tax authorities corrected the German taxpayer's tax return immediately after receiving a reply to the ŽOI in which it was stated that the goods had not left the FRG and demanded VAT from him in the amount of EUR 1 600.
In addition, the relevant tax authority has sent a notice to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of those goods is correctly taxed.
In the following cases, payers reported intra-community transactions that were unlikely to actually occur:
18.
The Czech tax authority received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from a German payer in February 2005.
Attached to the application was a copy of the Czech payer's VAT registration certificate.
In addition, a copy of the passport of the person who, as has been said, was to carry out the transfer of that car was attached.
An investigation by the Czech tax authorities found that this was a stolen passport, the person named therein had not imported any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax authorities.
