This information was included by the Czech tax authorities in their reply to the ZhOI, together with a statement that they could not confirm the acquisition of the goods – the car in question.
The SAO's inquiry with the local tax administration in the Czech Republic found that the Czech payer did not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register and the company's manager was uncontactable.
The Czech tax authority, following the complaint procedure for the February 2005 tax year, assessed the Czech taxpayer's tax liability at CZK 0.
Further investigation by the Czech tax authorities found that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity, which had bought it through an advertisement on the internet.
BRH found that the locally competent German tax authority, on the basis of the Czech answer to the ZhOI, would not recognise the German payer's entitlement to the VAT exemption for that supply.
19. During the inspection, the German tax office was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3 000 between the value of the goods acquired declared on the payer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was disclosed that the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth EUR 89 424 to the German payer during QIV 2004 to QI 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the VIES data, the German tax authorities requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The Czech tax administrator stated in his reply to the ŽOI that the only female manager of the Czech company had been removed from the Commercial Register on 8.7.2005 and the new manager had not been registered.
The German recipient of the goods appeared to be a relative of a Czech company partner.
The Czech payer filed tax returns for both VAT and SH, which were signed by an unauthorised person – that partner of the firm – after the agent was erased from the Commercial Register.
The Czech taxpayer's accountant confirmed to the tax authority that the company's partner had deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash receipts were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic, when questioned by the local tax office, found that the tax administrator had recognised the Czech payer's right to VAT exemption for the fourth quarter of 2004 on the delivery of goods to another Member State worth CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) and for the first quarter of 2005 of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548).
BRH found that the tax authorities in Germany had failed to correct the German acquirer's VAT return because a German judge had in the meantime confirmed the German payer's insolvency.
Since an earlier check revealed no evidence of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the tax liability assessed.
20. According to data in VIES, a German payer purchased goods worth €4,251,196 from the Czech Republic in 2005 after acquiring goods worth €43,274 the previous year.
In both the 2004 tax return and the 2005 tax return, the German payer did not report intra-Community acquisitions.
It also failed to report adequate supplies.
Due to these differences, the German Tax Office sent a YEI, covering Q4 2005 and Q1 2006.
The Czech supplier reported intra-Community deliveries of goods to a German payer in the SH for these two quarters, totalling CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6.9.2006, the ŽOI was received, in which the German side asked to verify that the intra-Community deliveries declared by the Czech payer had taken place.
In reply to this ŽOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the request of the German side could not be met because the Czech payer had no manager.
As is clear from the materials provided to the SAO by the competent tax authority, a report was drawn up with the Czech taxpayer's manager on the start of the VAT inspection for Q4 2004 and January to December 2005.
At the same time, the taxpayer was asked by the tax authorities to produce all accounting and tax documents for the aforementioned periods, but no documents were produced.
The sole agent of the Czech payer ceased to hold office on 16 May 2006, according to the Commercial Register, and the new director was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech taxpayer has stopped submitting VAT returns.
As part of the audit, the SAO, in cooperation with BRH, also examined several cases of intra-Community deliveries between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany, which were not the subject of a prior exchange of information between the tax administrations of the two countries.
Information on the cases reviewed was transmitted between the two supreme audit institutions through the CLOs of both countries.
21. A Czech company (eCR) which is not resident in Germany has informed the competent tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out taxable transactions in Germany.
Because of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005 but has not received the German VAT ID.
(ECR) has accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the delivery of these wind farms in the name, at risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of own capacity, the Czech company passed part of the order to a German payer (eD) based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relationships and mode of transport of wind farms:
According to the German legal situation, the location of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
– A Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent the wind farms to be assembled under his name, at his risk and his account in Austria.
Since the installation of that supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
– Since the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and on his own behalf, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started - in Germany.
Although the wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the beneficiary is a registered payer from another Member State, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) could not receive an exemption because the other Member State of destination differs from the other Member State of residence of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The delivery location of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of transportation.
The transport of some wind farms started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
– The delivery of those wind farms, which are produced in the Czech Republic, took place in the Czech Republic.
– Supply of other wind farms that are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intra-Community deliveries from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-Community deliveries from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not declare any intra-Community acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany or submit the SH to the German CLO.
So it's possible that the Czech company reported all intra-Community deliveries uniformly as intra-Community deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that the (eCR) did not report any intra-Community deliveries to Austria, but intra-Community deliveries to Denmark.
An examination of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), although this case shows no sign of tax fraud or evasion.
In addition, the SAO and BRH examined the transactions to highlight the differences between the reporting in the tax return and the VIES data, which were due to different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes to the legislation take time to implement the new legislation by both the payers and the tax authorities:
22. In the SH for Q4 II-IV 2004, the Czech payer reported intra-Community deliveries to the German payer for a total value of CZK 792 977 452 (EUR 25 197 885).
Over the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported intra-Community delivery to another German payer for a total value of 18,157,265 CZK (576,970 euro).
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above supplies in the SH in accordance with the text of Act No 235/2004 Coll., in force in 2004.
Further examination of the above transactions, the auditing group found that in 2004 there were differences between the CR and the FRG in the legal arrangements for the supply and purchase of electricity respectively.
Whereas in the Czech Republic the payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the applicable text of Act No 235/2004 Coll. as an intra-Community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legislation in force in 2004 it was not an intra-Community acquisition but a taxable transaction with a place of performance in the territory of the German Federal Republic.
The difference in statutory regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic with the adoption of Act No 635/2004 Coll. amending certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Administrative Fees Act, effective from 1.1.2005.
23. Furthermore, when examining selected intra-Community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was found that the Czech payer reported in the SH for Q1-4 2005 intra-Community deliveries to the German payer totalling CZK 240 411 163 (EUR 8 071 823) and another Czech payer reported in the SH for the same period intra-Community deliveries to the German payer totalling CZK 263 470 776 (EUR 8 846 050).
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Pursuant to the wording of Act No 235/2004 Coll., in force since 1.1.2005, in the case of the supply of electricity, the place of performance is the place where the customer has his registered office, place of business or has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have declared the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
By reporting intra-Community supply of electricity in SH, the two payers mentioned above distorted data in VIES by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation fulfilled the objectives of the BRH and the SAO.
Both SAIs have acquired a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that the VAT administration legislation differs.
Suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were identified during parallel controls.
Some of them make sense to check out afterwards.
Based on the audit findings, the two SAIs made recommendations on VAT administration.
The follow-up of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of the two audit institutions is the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT administration checks.
Communiqué
The report was written in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, the Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in checks on the management of excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introduction Word
The submitted joint report reports on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel controls carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky, aimed at the management of excise duties in the period after the accession of the two countries to the European Union.
The cooperation was carried out on the basis of a contract for cooperation in control activities, concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen in view of the fundamental change in the system for collecting excise duties which has taken place in the context of the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union since 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the European Union's internal market requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow goods not subject to tax to circulate until the day they are delivered for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation, adopted in both countries, allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under a conditional exemption scheme.
The system places great demands on tax administrations and foresees close interaction between the competent administrations of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation on controls of excise administration for the period 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Check Number: (Czech Republic) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of inspection: (Czech Republic) Excise Management (SR) Procedure of colné orgánov pri správe spotrebá tax
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO-CR) and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as the SAO of the Slovak Republic) concluded on 8 February 2006 the ‘Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activity’.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel checks ‘Administration of Excise Duties’, included in the SAO-CR's 2005 audit work plan under No 05/34, and ‘Control of the progress of colné orgánov in administering rebrebrebrebrebate taxes’, included in the SAO SR's 2006 audit work plan under No 48/11.
The parallel checks were in the nature of coordinated checks.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information that could not be obtained by the contracting parties when checking the management of excise duties on their national territory and producing a joint final report on the outcome of the checks within the meaning of the European implementing directives for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards - Directive No 31.
In the territory of the Czech Republic, control groups from the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of central Bohemia, southern Bohemia, western Bohemia, northwest Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia carried out inspections between 7 February and 2 June 2006.
27 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The persons audited were the Directorate General of Customs (DG) and 11 tax authorities.
Within the DG, 12 selected customs offices were audited out of a total of 54.
The audit in the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as ‘SR’) was carried out by the Finance and Tax Office of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the expositories of the SAO of Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 between 13 February and 2 June 2006.
Eight inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel controls was to examine the customs authorities' handling of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation has focused on the procedure of tax administrations in exercising supervision over the transport of excise goods, in particular on the registration of commenced and completed shipments under the conditional exemption regime, and on the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between excise tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
2. Excise management
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by financial authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken up by customs authorities, who have hitherto levied excise duty only on imports.
In the Czech Republic, mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The state budget's revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic totalled CZK 82.8 billion in 2004, and excise taxes accounted for 19.5% of the state budget's revenue from taxes and duties of CZK 424.7 billion.
In 2005, the State budget revenue from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the State budget revenue share from taxes and duties amounted to CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duty on mineral oils to the national budget was 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it was 90.9%.
The difference to 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the State Fund of Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the SR has been carried out by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duty on mineral oil, which they have administered since 1 January 2002.
Until then, excise duties were administered by the tax authorities.
Excise duty in the SR is levied on mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The State budget's revenue from excise duties in the Slovak Republic totalled EUR 43.4 billion in 2004 and accounted for 20.7% of total tax revenue of EUR 209.5 billion.
In 2005, the government budget revenue from excise duties was 50 billion units and the total tax revenue was 222.6 billion. The excise taxes accounted for 22.5%.
Graph 1 — Comparison of state budget revenue of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenue of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenue from excise taxes
- Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products (hereinafter referred to as 'Directive 92/12/EEC'), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as 'Regulation No 2073/2004'), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the movement of products subject to excise duty under excise duty exemption (hereinafter referred to as 'Regulation No 2719/92'), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649/92/EEC for movement of products subject to a simplified movement within a Member State.
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No 353/2003 Coll., on excise duties, as amended, (hereinafter referred to as Act No 353/2003 Coll.) in force from 1 January 2004.
In administering excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are bound, inter alia, by the following generally binding provisions: - Act No 98/2004 on the spot tax on mineral oil in the pollution of non-mineral predpissoffs (hereinafter referred to as “Act No 98/2004 Z. z.”); - Act No 104/2004 Z. z. z. o. on the spot tax on wine in the pollution of non-mineral predpissos (hereinafter referred to as “Act No 104/2004 Z. Z. z.”); - Act No 105/2004 Z. Z. on the spot tax on beer in the pre-spot tax (Act No 107).
2.1 Movement of excise goods under a duty suspension arrangement between Member States of the European Union
The conditions of movement of excise goods under a duty suspension arrangement are governed by Directive 92/12/EEC in Title III — Movement of goods Articles 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, the transport of those goods may be effected only by an authorised warehousekeeper, who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
A consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, but who may not store or re-dispatch such products under a suspension arrangement.
Authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic means a tax warehouse operator, economic operator is an authorised consignee for repeated or one-off acceptance of products subject to excise duty.
Under Directive 92/12/EEC, the movement of products subject to excise duty under a duty suspension arrangement is only possible with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be drawn up by the consignor in four copies before the transport begins, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require a further copy.
2.2 Procedure for the start and end of the transport of goods under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Transport from CR
The procedure for commencing transport is governed by Section 25, paragraph 3 of Act No 353/2003 Coll., which states, inter alia:
‘The tax warehouse operator shall, before commencing the transport of selected products, inform the customs office which is the local competent tax warehouse from which the transport is to commence;
transport of selected products may only commence with the approval of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent for the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax has been fulfilled ..."
The sender in the Czech Republic can start transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the local competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of the transport only if security of tax in the amount of tax attributable to the products transported is provided.
The consignor shall draw up an accompanying document in five copies before commencing transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document the consent to commence transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copy No 2, 3, and copy No 4 shall be handed over by the consignor to the haulier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorising transport.
Under Slovak law, the recipient keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document in SR. They shall confirm receipt of the products on copies 3 and 4 and shall submit both copies to the customs office responsible for them locally.
Copy No 3 certified by the customs office shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which he received the products.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
Transport is terminated by the acceptance of products by the beneficiary.
The release of the securing of the tax will be decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the start of the transport, within 5 working days after the presentation of copy No 3 of the accompanying document, which is certified by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Chart 2 — Circulation of the accompanying document for transport started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic
Transport from SR
The procedure for transporting alcohol and tobacco products from SR to another Member State of the European Union was modified until 31 December 2005 as follows:
Pursuant to Article 26(4) of Law 105/2004 Z.z.
‘Pri preprave liehu from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to a lawful beneficiary, alebo to a tax splnomocnencovi v inom členskom štáte je odosielatel’ (the deliverer’) the obligatory on the day before atia prepravy to send a kópiu of the first dielu sprievodného document electronically alebo faxom Colný úradu Poprad; tAttack kópiu is obligatory to send also colý úradu písomne to the piatich of the working days odo dňa beg a prepravy. "
Pursuant to Article 22(4) of Act No 106/2004 Z.z.
‘Pri preprave tabak productions from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to a lawful beneficiary, alebo tax splnomocnencovi v inom členskom štáte je odosielatel’ (the supplier) obligated in the present day to send a kópiu of the first dielu sprievodný Document electronically alebo faxom Colný úradu Poprad; tAttack kópiu is obligatory to send a colaj úradu písomne najor na piatich working days odo dňaňa bega prepravy. "
When transporting other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) between 1 May 2004 and 31 December 2005 (‘the period under scrutiny’), the taxpayer was under no obligation to notify the customs office Poprad or the competent customs office of the commencement of transport under a duty suspension arrangement.
It was only during a local investigation or a tax inspection that the tax authorities became aware of the transport of these products from the accompanying documents and the taxpayer's accounting documents.
The consignor in SR shall draw up the accompanying document in four copies before commencing transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, he shall send a copy of Copy No 1 electronically or by fax to the customs office Poprad and the competent customs office).
Copies Nos 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods being transported.
Under Czech law, the consignee in the Czech Republic keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document drawn up by the consignor in the Slovak Republic and acknowledges receipt of the products on copies No 3 and 4.
The certified copies No 3 and No 4 shall be sent at the latest on the first working day after the transport is completed to the local competent customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall retain copy No 4 and return copy No 3, on which it shall verify the accuracy and validity, to the consignee.
The consignee shall send the certified copy No 3 to the consignor in SR at the latest on the following working day after receipt.
Transport in SR shall be deemed to have ended on the day the products are taken over by the recipient.
Termination of the transport shall be proved by the consignor by production of copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and the tax authority in the Czech Republic.
Graph 3 — Circulation of the accompanying document in transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in SR and finished in CR
In 2006, amendments to all excise laws were progressively adopted in SR, under which the consignor of goods under a duty suspension arrangement is required to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the locally competent consignor before commencing transport.
The document proving the cessation of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products shall be Copy No 3 of the accompanying document, certified by the consignee and his competent tax authority.
The document proving the end of the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is Copy No 3, certified by the consignee.
The confirmation by the tax authorities of another Member State of the receipt of the said goods by the consignee shall be required where the latter is required under the legislation of the Member State concerned to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Registration of shipments initiated and terminated by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
There is no single electronic system in place to monitor the transport of goods under a duty suspension arrangement between the Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the implementation of an electronic system for the movement and monitoring of excisable products requires Member States and the European Commission to implement, from 1 July 2009, an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) enabling excise administrators in individual Member States to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently only used in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under the conditional exemption regime and to ensuring more effective control of the movement of untaxed products within all Member States.
This system will include national transport databases of individual Member States.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all traffic initiated and terminated on the territory of the Czech Republic in the Register of Selected Products (EVV) module.
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of shipments carried out only in the territory of the Czech Republic, tax authorities can obtain information about the start or end of transport immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in EVV.
The customs office shall release the securing of the tax on the goods conveyed by the consignor when the end of the transport is registered by the customs office to the locally competent consignee.
Customs offices in SR use a database based on the SysNed application software which provides automation of their excise management activities and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised beneficiary in the SysNed application software, that data is automatically transferred to the System for Exchange of Excise Data (SEED) database.
3. Preparation and conduct of cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO-Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO of the Slovak Republic, which discussed the concrete process of cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties, took place in January 2006.
The two sides have become acquainted with the excise legislation and the excise management organisation in both states.
Particular attention was paid to the procedure of the Customs Authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovak Republic in authorising and/or beginning and ending the movement of excise products under the duty suspension arrangement and the exchange of information between the excise administrations of the two countries.
At the meeting, it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak sides: - will process total data on the quantities of excise products shipped from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic and vice versa, the transport of which started during the audited period, - will compare data on the transport of mineral oils - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and ethyl alcohol - Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the conditional exemption scheme started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the periods examined were extended to the months of October and November 2005 and the transport of tobacco products under a duty suspension arrangement was also subject to an inspection during those months.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total amount of excise goods that were transported under the duty suspension arrangement between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the audited period.
4. Comparison of transport records of goods under conditional exemption
The SAO-CR provided the Slovak side with a database of transport operations completed in the Czech Republic, which included a total of 5 876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5 738 related to mineral oils, 134 to ethyl alcohol and 4 to tobacco products.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic forwarded to the Czech side a database of transport operations completed in the Slovak Republic, which included a total of 3 319 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 696 related to mineral oil, 2 066 to ethyl alcohol and 557 to tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared the data on the shipments listed in the register of initiated shipments in the Czech Republic with the data on terminated shipments registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are shown in Table 3.
The transport data for the months of November 2004 and September 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak Customs Administration, which the SAO handed over to him at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data allowing reliable reconciliation of individual traffic and therefore only 63% of traffic started were attributable.
Individual transports were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. sender, receiver, transport date, amount of products transported.
Data on shipments started in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic in the months of October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-Czech Republic with the database of the Slovak Customs Administration, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93% of the shipments started were unambiguously attributed.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the quantity of mineral oils was given in litres or tonnes, depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of alcohol was, in most cases, stated in litres, but this could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the database of that percentage of alcohol.
Quantities of tobacco products were given in pieces, in thousands of pieces and kilograms by type of tobacco products.
Shipments initiated in the Czech Republic whose termination could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database, or whose data on the quantity of products transported did not match, were checked with the accompanying documents.
Accompanying documents for 487 shipments of ethyl alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were inspected.
A check of these documents was carried out at the customs offices where the SAO-CR carried out the check.
For shipments authorised by other customs offices, accompanying documents were requested through DG C.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the realisation of 141 transport operations for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide the certified copies No 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products indicated on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products indicated in the database.
In addition, the Slovak side was transmitted traffic data registered in the Slovak database, which the transport database of the Czech customs administration did not contain.
The SAO SR searched the database of the Slovak Customs Service for 95 traffic.
Verification of the remaining 46 transport operations was requested by the competent customs offices locally, which proved their completion with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side copies of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which the transport was also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of the transport carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of the initiated transport.
The following cases were checked:
- the Slovak database of transport registered 11 shipments of ethyl alcohol in a total quantity of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 shipments of ethyl alcohol in a total quantity of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005.
The SAO-CR found that this was a transport of taxed products that the sender does not need the approval of the tax administration to start.
The dispatcher informed the tax authorities in writing of the start of the service. The transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under a duty suspension arrangement;
- A total of 94 mineral oil shipments, combined nomenclature code 2710 11 21, were registered in the Slovak transport database, in a total volume of 173,000 litres carried out by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005, the tax entity carried out the transport of 102,000 litres of untaxed mineral oils without the proper authorisation.
The taxpayer held a special licence to receive and use exempt products, under which tax-free products could be supplied only to the holder of the same licence.
He did not notify the initiation of the transport to the customs office in the Czech Republic and did not provide security of tax of CZK 1,207,680 on the products shipped.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the taxpayer shipped 71 000 litres of taxed mineral oils into SR. Even in those cases, he failed to comply with a legal obligation by failing to notify the customs office of the commencement of the transport operations.
Shipping of products put into free circulation on the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State may be initiated by the shipper in the Czech Republic without the approval of the customs office, but he is required to notify the customs office in writing before the transport begins.
A taxpayer who purchases products put into free circulation in another Member State is required to declare the quantity and secure the tax before they are collected.
Products may only be transported with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are governed by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also permits the use of an accompanying document for transport under a duty suspension arrangement, but on which it must be clearly indicated that it is a ‘simplified accompanying document for the purposes of fiscal control (products subject to excise duty)’.
The same rules governing the transport and admission of products placed in free circulation in another Member State apply in SR.
In those cases, the tax authorities transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under a conditional exemption scheme, the 3rd and 4th copies of which the beneficiary submitted to the SR tax authorities for verification.
Customs authorities in SR registered these services in the transport database under a conditional exemption scheme, as the accompanying documents did not indicate that they were a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the transport database of the Czech Customs Administration with the transport database of the Slovak Customs Administration and found:
- in the databases, the quantity of products transported was reported inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, hectolitres or kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported,
- the quantity of ethyl alcohol transported shown in the invoices did not tally with the quantity registered in the databases,
- not all related invoices were listed in the databases,
- two shipments of ethyl alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic made in November 2004 were registered in the Slovak customs database in a total volume of 47,237 litres of alcohol which were not in the Czech customs database.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between Czech Customs and Slovak Customs
Until 30 June 2005, Council Directive 77/799/EEC concerning mutual assistance by the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxation of insurance premiums governed the conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the management of excise duties.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004 entered into force, laying down rules and procedures enabling the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office to ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of excise administration and be responsible for exchanging information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, an ‘Excise Liaison Office’ (hereinafter referred to as the ‘ELO of the Czech Republic’) was set up in DG C to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union.
The security of tasks related to the management of systems to control the movement of goods subject to excise duties (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the SR was carried out with effect from 1 May 2004 by the ELO office of the customs office Poprad.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of the ELO office are carried out by the ELO (located in Poprada) of the Excise Duties Department of the Customs Directorate of SR (hereinafter referred to as ELO SR).
Under Article 3(3) of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible in particular for: - the exchange of data held in the SEED electronic register, - the Early Warning System Excise (EWSE), - requests for verification of movements of goods subject to excise duties sent to or received from other Member States by the Movement Verification System (MVS).
The content, scope and functions of the SEED, EWSE and ISA systems are governed by Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - system for exchanging information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national registers of excise payers and allows tax authorities in the territory of the European Union to ascertain whether products subject to excise duty are being traded by a person authorised to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States only for excise purposes.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union are able to obtain confirmation of the information held in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No 98/2004 Z. z., with Section 39 of Act No 104/2004 Z. z., with Section 46 of Act No 105/2004 Z. z., with Section 40 of Act No 106/2004 Z. z and with Section 39 of Act No 107/2004 Z. z ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, beneficiaries and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or beneficiary in the SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data is automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place generally once a month during the audited period, exceptionally several times a month.
SR Customs received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data to the SEED database in the Czech Republic are transmitted from a national register in which all persons authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorisations to dispose of such products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Customs requests for information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through the ELO CR.
EWSE - An early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods, through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
Transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by the European Commission regulation is considered to be a risky consignment and transport is assessed as a risky consignment by the tax authorities.
The exchange of information is carried out in two forms:
- information - to be sent when the limits laid down are exceeded,
- a warning message - is sent when the transport of goods is assessed as being at risk.
When assessing the risk level of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database for sending a warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
In the event that the data in the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the residence of the consignee does not match), ELO SR shall draw up a warning message to be sent to the ELO of the Member State of the consignee of the goods.
ELO's reporting is governed by the Tax and Customs Commission Regulations CED 317 and CED 457, which, among other things, determine the type and quantity of goods in the respective units of measurement for information and warning reports.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent one warning message.
In the Czech Republic, information on shipments of products initiated in excess of the limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving the transport.
If, on the basis of its own analysis, the tax authorities in the Czech Republic assess the consignment as a risk, they will process a so-called warning message, which they will send to the relevant Member State via the ELO CR.
In 2005, ELO ČR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The ISA - the system for controlling the movement of goods - allows, through applications, the ISA to control the individual transport of excisable products as well as the control of the specified transport route between the entities mentioned in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information is based on a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is mainly used in cases where the consignor takes a certified copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requests e.g. reimbursement of excise duty, and in cases where the data contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent 33 applications to ISAs.
ELO ČR sent 25 applications to ELO SR to MVS.
Customs authorities in the Czech Republic most often checked the information contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantity of products received and/or dispatched, or whether the consignor of products mentioned in the accompanying document was authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty, if this could not be verified in the international SEED database.
Received ISA applications in both countries were forwarded to customs offices locally responsible for the consignee or consignor of excisable products.
The customs authorities checked the required data and notified the outcome of the investigation to the other member country via ELO.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the SAO-Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic made it possible to compare the basic legislation governing the field of excise duties in the two states, the procedure of the Customs Authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the opening and closing of the transport of products under the conditional exemption regime between the two states, the registration of these traffic, and to further compare the exchange of information between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Comparing the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, differences were found:
(a) the procedure followed by the tax authorities and the tax authorities in commencing the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme.
The transport of products under the conditional exemption regime can only be initiated by a tax entity in the Czech Republic with the approval of the tax administration, which authorises the commencement of the transport on condition that the transported products have been provided with a tax guarantee equal to the tax attributable to them.
The commencement of the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme in SR is not subject to the authorisation of the tax authorities.
During the audited period, the taxpayer was required to notify the tax authorities of the start of the transport of ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
He could start the transport of mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax authorities.
In 2006, amendments to all excise laws were progressively adopted in SR, under which the consignor of goods under a duty suspension arrangement is required to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of local authority of the consignor before commencing transport;
(b) within the time limits for dispatching copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copies No 3 and No 4 of the accompanying document to the tax authority for verification at the latest on the following working day after the transport is completed.
The certified copy No 3 shall be sent to the consignor at the latest on the following working day following receipt from the tax authorities.
The recipient in SR is required to send to the consignor of the products copy No 3 certified by the tax authorities and the consignee of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both SR and the Czech Republic keep an electronic register of shipments of products under the conditional exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping such records are not regulated by law in the Czech Republic or the Slovak Republic.
Customs authorities in both countries record all the data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
There is currently no single electronic system for monitoring the transport of goods under a duty suspension arrangement between the Member States of the European Union, allowing excise duty managers in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
Under Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, the introduction of an electronic system to monitor the movement of excisable products is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of the agreement on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme started in SR and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The database included 5,876 items relating to transported mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side handed over to the Czech side a database of the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in SR.
The database included 3,319 items relating to transported mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data for shipments listed in the register of shipments initiated in the Czech Republic with the record of shipments terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared data on the transport of goods under the conditional exemption regime initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
Data reconciliation was hampered by the fact that the quantities of goods being shipped were not uniformly reported in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly attribute data on individual traffic in the two registers, an examination of the accompanying documents was carried out and neither breaches of the conditional exemption scheme nor cases of tax evasion were found.
On the basis of the findings of the parallel controls, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the traffic register to improve the management of excise duties.
The setting up of an electronic system for the movement and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow for the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movements under suspension of excise duty within the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the President of the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic.
Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on follow-up results
Introduction Word
Taxes in general are a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus their attention on this area.
Value added tax (VAT) fraud is an example.
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated each year in the European Union (EU).
As early as 2005, attendees of the VIth EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also referred to as the SAO) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, hereinafter also referred to as BRH) carried out the first parallel VAT control action in 2006.
The report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not limited to a single country, but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between the SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive assessment of the steps being taken to address the problem.
The two SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a follow-up parallel check.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up)
Target of control:
(CZ) The objective of the audit operation was to examine the VAT administration procedure of the tax authorities, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of the two countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The audit action was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
It was also intended to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended to compare with established good practice (if any).
The audited period was the years 2006 to 2008 and, where relevant, the period before and after, until the end of the auditing period.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
A follow-up inspection of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
Suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions have been identified during previous parallel checks.
Some of them required further screening.
Based on the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations on VAT administration.
The follow-up was carried out to evaluate the actions taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspected cases.
The audit further focused on e.g. selected cases of high-risk intra-Community transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of claims and the carrying out of VAT checks on large tax entities.
When reviewing the VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors made the following control findings:
1. Recommendations from previous check
• Recommendation 1: Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
In previous parallel controls, a comparison of VAT registration systems in the two countries identified differences.
As different ways of registering cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registering payers within the EU.
This recommendation has been made at EU level.
The proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter referred to as "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the database of VAT payers' tax identification numbers.
He also amended the common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
The SAIs expected EU Member States to agree on adequate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of that document, agreed by the EU Member States under ECOFIN, no longer contains the issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to regard this intention as a relevant prevention tool in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU states introduce a monthly reporting period to allow for more timely examination of intra-Community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the reporting period for recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to file recapitulative statements on a monthly basis was not introduced by the deadline in accordance with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany with a view to making VIES data more reliable and considering linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of the fraudulent activity will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit found that our two Member States use different risk management systems, which have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO audited EUROCANET, which allows information exchange within the EU, while BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected intra-Community transaction cases
During the previous audit operation, business transactions were jointly examined where there were doubts about their execution or irregularities in the reporting of business transactions on tax returns or recapitulative statements by tax payers from both countries.
The two SAIs selected for follow-up nine cases involving intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The checks carried out by the tax authorities of the respective countries have not been completed by the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
A follow-up action verified that most of the tax proceedings in relation to the specified selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany had been concluded and that adequate measures had been taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT assessments or avoidance of input tax refunds).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-Community transactions by EU payers enrolled in EUROCANET were selected for the check.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risky taxpayers within the EU.
The participation of Member States in this scheme is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant in the scheme if some Member States refuse active participation.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration was not involved in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, no information could be obtained on which suppliers with German VAT IDs were assessed as being at risk.
In the framework of the audit operation, the SAO found both cases of normal commercial transactions and cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent VAT activities.
Tax authorities have limited means of controlling risky transactions, particularly when it comes to missing traders, and mere physical examination of documents can make it difficult to prove any fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer.
A similar situation for tax administrations arises when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel shops.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater co-operation between customs and financial authorities to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation, as well as to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively participate in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other instruments are being used to detect at-risk taxpayers, which have so far proved successful for the German tax administration.
In this area, there is a need to communicate and exchange experiences between EU Member States.
The EU Council has reached a political consensus on the proposal for a Regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in using EUROCANET should underpin the creation of this new network to fight VAT fraud.
4. Mutual assistance for recovery of claims
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which applications for international recovery assistance are handled is identical in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs find it useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAIs agree that reliable statistics should include more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to produce an analysis, based on more detailed statistics, to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In both SAIs' view, this means helping Member States with low recovery rates to be able to raise recovery rates to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in the process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAIs analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control of large tax entities (VDS) in both countries.
In addition, they gathered information from tax administrations in the form of a questionnaire on areas that SAIs consider essential for the management of this issue.
The responses received clearly show that the situation in the two countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system in place to guide the selection of risk-prone cases, relying on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax checks carried out, balance sheet data and profit and loss accounts, etc.).
This ensures the effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
The establishment of a dedicated financial office for the management of VDS is planned in 2012.
In Germany, a similar system does not yet exist, making it difficult to manage and analyse VAT controls in general.
Germany has so far concentrated more on selecting the individual cases in question, mainly on the basis of data from the VAT return and recapitulative statement.
The analysis of this data relies on various risk management components which will be strengthened.
3. Control Action Progress
3.1 Czech Republic Follow-up
The audit was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by Division II - the revenue department of the state budget and territorial departments IX. Plzeň, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited persons were: the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also referred to as the Czech Ministry of Finance) and 25 financial offices (hereinafter also referred to as the ‘FIU’): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ Brno in Břeclav, FÚ BrÚ Vary, FÚ VÚ in Domestic, FÚ BrÚFÚ FÚFÚFÚ in PraÚFÚFÚ KrÚFÚFÚ, FÚ ÚFÚFÚFÚ I and FÚFÚFÚFÚFÚ FÚ I8, FÚ
The audit conclusion from this audit action was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Conduct of the inspection operation in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Indirect Taxation Control Unit and the personnel of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of a sample of cases, a number of Länder were notified of the mission of the inspection operation.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, a control event took place in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hessen, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Tax Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-sever), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, discussions took place with the fiscal authorities of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-jih) and the finance directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on the inspection findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
In preparation for the parallel audit events, a meeting of representatives of the two audit institutions was held in September 2008 to discuss and identify topics of control.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the leaders of the two SAIs signed an agreement to cooperate in carrying out parallel controls.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the control teams informed each other of the initial results achieved in the course of preparing the inspection, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on a course of action.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2-4 December 2009.
The review teams exchanged the findings collected so far and agreed on a timetable for compiling a joint report.
The two SAIs, in carrying out parallel control actions, decided to focus on: • a follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report; • an examination of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were not resolved during the previous parallel check; • an examination of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were classified as high risk; • a review of the tax administration's procedure in the area of international assistance for the recovery of VAT receivables; • tax controls of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during a workshop in June 2010.
4. Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of previous review recommendations
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
Based on the results of the previous audit action, the SAO recommended the modification of the conditions of VAT registration and the introduction of a new rule for the cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
The modified conditions should make it possible to reduce more effectively the risk of possible tax evasion in the collection of VAT.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not use the power to cancel VAT registration to taxpayers who did not comply with the obligations under Act No 235/2004 Coll. on Value Added Tax (‘the VAT Act’).
The amendment of the provision to introduce the obligation for tax administrations to cancel the VAT registration of payers upon repeated non-submission of a VAT return has not yet been proposed by the Czech Ministry of Finance.
Under the VAT Act, the tax authority may revoke the registration of the taxpayer ‘ex officio’ in cases where: (a) the taxpayer has not, without giving notice of the reason to the tax authority, carried out a transaction for 12 consecutive months; (b) the taxpayer has failed to fulfil his obligations under this Act; (c) the taxpayer ceases to be a taxable person.
In a previous audit action, it was found that the legislation in force allowed the Tax Office for Threshold 1 to cancel VAT registration on 31 January of the following calendar year to so-called non-established payers who had not incurred any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
Often, the FVO for Threshold 1 did not revoke these taxpayers' VAT registration, as the relevant provision provided an insufficient deadline for deregistration.
This problem was eliminated by amending the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax authorities shall be entitled to cancel the registration of the non-established taxpayer where the taxpayer has not supplied any goods or services subject to tax or exempt goods or services with a right to deduct VAT in the preceding calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU states introduce a one-month deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements.
The Council Directive reduces the reporting period for recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to file recapitulative statements in electronic form.
A summary report must also be made by the payer if the services for which the place of supply is determined in accordance with Paragraph 9(1) of the VAT Code are supplied to a person registered for tax in another Member State and the recipient is obliged to declare and pay the tax on those services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of the service.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative reports to achieve higher data reliability in VIES This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration conducts comparisons of intra-Community transaction data reported in VAT returns and summary reports of Czech payers automated in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
Combating VAT fraud is therefore an area of priority concern and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, inter alia, by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the eligible and the actual VAT collected in the 25 EU Member States (hereinafter referred to as the EU-25) during the period 2000-2006.
Based on an analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concludes that the estimated amount of loss of uncollected VAT for this period is between €90 and €113 billion, with an average of 12% of eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18%.
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action found that an effective risk management system could not be developed by just one Member State.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in every EU Member State.
Regarding the risk management system, the SAO carried out a check of EUROCANET, a system used to exchange information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-Community transactions by EU tax payers included in EUROCANET were selected for the check (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should help to improve the cooperation of the responsible authorities into a form that allows fraud to be detected in its infancy.
This network should later also become an important source of information in risk assessment for intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 October 200812, while setting out the basic principles that will guide the network.
The EUROFISC picture is the already functioning EUROCANET fast and selective information exchange system, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky business transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report produced the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
The German tax administration has set up a well-functioning system for registering taxpayers, based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance brought the scheme to the attention of the Commission in October 2007.
Improvements to the system are made on an ongoing basis.
Currently, the questionnaire data is electronically processed and will subsequently be used for the survey as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to safeguard the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
A law on the transposition of EU directives into national law was adopted on 8 April 2010.
That law includes provisions for the monthly submission of recapitulative statements on intra-Community deliveries.
Those provisions took effect on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in order to achieve greater data reliability in VIES and consider linking the two VAT return and recapitulative reporting systems
A joint working group was set up, made up of staff from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance.
The group has developed a strategy for automatically comparing data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the working group looked at a tool designed to optimise the control process for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a participant in this exchange under the so-called Risk Management Platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of the platform and, following a written consultation on 18 October 2006, the establishment of the Risk Management Platform was added to the Fiscalis Action Plan 2006-2007.
The members of the platform are further divided into sub-groups that address individual topics such as: • risk management tools; • influencing behaviour; • evaluation; • updating the risk management guide.
Reports on the performance of these subgroups were published in early 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and the withdrawal of such registration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including the VAT payer tax identification number database.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
For the time being, the issue of registration and de-registration has been left to the national legislation of EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political agreement on that draft Regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States must implement national procedures and only have the obligation to inform the Committee on Administrative Cooperation about these procedures.
Both SAIs deplore the Commission's failure to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs view this measure as an important preventive element in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts from the Commission in this direction.
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU states introduce a monthly reporting period, allowing for a more timely examination of intra-Community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the reporting period for recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it took effect on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced a monthly recapitulative reporting obligation according to a fixed calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in line with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater data reliability in VIES and consider linking the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
