The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is ongoing so far and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO carried out a check of EUROCANET, a system used to exchange information in the EU (see chapter 4.3).
BRH in this area concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected intra-Community transaction cases
The previous audit operation jointly examined the execution of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution or inconsistencies in the way in which the payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions on their VAT returns or recapitulative statements.
The two audit institutions selected for follow-up nine cases involving intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, whose control by the tax administrations of the two countries had not been completed during a previous joint control action.
1.
The Czech payer purchased goods worth €22,686 from a German payer in the 1st quarter of 2005.
This acquisition of goods was not declared by the Czech taxpayer in his VAT return because the German taxpayer did not have a VAT ID allocated to him during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax authorities received information that, under the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for the intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that, on the basis of a check carried out by the Czech tax authorities, the Czech taxpayer had filed a supplementary VAT return in which he declared the acquisition of the goods at that value and at the same time claimed the same amount of VAT deductible on that tax return.
2.
In the 4th quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase EUR 12 561 worth of goods from the German payer.
The acquisition of those goods was denied by the Czech taxpayer and did not appear on his VAT return.
The German tax administration refused to cooperate at the request of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax authorities did not obtain evidence, they terminated the inspection without finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax administration had received two spontaneous pieces of information from Germany under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer had invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and listed this acquisition on the correct VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
In the 4th quarter of 2004, a Czech payer was to purchase a €48,500 passenger car from a German payer.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not declared by the Czech taxpayer.
This payer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, so the tax authorities charged CZK 0 in VAT for that quarter.
On the basis of information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax authorities invited the payer to submit an additional VAT return, but this was not submitted by the payer.
A subsequent check revealed that the tax administrator had carried out other acts in the tax procedure in 2007 which showed that the passenger car in question had been sold by the Czech taxpayer to a car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax authorities issued a payment notice for the December 2004 tax year, by which they retrospectively assessed VAT on the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295 379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was cancelled with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of enforcement of the taxpayer's enforceable assets, the arrears appear to be irrecoverable.
4)
The Czech payer was to make deliveries of new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the 4th quarter of 2004 and 1st quarter of 2005 for a total value of EUR 198 167.
A response to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 revealed that there was an open tax-criminal case against the German entity in Germany.
In a follow-up, BRH obtained information that, after the tax proceedings in Germany had been completed, it was demonstrably established that the German taxpayer had been integrated into fraudulent activities.
Intracomanial acquisitions of goods were taxed at a value of €182,424 (2004) and €369,690 (2005).
The SAO subsequently found that the Czech payer had been involved in carousel business with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the examination of the supply of goods, a VAT check was initiated with the Czech tax entity for the tax years April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the inspection findings and information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information, the tax authorities additionally assessed VAT for the period May 2005 at CZK 703 031 and for the period June 2005 at CZK 726 551.
5.
Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth a total of EUR 58 000 from a German payer in February 2005.
This German payer was due to deliver EUR 88 027 worth of machinery to Czech payer B in Q3 2004, but payer B denied this acquisition.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that payer B had acquired the machine from a German company that had an organisational unit set up in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not report the acquisition of goods from a German payer on his VAT return.
A reply from the German tax authorities to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer had not made an intra-Community supply of the machine worth EUR 58 000, but had made a delivery of the goods within the Czech Republic.
BRH subsequently found that, following a tax audit, the intra-Community supply of the machine had been reclassified as a domestic supply of the machine and the VAT exemption had been abolished.
6)
The German taxpayer was due to deliver EUR 11,600 worth of goods to the Czech taxpayer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO's subsequent audit found that the Czech tax administration had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods at that value, was wrongly recorded.
BRH found that after receiving a response to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax authorities corrected the German taxpayer's VAT return and retrospectively assessed VAT worth EUR 1 600.
Further movement of goods in Germany and application of VAT in Germany are subject to tax control.
The German payer's summary report has not yet been corrected as only the payer who filed the recapitulative statement can make corrections to the recapitulative statements in Germany.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as to whether the Czech taxpayer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
The Czech tax authorities assessed the Czech taxpayer at CZK 0 after the tax procedure for the February 2005 tax year and told the German tax authorities that they could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer had been revoked in 2007 for non-compliance and the Czech tax administration sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
A subsequent check by BRH found that the German taxpayer had changed his residence and that the new locally competent tax authority had revoked the VAT exemption for the supply of the car in question to the Czech taxpayer on the basis of the inspection carried out.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the figures in the recapitulative statement and has lodged an appeal against the tax authority's decision.
8)
According to VIES data, the German taxpayer delivered goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the Czech taxpayer between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator was trying to determine the causes of the differences incurred by the Czech taxpayer in acquiring goods between Q3 2004 and Q1 2005.
The Czech taxpayer has repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech Tax Administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of purchased goods amounting to CZK 134 273 for the period from Q3 2004 to Q1 2005, since, according to the Czech Tax Administrator, it was not possible to accurately capture the business transactions for each quarter and therefore the Tax Administrator accepted the submitted additional tax returns.
9)
The German taxpayer delivered EUR 46 854 worth of goods to the Czech taxpayer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The Czech payer admitted intra-Community acquisitions of goods worth only EUR 14 856 over the same period.
The Czech tax authority verified the amount of supplies made in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total declared value of the supply of goods of EUR 31 998, a value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech taxpayer in the VAT return and the VIES data.
A subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that the Czech taxpayer had filed a supplementary VAT return for the July 2004 tax year only in January 2007, after many urges from the tax administration.
At the same time, in that tax return, the taxpayer exercised the right to deduct VAT, thus keeping the tax liability for that tax period unchanged.
A follow-up check verified that for selected cases of business transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most tax procedures were completed and that the tax authorities in both the Czech Republic and Germany took adequate measures (i.e. subsequently assessed VAT or prevented input tax refunds).
4.3 Checking selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
4.3.1 Czech Republic audit results
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for detecting risky entities within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from the EUROCANET system was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with data on the acquirers.
Starting from the 1st quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic sends data on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers to EUROCANET.
In the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system have been selected for inspection.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States was captured in EUROCANET.
As the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, no information could be obtained to help establish whether suppliers with German VAT IDs were assessed by the German tax administration as risk subjects.
The audit revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Where applicable, tax administrations have made use of the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• The tax authorities did not detect any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions when verifying the signal information.
The tax authorities keep track of such tax entities due to their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show any deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT in the accounting records submitted, even though they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed business relationships with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• The verification of commercial transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with the tax authorities and could not be contacted.
Locally competent tax authorities have mostly screened the risky tax entities and risk transactions identified in the signals from EUROCANET.
Tax authorities have limited options when examining risky transactions, particularly in the context of the screening of missing traders , and it is difficult to prove fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer from a physical check of documents alone.
Stricter VAT registration requirements and more flexible deregistration would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered to report fictitious intra-EU supplies of goods or to issue formally correct tax documents to payers who unduly draw deductions of input VAT on their basis.
In cases where there is a suspicion of involvement of tax entities in carousel transactions and other fraud, and where goods are imported and exported from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help in identifying goods and irregularities in shipping documentation, as well as in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament in late 2008 as a weakness of EUROFISC, which should be remedied by setting up a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Control results in Germany
BRH analysed the information available from the Federal Central Financial Office, which contained data from EUROCANET.
Those figures were the criterion for selecting six files of German taxpayers for inspection.
Like some other countries, Germany has refused to actively participate in EUROCANET.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but only receives data from EUROCANET.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement:.in the Government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public administrative) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis for breaching the applicable rules on the concealment of tax information.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such data are used by other Member States within EUROCANET. ‘17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has been carrying out analyses of EUROCANET data and forwarding them to the tax authorities of the Länder in accordance with an agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive control information on the direct business relations of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been enrolled in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities receive no information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relationship with traders from other Member States who also have business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to actively participate.
As a result, the control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
Both countries' tax administrations have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is essential to establish a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The EU Council has reached a political consensus on a proposal for a regulation whose main contribution lies in the establishment of EUROFISC.
Experience gained from using EUROCANET data should also become part of the envisaged network to fight VAT fraud.
Member States should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought before courts at national and European level show that a discussion between Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions appears to be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for recovery of claims
4.4.1 International recovery assistance in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives provide the basic framework for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance for the recovery of certain financial claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal order while amending the aforementioned Act No 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No 191/2004 Coll. on international assistance for the recovery of certain financial claims was adopted.
The new regulation in the system for adjusting international cooperation for the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28.11.2008.
The annex to the regulation sets out new templates for applications to be used from 1.1.2009, the new obligation for electronic communication and the obligation for the requesting authority to certify the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guiding principles for providing international recovery cooperation:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always given only on request containing the prescribed elements;
3. assistance does not cover financial claims which have the nature of a criminal sanction in the requested State;
4. the provision of international recovery assistance shall be governed by the domestic law of the requesting State;
5. foreign claims do not have priority in enforcement;
6. assistance shall be provided only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has used, without success, all the available options to recover a claim under its legal system).
Act No 191/2004 Coll. defines three forms of assistance, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
The locally competent tax office shall electronically send a request for information, a request for delivery or a request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance through the finance directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will provide a translation of the request into the relevant language, scan it, including its attachments, and send it to the competent authority of the tax administration of the designated State via the CCN/CSI network.
There are two basic requirements for enforcement: the claim must be for more than €1,500 and must not be more than 5 years old.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Upon receipt of a request from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the request as soon as possible and no later than seven days.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the refusal and indicate the specific provisions of the Directive it invokes.
Such communication shall be sent no later than three months after the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance verifies that the application has all the elements required by law and should transmit the application without delay through the Finance Directorate to the local tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax authorities inter alia survey the debtor's assets, e.g. by obtaining land registry statements, checking bank accounts, verifying vehicle registration at the DMV, etc.
Six months after the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the requesting authority of the outcome of the investigation carried out to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities, where recovery is not possible, the applicant authority should also be informed.
Any sums recovered by the tax authorities shall be transferred to the requesting authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not inconceivable that the Czech tax authorities collecting foreign claims will allow it to be waived or paid in instalments if the State requesting the recovery agrees to do so.
During the recovery period, the debtor is prescribed interest or penalty payments under Act No 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty is due to the State that requested the recovery.
In the case of accepted recovery requests, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit the application to the locally competent tax authorities on time, in particular in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the framework of international recovery assistance as well as in the case of applications received from tax administrations from the Czech Republic.
The audit action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not comply with Act No 191/2004 Coll. because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months of the date when the receipt of the application was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistics
The Czech Ministry of Finance, in accordance with the provisions of Section 13(4) of Act No 191/2004 Coll., shall compile statistics for the European Commission by 15 March each year, indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or recovery sent or received in the past year, indicating the amount of claims to which the requests relate.
The European Commission draws up a report on the state of recovery on the basis of supporting documents provided by all EU Member States, which it submits to the EU Council and the European Parliament.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data due to an error in the recovered receivables item in 2008 by EUR 5,250,000 by stating the incorrect value of the recovered VAT receivable (this was a shift in the decimal point after converting the receivable from Czech crowns to a value in euros).
This error was subsequently reflected in European Commission statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including recoveries, is given in the table below.
4.4.2 International recovery assistance in Germany
The legal authority for international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from European Community law, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Recovery Directive) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In the interests of more accessible wording and better clarity, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76/308/EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply inter alia to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the EC Act of 3 May 2003 on the collection of state taxes.
The enforcement procedure in Germany is governed by the German fiscal code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities can provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities in force in national jurisdiction and on the basis of the EC Administrative Assistance Act.
Part Six of Germany's fiscal code (Articles 249-346) enshrines legal provisions governing the enforcement process.
In particular, the administrative operations of the tax authorities are governed by the instructions for execution and the instructions for enforcement.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with representatives of the Länder supreme tax authorities regarding the principles of administrative assistance in the assessment of taxes and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general conditions for lodging requests for recovery are as follows:
• The legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of recovery have been exhausted.
• Claims which are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be definitive.
• No more than 5 years may elapse between the issue of an enforcement order or the date on which the claim comes into effect (i.e. is no longer subject to an appeal) and the date on which the applications are submitted.
• The total amount receivable must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for the recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the tax authorities' implementing departments to the relevant foreign office, such as the Czech CLO, via the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
Further follow the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 January 2004.25 A working group of the Federal Government and the Land Governments is currently reviewing this methodological guideline in order to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
Applications, including attachments, shall be submitted electronically by the Financial Conduct Authority to the Intermediate Authority.
This office checks the accuracy of the application in content and form.
If the request is not correct, it shall be returned to the relevant tax office.
If it meets all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office will then ensure the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and will also provide a translation of the request.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and an acknowledgement of receipt shall be sent within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check whether the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these requests to the intermediary office, which then forwards them to the competent tax authorities and monitors their processing.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the request takes more than 6 months to process, the intermediate authority shall invite the submission of an interim report to be submitted in accordance with Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94/DG.
Once the formal and factual elements of the request have been checked, the implementing departments shall notify the enforcement method.
Any sums recovered must be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of their receipt.
Statistics
Information on mutual assistance for recovery between Germany and the Czech Republic in 2006-2008 (as at 31.12.2008) can be found in the table below.
4.4.3 Recovery control, case studies
Under international cooperation, 21 requests for international recovery assistance between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for scrutiny.
Examination of 10 selected cases found, inter alia:
1.
On 20.10.2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance from Germany received a request for recovery of a VAT claim for the years 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3 883, or CZK 109 820, from a Czech taxpayer.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax authority until 26.2.2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administration established a mortgage on properties owned by a Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire recovered debt by mortgaging the properties, a payment schedule was agreed with the Czech tax entity, with repayments of at least CZK 2 000 per month.
On 31.8.2009, information was sent to the German tax administration on the state of recovery, noting that as of 25.8.2009 this claim had been partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49 600.
This sum was sent to Germany and then another instalment of CZK 3 000 was sent to Germany on 28.8.2009.
2.
On 7.1.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery of tax arrears from a Czech taxpayer who owed EUR 180 869, or CZK 4 434 915, in Germany for VAT and for income tax and related taxes.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the tax authority only on 27.11.2008.
The tax administrator, by examining the ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movables, found that the debtor did not own any enforceable assets.
Furthermore, the local investigation established that the debtor did not stay at the address of permanent residence for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6.4.2009 and on 16.4.2009 the reply from the tax administration was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany on 21.11.2007 for recovery concerning tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3 139, or CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for the recovery of this claim to the tax authorities on 6.8.2008, although on 18.2.2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance had received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9.12.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax authorities that the recovery request was being processed by the payment of a claim by a Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also recovered in the context of recovery in the Czech Republic and entered in Germany on 27.10.2008.
Due to the long time limits within which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the competent tax authorities, the claim was paid twice in this case - by the entity itself in Germany and by the Czech tax authorities recovering the claim.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been set off against a claim from a further recovery request of EUR 6 649 to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance records only a claim for recovery of EUR 3 139 with this company, a claim for recovery of EUR 6 649 does not appear in the Czech Ministry of Finance file with the company in question.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany to recover the tax arrears of a Czech taxpayer who owed EUR 39 957 in income tax and VAT and accessories in Germany, or CZK 956 654.
On 19.12.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax authorities.
A recovery procedure was initiated on 1.6.2009, ordering the seizure of a claim on accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and of a salary deduction (the deduction amounted to CZK 7 000).
In his dealings with the tax authority, the debtor stated that he disagreed with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax administrator found that the taxpayer was willing to repay EUR 250 per month in the past, which was not accepted by the German tax administrator.
The tax entity has promised to discuss the application with the German tax administration with a view to obtaining a change in the amount of its claim.
The recovery of the debt was still ongoing during the audit operation.
5.
On 19.11.2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a recovery request from Germany concerning a Czech taxpayer who owed CZK 3 116 304 in income tax for 2005 and turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories.
It was not until 14.11.2008 that the Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the Tax Office for Prague 1, which is responsible for administering the tax to non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, as it was not possible to determine the locally competent tax authority on the basis of the address given by the tax entity.
During the FÚ investigation, it was informed that the debtor had an income of EUR 4 704 on 19.9.2008; however, the FÚ could no longer issue an enforcement order for that amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance did not transmit the request for recovery until after that date.
On 26.1.2009, the Czech tax administrator initiated enforcement of the claim and issued an execution order for the attachment of the claim to the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit unions.
The recovery of the debt was still ongoing during the audit operation.
6.
The Czech tax authority requested international cooperation in recovering the VAT claim and costs totalling CZK 146 223 742 on 3.10.2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax administration until 13.5.2008.
On 8 September 2008, the German tax authorities transferred to the Czech authorities, through the Federal Bank, the sum received from the execution of funds in the debtor's account, amounting to EUR 17 700, or CZK 439 226.
An error in the recalculation of the amount recovered was found when verifying the volume of claims recovered.
The recovered amount of CZK 146 223 742 was converted at EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct conversion of the amount recovered is EUR 5 833 781,83.
A request was therefore sent to Germany to recover the sum, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover a tax arrears with a Czech taxpayer who owed CZK 1 970 632 in VAT and accessories, or EUR 79 847.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send an application to the German tax administration until 10.11.2008.
On 4.2.2009, the German tax authorities called on the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant decreases in the company's turnover in the 2nd half of 2008 and in particular in the 1st half of 2009 and the related liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to cover the arrears: EUR 4 600 on 8.4.2009, EUR 3 000 on 6.5.2009 and EUR 2 500 on 16.6.2009.
These payments were sent to a tax administration account in the Czech Republic.
On 23.6.2009, the German tax authorities agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500 by 30.6.2009.
8.
A claim for recovery totalling EUR 398 653, or CZK 9 832 779, including a claim for real estate transfer tax, was received from the Czech tax authorities to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 May 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2.10.2008.
On 3.4.2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a communication from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax administration justified the refund on the ground that the tax on the transfer of immovable property was not a tax within the meaning of Article 2(e), (f), (g) or (h) of Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
The German tax administration further stated that Article 2(g) concerns claims in relation to income tax and wealth tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55/EC applies to taxes on income and on capital listed in Article 1(3) in conjunction with Article 1(4) of Council Directive 77/799/EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed to draw up and submit a new request for recovery, excluding arrears of real estate transfer tax of CZK 61 759 and including arrears of VAT, corporation tax and personal income tax, which will be re-sent to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has received a new request from the Czech tax administration for the recovery of tax arrears concerning the same taxpayer who owes CZK 7 079 735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6.2.2006, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears by a Czech taxpayer who owed CZK 3 445 782, or EUR 123 328, in personal income tax and VAT.
Of that amount, VAT was CZK 1 133 967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the German tax administration until 18.04.2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax administration the reply from the German tax administration dated 9.7.2007 until 11.11.2008.
The reply stated that the German tax authorities had issued an enforcement order against the bank account with the bank on 11.6.2007, but it said that it had no business relations with the tax entity.
By doing so, the German tax authorities considered the application to be settled.
10.
On 26.9.2005, the Czech tax authorities sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1 296 845, or EUR 43 591.
The application from the Czech tax administration was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10.10.2005.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the German tax administration on 15.12.2005.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax administrator executed the execution on the debtor's funds in bank accounts and the payroll deduction and set up a lien on the immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authorities on 16.3.2005.
The reply to a request for information received by the Czech tax authorities on 16.9.2005 showed that the Czech taxpayer was resident in Germany and had income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20.4.2006, but forwarded it to the Czech tax authorities only on 12.2.2008.
The reply stated that no recovery proceedings could be initiated in Germany because of the debtor's insolvency - no assets had been identified for him and his income from non-business activities was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
In doing so, the German tax administration considered the request for recovery to be completed.
4.4.4 Comparison and Evaluation
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which applications for international recovery assistance are handled is identical in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay close attention to the management of their statistics.
In a 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of discrepancies in the statistics had decreased, even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important that statistical issues are renegotiated at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics are to show the annual number of claims as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amount of claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by Member States as this may assist Member States in assessing their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that recovery rates per Member State can be calculated is considered useful by both SAIs for Member States with lower recovery rates to intensify their efforts and seek to improve recovery rates at least to the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in the process.
Especially in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery on time to the locally competent tax authorities.
A similar situation was found for requests for international assistance received from tax administrations from the Czech Republic.
The audit action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance had failed to comply with Act No 191/2004 Coll. on International Assistance for Recovery of Claims because it had not informed the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months of the date on which the application was confirmed to have been received.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of VDS is based on Act No 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were set up or set up for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax period indicated in the income tax return for natural/legal persons amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The classification of the taxpayer as a VDS took place after the submission of the income tax return for the relevant tax year, for the first time for 2003.
A taxable person ceased to be known as VDS when, in three consecutive tax years from the end of the tax return under which he was included in the VDS, his net turnover for the tax year fell below that threshold.
A taxpayer could not be excluded from the VDS register without carrying out a tax check of at least one tax per tax year.
All VDS were checked at a minimum frequency of five years by the end of 2009.
From 2010 onwards, a written assessment of the taxpayer must be carried out at least every two years and the follow-up chosen must eliminate tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The FCA control is focused on at least one type of tax; tax authorities generally elect several tax years at the same time.
VDS were audited by the specialist inspection departments, which are set up in total for 13 FCs, or by the control departments of locally competent FCs.
The Specialised Inspections Unit carries out tax inspections within the remit set by the Director of the Finance Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• Tax entities operating in unusual and specific business sectors;
• Entities for which it is technically and time-consuming to carry out a tax audit;
• Entities with a sprawling territorial and organisational structure;
• Entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• Entities linked in chains and networks suspected of large-scale tax evasion and unjustified luring of excess deductions.
The number of tax inspections carried out by the specialised inspection units of the FCA and the results of those inspections are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed an amendment to Act No 531/1990 Coll. on Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists of the establishment of a specialised FÚ with nationwide coverage for selected tax entities (inter alia for corporate entities created for business purposes, which have achieved a turnover of more than CZK 2 billion).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls on large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • German Fiscal Code (AO), • Fiscal Governance Act (FVG), • Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on control are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax inspection on the spot. In particular, these articles lay down the rules governing the admissibility of on-the-spot tax checks (i.e. at the premises of the business), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules governing the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the inspection notice, the principles of control, the duty of the taxpayer to cooperate and the conditions for carrying out the final discussion and the communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax inspections are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Governance Act Pursuant to Section 5.1, point 1, in conjunction with Section 19 of the Act, participation in on-the-spot tax inspections carried out by the tax authorities is compulsory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The authorities involved will agree with each other on the spot the nature and extent of the Federal Central Tax Office's involvement in tax inspections.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the particular undertakings it selects be subject to an inspection at a time to be determined by it.
In such a case, it may declare rules on the conduct and content of the inspection at the premises of such companies.
Rules on tax controls According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the regulations on tax inspections (German acronym BpO 2000) were agreed by the Bundesrat, the upper house of the German Parliament in which the governments of the Länder are represented.
These administrative provisions apply to on-the-spot checks by the tax authorities of the Länder as well as by the Federal Central Tax Office.
Undertakings are classified by size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to ex post control (Article 4.2 BpO).
Under Article 33.1 of the BpO 2000, any informed tax authority must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the additional methodology for tax administration provides the following guidance:
• A uniform manual for special VAT controls in Germany ;
• a USLO manual setting out the methodology for using intra-Community trade relations data conducted in VIES;
• the ZAUBER manual, which sets out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits according to the type of business.
The data are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are assessed every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to inspect - not just large enterprises - must be determined at regular intervals.
As a general rule, inspections of large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually announced including VAT checks.
This means that, in the course of the inspection, checks will be carried out definitively, in particular on income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks can be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisation of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by the checks is usually between three and five years.
BpO 2000 foresees a three-year control period.
All taxes on a given company are subject to verification.
4.5.3 Control management of large tax entities
Both SAIs chose not to examine individual cases of VDS checks carried out, but focused on management issues to get an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT controls at VDS.
By means of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax authorities on areas they consider essential to the management of the issue.
• What statistical records and analyses, related to the VAT inspection of VDS, are available to the management of tax administrations?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or measurement records that distinguish between the fight against VAT fraud and, in general, VAT control?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow for such a distinction at the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between a check designed to combat VAT fraud and a general VAT check.
• Are there any statistics or a record of the timeliness of VAT checks (linked to the time period of transactions checked)?
Czech Republic: Records of timeliness of questioning relevant for intra-Community acquisition of goods on behalf of selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information registered in the ADIS system also includes data on how long the questioning took.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors contain only information on the average time of the last check (year information).
This figure does not provide an overview of selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, the statistics produced at Federal level for the special VAT control units do not provide information regarding the classification of tax entities.
• There are some statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenues generated, disaggregated for example according to the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the taxpayer has improperly applied a reduced rate of VAT instead of the standard rate of tax);
ii. only a nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. moving a fully qualified VAT case to another tax year);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the amounts of tax levied retrospectively broken down by type of tax, by the number of taxable entities audited and by the number of tax years audited.
Other tax practices (local inquiry, complaint procedure) are followed in the same way.
Timetables and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded as a separate task.
General debt statistics broken down by type of tax, but not by declared tax or tax identified by the tax authorities, are also kept.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not distinguish between the criteria listed.
In addition, most of the tax administrations visited do not distinguish between these differences.
• Are the control areas from which high additional revenues are generated recorded?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administration has the right to select the taxpayer for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of ADIS.
Germany: There are no federal regulations.
It follows that uniform stats at Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
Nevertheless, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must record their increased tax (VAT) liability if they exceed a certain amount.
In that case, they must specify, for example, the nature of the tax increase imposed.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDS claims an unjustified right to deduct input tax on supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity under Section 72(1) of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation under Section 75(3) of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73 (1) of the VAT Act;
- The VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Article 21(1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It has been established that there are no regulations at Federal level.
It follows that uniform stats at Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
VAT findings are not recorded separately by the Länder if they result from VDS tax controls.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must enter their assessed increased tax (VAT) liability if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Revenue Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration carry out analyses of areas of control from which there is a high "yield" and draw conclusions for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching nationwide audits focused on risky commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no federal regulations.
Uniform Federal-level statisticians for Tax Controllers and Special VAT Inspection Units do not provide data on audit areas from which high "revenue" is generated.
There are differing views on the analysis process as well as on case management in terms of relevance.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but its use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and Evaluation
Differences in the responses of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a wealth of data from the tax checks carried out, as well as data from the financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same is true of the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to set up a dedicated financial office for the management of VDS in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows that those tasks are more difficult to perform in a similar manner.
Germany's philosophy, however, places greater emphasis on selecting individual cases based on data from submitted tax returns.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce shortfalls in VAT revenue.
As a result, it will increase the revenue from VAT collection and improve the level of risk detection among unreliable entrepreneurs.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of the two SAIs on parallel controls of the VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
The two SAIs got to know each other better about the systems in place in the following areas: • intra-Community transactions; • VAT risk management, in particular regarding the selection of risk-prone transactions; • Assistance to recover VAT claims; and • VAT control of large tax entities.
Cooperation between them has revealed differences in the strategies for detecting VAT fraud cases as well as differences in the above areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The control findings were compared and good practices were identified based on them.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will give a boost to stakeholders to start a discussion on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation between the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6. Communiqué
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Release deadline: June 2010.
